O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Here is the translation:
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to me in vision that I will complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is forgotten in our region and is unknown throughout all, so the science is perished and decayed, and nothing remains except for the small descriptions in books of the ancients that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come the error and vanity, and intentions are closed, and the science is estranged.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	It seems to me that I shall bring it to life together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation.
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and I shall bring together the forms of cautery instruments and other tools of work with the adjustment of declaration and preparation for them, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because for this reason no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is estranged.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for the one who undertakes this to ascend in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the proportions of members, and their forms and connections and separations, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and veins and the number of joints, and their movement and rest, and the location of their origin.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And therefore Hippocrates says that a name without a name is much, but with work it is little.
et meismement en l’art de main.	and similarly in the art of surgery.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We tell you at the beginning of this book that if someone is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned above, he must beware lest he err and kill people.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	as I have often seen many of those who involve themselves in this science, and abandon their knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I saw a foolish surgeon who cut away the abscess of scrofula from a woman's neck and also severed the arteries of the neck.
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	Why so much blood issued out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And there was another surgeon who treated a stone from an old man's body, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	and he carried away with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and saw the patient's condition and the great size of the stone, and knew well that if it was not removed he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And there was another surgeon who treated a duke of our land who had his leg broken, and with the breaking he got a wound;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the surgeon, full of ignorance, tied the break above the wound with rough string, and left no dressing on the wound, and let it end thus.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and he commanded that it not be untied at all;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and it remained thus until the leg became completely inflamed and the toes came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I was called to come to him, and I hastened to come to untie the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I dislocate it so it becomes quiet and feels no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But all the corruption was already confirmed in the member, and could not be healed;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member until the member was completely lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another surgeon who opened up an abscess that had become inflamed and then spread through the evil of his authority.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a chancre, when it is purged of melancholic humor, should not be touched with iron unless one can remove all that which is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And therefore, dear son, it is necessary that you know that the work of hands is divided into two parts:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that is to say, work in which there is danger in many conditions;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show you each place in this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Therefore it is necessary that you guard yourself so that the foolish speaker cannot speak evil of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	Take your arms in custody, and approach your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best way that through God's grace you may come to salvation and be praised.
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and let dreadful diseases of grievous sickness;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	and put aside your arms that cause you to doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galien says in some of his admonitions:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Take no heed of a bad disease unless you are summoned to be a foolish doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapters are about fire cauteries and medical emetics, and the chapters are arranged from head to feet.
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and the forms of instruments, and the fixings of cautery, and everything that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapters are about cutting and piercing, and poultices and wounds, and extracting arrows, and similar things;
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and the chapters are arranged and the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is of restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and is ordained for the chief joints up to the feet, and the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Therefore that we remember the work, it is necessary that I say the quality of the aid and the harm of each temperament.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the quality of aid, and of harm, is the longest and most subtle speech, and the secret answers.
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and about these things many wise men spoke, and agreed with them;
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	and I will add no more words to theirs, for I fear the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that fire cauterization helps universally all humors or bodies, except two humors:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	that is to say, hot humor without matter, and dry humor without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In hot and dry humors with matter, they all agreed and said that cauterization is great help;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and the others say the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that a cauterization is not good for a disease that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be cured by heat or dryness;
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and that one who says the opposite says that cauterization makes great help for hot and dry disease that comes into the bodies of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you understand the body of man and its moisture according to the temperament of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this saying.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be true on many occasions through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in any case, do not meddle with fires except by him who has tried it and knows through long use the book of cauterizations, and the diversity of human complexions, and their dispositions and causes of diseases, and the surprises and the pace of time.
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	of other complexions we have no fear, especially in cold and wet diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the doctors assembled and agreed on cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that cauterization with fire is part of the secrets of cures, and of greater virtue than cauterization by burning medicines.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not go beyond the member that is burned, and does not harm another member unless it is named.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	The burning medicines come from member to member by approaching, and bring to the member grievous disease of great corruption;
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and by chance the patient dies.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fire due to its highness and the goodness of its substance does not burn if there is no excessiveness.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And I have found this by experiment and the length of my service and study that I have put into the art, and it is based on the truth of things.
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	and therefore I excuse myself for the length of my speech, because it does not please me to take away from you the secret which is replied with fire, and the quality of the work, how it repels diseases from bodies, as philosophers say in demonstrating.
or le recevez en vos pensees.	or receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on when the cauterizations should be done and chose precedents.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cauterization is suitable at all times, because the harm that happens is put away by the aid of cauterization;
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and likewise if the cauterization is for necessary and pressing pains that cannot wait until a greater harm comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And never think about this, dear son, as foolish people do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for the disease that is cured by cauterization has no return;
et il le dient ensi;	and they say so;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it's not as they think, because cauterization is not a medicine that changes the complexion, and dries out the humors that are the cause of the pain, and its value lies more in its promptness than in its medicine, due to its virtue and the power of its operation.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And it is possible that the disease comes sometimes according to the complexion of the patient, and the location of the disease, and its virtue;
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and the excesses are gathered in him by the consumption of meats and similar things, unless it is cauterization administered at a place where there is little excess and moisture, as with cauterization for denseness due to pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return;
mais ce avient poc.	But it happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the latest in medicine, and that is true;
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cauteries are worth after medicine, but their intentions are false, and it is said that cauteries are the latest in medicine because when we administer methods of treatment for any disease and they do not work, then we administer the cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore it is clear that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish doctors.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancients said that gold cauteries are more effective than iron ones, and they did not say this except for the quality of the gold and the height of its substance;
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they said that the heat of a cautery does not cause corruption, but this is not true for I have tested it, and found that it is true in some men;
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	and gold cauteries are worth more than iron ones, as they also said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And even when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it becomes cooled down soon.
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if you heat it too much;
si font au feu;	so they become red-hot;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and thus it has enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And therefore we use fire cauterization because we have found it to be suitable for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	And I have ordered this chapter from the beginning to the end, so that the view may be more light for you to find.
dou cautere olivaire	of the olive cauterization
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cauterization is worth against moisture and cold on the head, and there are two ways in which it is done due to the cause of a disease called "soda", and due to many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, and to the ears, and because of excessive dreams and pain in the teeth and throat, and similarly for all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged by medicinal solution, moderating the head's third humor or fourth, according to what the virtues, age, and habituation of the patient can bear.
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then make the patient's head return.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then make him sit cross-legged in your hands, and put his hands on his lap;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	after place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and let it come to your middle finger, so that it bleeds forth then reheat the cautery which is called "olivare", of which this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And place it on the level marked with ink, and move your hand slowly and carefully, little by little, twisting.
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	then lift your hand slightly, and return to the level if you see the bone just a little bit;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	and if you do not see it, then start the cautery again until you see the bone as I have told you;
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	after that take a piece of silk, and put in an absorbent and soft cotton inside, and place it on the level, and let it be for three days;
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	then apply moistened cloth wrapped in butter;
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and leave it on until the scab is removed;
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the wound of the tetra-pharmaceutical, as long as it remains healthy.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And they say that when an open wound stays longer, the more it purges;
et por ce si aide mues.	and so if aided.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some of them said that one should cauterize as much so that part of the bone is burned, and then remove what has been burned from the bone, and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And others say that one should cauterize it as slowly above, and press as hard so that the bone is made as wide as a green thread that women put in their purses so that the humors may be moved out.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one should leave the wound open for a long time.
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	after that, one should clean and dress it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two manners of cauterizing do not seem to be good in all respects, except in certain men where there is a way of fear.
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and it seems to me that I should leave it.
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	for the head is weakened by the continuous flow of natural fluids, as we witness in other members;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and also when the patient's head is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterizing is more safe and gentle for me, and I work with that in such a way that salvation ensues.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	from ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When in all the head comes chronic pain and endures long, then the patient should use yellow and pills that are called "cochie", and for purging of the head, oils, and plasters.
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if one does the fire cautery that we have mentioned before, and it is ineffective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take care if the head of the patient is hot in nature, and it is not too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	then cauterize below that one that we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	After, make a fire cautery on each horn of the head up to the bone, just as we have said before, and make one at the place that is called "vasselz".
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and it is the place where one puts poultices;
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and hold your hand so that you do not see all the way to the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	The patient feels too much greater pain in this fire cautery than in others, and I will speak of it elsewhere.
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and it is necessary that the corner cauteries be more subtle than those used to cauterize the middle of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	of the head cautery
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When sudden pain comes to one part of the head, and the disease spreads as far as the eye, and the head is purged by medicinal remedies, and all other cures that I have said in the division of diseases are tried, and none of it helps.
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	then he does the cautery by two manners, namely from medicinal agents and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The cautery of medicinal agents is that you take a piece of aloes, remove the rind and pound it into two pieces for the shoulders, and then make an incision in the temple where the pain holds in such a way that you can place the piece of aloes under the skin.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it is set back, if he binds it well and tightens it so and leaves it thus for twelve hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	and then loosen it and treat with butter of garlic, and leave the wound thus for two or three days;
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	then put on a poultice of butter as long as impetigo appears.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the treatment with oil until he is healed;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you see that these remedies which I have written or discussed concerning concomitant treatments are of no use.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done according to this method.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery until it takes its shape.
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "clos" because the head is shaped like a clove or if it has one little hollow, and in the middle there is a small appearance;
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and he puts it on the painful spot, and holds his hand and turns the fire a little bit, until half of the fat that needs to be burned is burnt.
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and lift your hand so the artery does not burn, which is outside, and abundance of blood flows.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	Then put cotton on the wound, and place it on the site for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then put moistened cotton in butter, and then treat the wound with oil until it is healed;
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cauterizer called "cultellare", at every point, and take care not to touch the artery in this migraine that is not old.
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat migraine as we have said before in the divisions of diseases, and it does not help, and you see that the cauterizers previously mentioned from medicine and fire do not work, then it is necessary to heat the cauterizer called "cultellare" until it is white;
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	and mark a line on the weeping place of about half a digit in length, and take your hand away once, and strain that you do not cover the artery and do not bring it just to the bone;
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	and beware of the jaw that will fall when eating, and the nerves have regard only to the falling and spasms do not come upon the patient, and beware of the disarrangement of blood from the artery when it is cut, or cutting has great fear and also for him who does not understand, and is not skilled in this and experienced;
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and let the work remain in my way;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to stop blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it applies in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that this cautery does not suffice for the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize it on the head just as we have said, and heal the wound until it is sound.
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	and if you see, administer the fire cauterization that we have said in the chapter on artery extraction, with the cauterizer that has two knives;
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	and this fire cauterization is better than that one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of ear pain from coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When ear pain comes from coldness and one has tried medicines that dissolve and other cures that we have said in the division, and the pains do not subside, then heat this cautery which is called "poins", according to the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	After piercing all around the sick ear, or around both sides where the pain holds in both, and remove one pace above the root of the ear once you have marked the place to burn.
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	and make 10 points around each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	after curing the wound until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of mouth torture
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	The torture that must be cured by cauterization is not other than those that move from phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of disease;
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not make any cauterization on likenesses that come from dryness and spasms of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you treat this likeness of torture which moves from bloodletting and purging the head and gargling, and it does not help, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient with three fire cauterizations.
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	One in the root of the ear, and another a little behind the temple, and the third at the joining of the two lips.
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	And put the cauter in the part that appears sound, and make it cauterize near the top of the ear above a little below the horn of the head, and another on the temple as long as a thumb.
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and leave the cauter so that the middle part of the ear is burned.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cauter:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it is like the appearance of a scalpel that we have shown before, but it is a little more subtle and it is necessary that the knives are a little thicker.
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment, as I have said before, until he is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When apoplexy is ancient and you treat it as we have said, and it does not benefit, and the patient has no fever, then make 4 cauterizations.
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	Two on the two horns of the head, and one in the head, and one on the "vessel" as we have said before, and the last cauterization on the mouth of the stomach.
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and be treated as we have said before.
de litargie	From lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	To this disease, give the patient great years and pills made from mandrake to the brain;
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	After having raised the patient's head completely, and place the mustard plaster written in the treatise on emplasters on the occiput.
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	and this is the manner of cauterization:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	If he does so as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If he is healed thus, it is good;
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	and if he is not healed, then make three fire cauterizations inside the head from top to bottom until the neck, and leave a space of two fingers between each one.
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	and treat it as the others, and if you see swelling coming on, and the patient is suffering, then make one fire cauterization in the middle.
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if necessary, two others above the two horns, and treat it until he is healed.
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and let the cauterization be that which is called "olivary", as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	from chill of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is necessary that the head be cleansed of years and all that we have previously said;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	after which remove the head of the patient, then make a cauterization inside the head and on each horn, and one last and three on the spine of the neck.
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the disease is severe, make four fire cauterizations on the spine of the back;
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	and leave it so that the most excessive burning has passed, and lift your hand;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	after the treatment until he is healed, and the cauterization which is called "olivary" that we have mentioned before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use cauterization unless they are phlegmatic, and it is necessary first to purge the brain with years and other cures that we have said in the division when the patient is large and suffering from poor medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is a child who cannot bear to suffer, make gargling and gentle mastication frequent the brain often with good meat;
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	after the king's head is put in a medium, and one cauterization according to what we have said before, and one cauterization on the vessel, and on each horn;
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and if the patient is severe and suffering, make cauterizations as I have said to one who has paralysis and softening of body, on the spine of the back and of the neck, and be the olivary cauterization according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is an infant, make one subtle cauterization in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When by the cause of melancholy the superfluities or moistures are corrupted and thick phlegm is formed, then make those cauterizations as we have said for someone who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if by the cause of melancholy the superfluities are declining into melancholy, and the patient's body is moist, then give him something to drink that will purge the brain, according to what is said before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After instructing the sick person;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	After making a bandage of well-made linen, just like a circle, and putting it on the head;
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	and the patient should be crossed, and kept well from all parts;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	After applying the poultice, and smear with old goat butter;
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	and let it be heated over tempered fire, so that the patient can bear it being applied to the wound.
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	After removing the circle from inside the head and letting it cool down;
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and do this to the patient once a week with good management, until he is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you see that it is being cauterized by making several points all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This way of cauterizing moistens the brain adequately;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then put on a damp cloth soaked in butter and goose fat.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes' evil
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When evil comes first to the eyes by the signs that I said in the division, then begin and give the patient something to drink that purifies the head, and watch out for all moisture, and make him sweat or take a bath several times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	After instructing him to sit behind his head, and having him cauterized on the head, and having two cauterizations on the two temples if the descending of the evil is together in both eyes, or in one if it is in one;
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	and stop all cauterization of all veins and arteries that are beneath the hair, and let the cauterization be long according to the width of the temple;
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	and beware of shedding blood, and if you see too much blood issuing, then stop it to the extent that you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in the cautionary incision how to stop it;
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	and never do a cauterization or hatterail below the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	of the tears of the heart
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are above the veins or below the arteries that appear on the surface of the head outside.
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and one sees that it is cold, clammy superfluities, then make the cauterization that I said at the beginning of this cure, descending to the eyes:
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	I cautery on the head, and two cauterizations on the two temples, and two cauterizations beneath the lower jawbone.
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	and if there is need for more, then he should cauterize the bleeding above the skull at each little cauterization.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the tears of the heart within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you apply medicine according to what we have said in the division, and it does not benefit, then give the patient three draughts of mulberry juice.
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	after the king's head, and make a cauterization in the oil pit of the cauterizer.
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	and make two cauterizations on the "clavilis" above the temples, one a little below the hair.
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and take care not to cut the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cauterization called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the parchment of oil is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize it with this caustic called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	Until it takes its shape.
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see that you should make two cauterizations on the two temples as long as the temples are.
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and don't let go of the hand until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the way I said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of the hair that points the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	Sometimes it happens that the hair of the eyelids is converted into a partition, and pricks the eye, and one makes cauterizations in two ways.
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	it means by fire or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let his hairs grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they have grown and are even, then put the patient in your sight;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	after which mark on the paper of the eyes a figure that is like the leaf of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be below the hairs;
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Then I place moistened cotton in egg white and persimmon juice on the eye, then heat the fire cautery to its usual form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	After cauterizing on the figure you have marked out little by little many times, so that the colors be burned away from there.
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	and the signs of the health of the operation are that you see the parchment retracted and the hairs raised to the point of the eye.
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	Then lift your hand, and let it be like this for three days, then place moistened cotton in butter until the scab is removed.
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the treatment of ointment as long as they are healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And if after this the hairs come and the parchment is softened then recommence the cautery on that same place, just as you did at first.
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if the hairs are gone, so cauterize it as long as the paper is lifted to its natural place and is even, and do not prick the hairs with oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The burning cauterization of medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow as long and even as possible, then make a parchment in the shape of myrtle's leaf.
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	Then take French soap and live coal, each one a., and grind them together well.
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	and make it quickly, so that it doesn't cool down, then spread it on the shape you have made like a myrtle leaf, and put it on top of the paper.
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	and if the illness is held only in one eye, then you should operate on one, and also on both.
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	and put moistened cotton under the eye.
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	et the patient's chest be in your hand and place your thumb showing above the medicine, and press it and move it all the times that the patient feels the biting of the medicine, for he feels biting as if from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then take away the medicine from your hand.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the biting is past, then lift up the cloth, and reward if you see the paper lifted as if it were lifted by constraint of fire or by incision.
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and if it is thus, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If not so, then put more medicine on the cloth or let the medicine have its effect, until your works are equal and your eyes are in order.
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put a moistened cotton poultice on it until the redness is gone, after treating the cloth of ointment which is called "diaphenys" and others, until he is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary for you to take great care with your work so that it does not fail in the eyes of others.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper becomes soft afterwards, and the hairs prick in the eye, then the medicine recommences on that same place which is softened by the paper properly, just as you did before;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the cure until they are healed;
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and that is the shape of the fir cone of myrtle:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in greatness and smallness, and according to how they are constricted;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and let not the right way be revealed to him who is ignorant of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	(Note: This appears to be a new section header, indicating that the text is about to describe a different medical procedure or treatment.)
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you cure a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your cures do not help, then it is necessary that you make it cauterized according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Command the patient to place his head on your shoulder;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and hold the ministers' head between your hands in such a manner that it does not move or leave its place;
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	then put wet cotton in egg white or in purslane juice on the eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	after burning the cautery which is thus:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and it is shaped like a comb at the top as if it were the cautery itself;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if you look, then it is pointed from one end to the other, and if you look, then it is also like a tent;
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but all the same, this which is shaped is useless for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	After pressing the fistula if it is open, and removing the purulence, and drying;
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and if it is closed, then you must work on it, and remove the pus from inside.
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	after put above the hot cautery and hold your hand on the cautery at the part above the nose up to the eye so that your hands do not go crazy.
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and put the cautery in the fat of the oil and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery just up to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If not, then repeat the fire treatment once more, and if necessary again, and let it be for three days.
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	After that, apply a moist cotton poultice in butter, and the treatment of drying ointment until it is healed, and if 40 days have passed and it is not healed, then apply medicine with a corrosive quality until the bone is uncovered.
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and read according to what comes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of doing a cautery on a fistula that none of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	You open a fistula and leave it open;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	After that, put in the opening one subtle camomile of which there is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and fill it to the quantity of an egg-sized piece of pommade;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and hold your hand with camomile firmly, and do not let the patient move until the pommade has melted into its own oil;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and it is necessary to put on the patient's eye a damp cotton cloth over an egg white or in water:
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	the poultice if it does not take the place of a fistula, and the wound by marvelous sanitation.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed through the cautery that we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then it is necessary to make a perforation in the navel, and bring the fistula back to its natural place within the navel according to what is fitting for its own location.
des crevaices en levres	(Note: This appears to be a new section header, indicating that the text is about to describe a different medical procedure or treatment.)
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times there occur cracks in lips called "fissures", and similarly in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as we have said in the divisions, and the treatment does not help, then warm a small surgical cauterizer according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And put it hastily into those fissures until it becomes just so;
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the treatment, the place of cerote as long as it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	(Note: This appears to be a new section header, indicating that the text is about to describe a different medical procedure or treatment.)
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess comes to the root of the throat or in the uvula, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it has made a purulence and run and is enveloped and becomes a fistula;
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you cure it as we have said in sections, and it does not benefit.
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	then it is necessary that you make the cautery according to the quantity of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	After the boil or abscess of the fistula, and hold your hand so that the iron becomes cool in its presence, and then leave.
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do it thus once or twice, after the treatment of what we have said in remedies, until he is healed.
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if he is healed thus, that's good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in his chapter.
dou movement des dens	of movement of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure him with medicines and it does not work, then place the patient's head in your hand.
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	after apply the fire cauterization where the form will come out here after, in this manner as you put a chain on the tooth.
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and place the hot hasten inside the cauterization, and hold it so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth.
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	after lifting your hand and restarting the cautery according to your will;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	after filling the patient's mouth with salty water, and having him hold it for an hour and a rich sweat.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this manner the teeth that were moving are fixed, and the gums softened are restrained, and the moisture corrupted is dried.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When the toothache comes from coldness, whether it is hot or cold, and medical treatments do not work, then it is necessary to cauterize according to two ways:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and butter cautery and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Butter cautery is such that you take butter from a cow, and shape the end into a iron or copper spoon;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	then take cotton and wrap it around the point of a tent, and melt in butter, and place on the aching tooth quickly and hold until it cools.
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	and thus do it often until its virtues come to the root of the tooth, and if you see that the wool and cotton are soaked in cold butter, and place on the aching tooth, and then put hot iron until the fire reaches the gum of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The fire cautery together with fire is such that you take a dog of iron or clay, and it is thick so that the fire does not come to the mouth of the patient.
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	After heating the cautery, in order that the form will come out afterwards, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled down.
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Do this often, for the pain will be taken away that very day or the next one.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary for the patient to fill his mouth with good butter in the pressure of that cautery, and then let it flow.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And make a cautery wherever you want, and according to what you can.
et c’est li forme de la caine:	and this is the form of the iron rod:
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When scrofulas are of a slimy and cold moisture, and are not obedient to digestion through medicines, then burn the cautery so that the form comes out, and have two openings for the fumes to issue from one side of the cautery.
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	and place the hot cauterize on the abscess once, or twice if necessary, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess;
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	and if the abscess is small, place the cauterize according to the size of the abscess, and leave it like that for three days;
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	and put a moistened cloth in butter so that the sore is removed;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterwards, apply ointments and unguents until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the gut:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When the moors overcome the channels of the womb, and similarly when this comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be purged first by soluble medicines;
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	afterwards, make a cauterization at the root of the throat, and take care not to come all the way up to the throat, and let it burn only a little bit.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	After which, I do another cautery at the joint of the neck to the head of the spine, and it is the cautery that is called "clavicle" from which we have the form beforehand.
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat the place as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	of the throat
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When all and every illness of perturbation are from cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or sweating, and it is an old disease, then I do two cauterizations on the forehead in the soles.
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	and another cautery inside the breast between the two breasts;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	and it is the cautery that is called "clavicle" according to the form previously said.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you see, do a cauterization that pierces all the cauterization which is called "point" from which the form is before in the illness of the ears;
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and let the points be just up to thirty, or around that.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After healing according to what is said above, and having the fire cauterization at three rings according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And therefore are the cauterers lighter, because you make them in triplicate.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	(unchanged translation from earlier)
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	Then instruct the patient to lie on his back and on his side.
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	after lift the kerf that is inside the tittle of the doves with your left hand.
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	and if the joint is dislocated within, then apply the cautery which has two needle-like things in this form.
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	and cauterize the kerf as far as it can be pierced to the side, and let the figure of the cautery come together with four cauteries.
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	and because of this it is made a cautery with the cautery that has three needles, therefore the figure of cauterization has six cauteries.
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and are the nerves according to the subtlety of a tent and this is the form of the cautery that has three needles.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And once is added to that one nerve for which there are eight cauterizers.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	After this put on the fire cautery powdered with ceruse.
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After this make the patient rest, and do not move the limbs for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, little good happens then, so make a cauterization on the thick part of the cauterized skull, or many cauterizations in pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and much moisture come to the stomach, and they trouble his complexion, and there are many cathartics for him, and he is accustomed to the usual cures but does not benefit, then it is necessary that the patient lies down on his back, stretches out his legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	Then make three cauterizations below the ribcage to the quantity of an egg, with all the cautery sharp, and two cauterizations outside the two sides until the shape of the cauterizations is at three angles, and have such space between one and the other that they will not be joined together when they will give forth pus.
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	and let the cauterizations be so deep that they penetrate the two parts of the skin, and let the shape of the cauterizations be according to this form without adjustment.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you see it necessary to cauterize a large one in the stomach according to this form;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	and whoever has fear of this cautery, cauterize it in piercing and sign on the stomach at one point according to the quantity you see fit.
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	Then the cauterizer performs the entire fire cautery which is called "points".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the care of the wound that we had before, until he be healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When pain comes to the liver from cold and moisture and great windiness, as long as it is greatly removed from its natural composition by superfluities;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the patient is treated as we have said in sections, and it does not help him, then it is necessary that the patient be purged on his liver;
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and mark three cauterizations according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, below the ribs, where the man's flank comes;
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	and have a space of about an inch between each cauterization;
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	and let the cauterizations be on the length of the body, and do not press too hard with your whole hand at each cauterization;
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	and let it burn only half as long as the key, and have the patient stand straight on his feet;
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	and if he cannot, then he must kneel, stretch out his legs, and lift up his arms.
et c’est li forme:	and that is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if you wish, then burn the cauterizing fires with a knife, being subtle and skilled in the art, and beware that you do not burn all the flesh, for you would dry out the entire body.
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and let it come just to boiling, for the blood is very subtle thereabout, and you know this well.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When he has an abscess on the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the capsule:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	if it is in the flesh, then the patient feels no more than moderate pain;
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	and if it is in the capsule, then he feels excessive pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And then when this treatment was for mirrors, it is necessary that the patient be placed on his back on a pillow;
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	and then sign over the site where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which is similar to a reed, because this is its form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And cauterize the cautery so long as the coals are burned, and come to just short of bursting, so that the burning is all gone.
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the treatment according to the treatment of wounds until he is healed;
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	and it does not behoove anyone to use this cautery except someone who has studied for a long time in the art of medicine, and by whose hands these illnesses have been cured on some occasions.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	He can work boldly, and it seems to me that it is better to leave them.
dou cautere de pleuresin	of the cauterizing for pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The old ones said that one should make plural cauterizations of aristolochic roots, and in such a manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	take a root of aristolochic, as long as you can find, and be dry, and also as thick and as long as your thumb;
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	and the moill in oil, and the emprens to fire, and cauterize the cautery between the forcele and low col, and two little cauterizes a bit down in the part that is below the beard;
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	and two little cauterizers between the fifth rib and the sixth, declining a bit behind;
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	and one cauterizer in the breast, and another above the stomach, and one between two shoulders, and two on the ribs of the breast after the cauterizer that is between two shoulders;
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	and do not press your hand, but make it open freely just as in smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	And they say that any old person uses the fire cauter to make it look like a razor, and heats it up and puts it between the ribs, until it comes to that abscess;
