et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout;	and let them be separated between the two shoulders because they are not joined together with this fire cautery at all.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and that is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	When tears are flowing from the eyes that are above the forehead of the head of hair, and there is no profit at all from medicine being applied to it, and you see the patient's face growing red, and feels the forehead burning as if it trembles;
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	and if the skin is tender and moist so that the hairs of paper are fallen, and the papers are scorched and burned by the heat of tears, then there is need for this care.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And the ancients called it "contused cure", and that is to make three incisions on the forehead of the patient who has this disease, in equal parts according to the length of the forehead.
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	and be one of the cuts like two going all around in front, and the others go up to the ribs above the papers, and take care of incising the arteries that are on either side above the papers;
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	and keep your hand away from the continuity of the two jawbones, and be each wound the size of three fingers across the joint;
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have prepared a piece of sponge and many cloths to absorb the blood, then pour the vinegar solution through two parts where this is the shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	from the incision which is below the temple just to the second incision;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	and scrape off all the keratin that is between the two cuts up to the furrow on the bone, then do the other part from the middle incision just to the other second, and then draw out this vinegar solution.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	So insert into the first cut the instrument called "culterelle", and it is very well sharpened on one side, and soft on the other side, not sharp at all, and this is the form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the knife cutting towards the fatty part of the shoulder blade, and the knife soaping towards the bone, and push it in as far as it comes to the middle incision.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And tie all the bandages that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous right up to where the key opens, and then make another cut in the middle slit right up to the other edge.
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	and then draw out equal blood, and express the place by the taken blood;
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	then put a cloth made of old cotton in each slit, and put wet cloths soaked in vinegar, oil, and ashes on top, and make sure that no abscesses form.
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and on the third day, loosen the bandage, and administer great plenty of cold water, then apply a balm of basilicum with rose oil, and other treatments used for wounds, until they are healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When anyone comes with a long-standing catarrh accustomed to it, and you see the eyes tight and small, and weakening the sight, and burned papers.
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and the hair falls out, and the head is filled with a deep pain, and the patient is worn out;
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	then you should know by these accidents that those materials and the cautery do not come forth except from many veins, and the mother cares for what is there, so it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you instruct the patient to rear his forehead, then make a great gash in the forehead and another of considerable width inside.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And begin at the left temple to the right temple, and make the incision up to the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and withdraw your hand from the nerves of the temples that move when eating;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is exposed, squeeze out all the blood with a sponge, and then insert between the two lips of the incision a piece of old cotton cloth, and tie it with linen;
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	then bind it above with damp cloths soaked in wine and oil, and beware of hot apostemes;
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	when it is removed, then you should rub the bone until cartilage begins to form, and then treat it with things that excite flesh, which makes it grow.
En teil maniere:	In such a manner:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	Take two parts of flour of wheat, and four parts of saffron, and make a plaster.
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	and administer it to these wounds in order to expel all sorts of corruption.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stopping of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	All that falls into ears is one of the four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	or grains, or beasts, or a piece of mining iron, or similar things like iron;
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	or seed, such as jasmine, vetches, peas;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or flowing things like water and soft mud and similar substances.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it pierces the ear or in some other way does not fit at all with the ear and does not grow in the ear, then place the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, if it yields any drop of purple oil or sesame oil, then administer an extraction;
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	and make it stink with conditions, and stop his nostrils when the stinking comes, and put around his ear pieces of cloth or wool;
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and it stands above the ear.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Many times harm comes from this treatment;
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come harm, then provide extraction with fine forceps, of which the shape is this:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it jumps out from the forceps, that's good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	if not, then provide extraction with a fine needle of small double edge;
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	and if it does not jump out through that, then make a rope of linen and insert the end of the rope or the hole of the ear strongly, and stop what is around the rope with wax so that the blood cannot enter with the rope;
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	then pull it out forcefully, because many times harm comes from this as we have said;
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	and if harm does not come in that manner, then take some glue of which it takes the birds, and put in some instrument that is sharp for this to do, and wrap a little cotton around;
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	Then press the glue on the stone or whatever it is, and make it stick.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if she doesn't burst forth from all these things that we have said, then hasten to cut off the ear before the abscess comes forth and spasms.
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	and the manner of cutting is that you first let the patient's head bleed from the cephalic vein, and extract the blood according to its natural flow, then have the patient sit between your hands and turn their ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear in the fatty or bony area.
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and make the incision as round as a moon, until you come to the stone, then scrape it according to your power, and quickly suck out the bone.
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and care for it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if there are grains within and they swell, then administer an extraction.
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if he cannot come out, so administer a spoonful of subtle medicine according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and apply an incision to that lump.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do it when you think that the grains are moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have cut it into many pieces;
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then extract with subtle forceps and a sucker, just as we said, so that the extraction is easy.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water that flows into the ear, it is necessary for the patient to use condimental sneezing first, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And be steady above that ear itself where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps forth because of that, it's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	if not, then take many pieces according to the length of your should be thin and light, and heat them slightly in the fire;
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and put one or two holes in the patient's ear, and lift up from below with his fingers from the other side, and strike with another piece on top of the piece that is in the ear;
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and do not cease to pile stone upon stone until the water flows out entirely, and thus it will flow entirely;
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	and if you see, then take a vine, and put one end in the ear, and wrap the other end around it with fire until the thickest part of the vine is burned;
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	then do the same to other vines until the water flows out entirely, as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In the extraction of an animal, if it is small, like a hedgehog and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division;
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it is large enough to be felt, perform an extraction by forceps;
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and this is the easiest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In the extraction of earwigs from ears, when you have cured it as we have said in the division and in treating with distilled things, and the cure does not benefit, then you must look at the ear to the sun:
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	If no wound is apparent, then treat with subtle tweezers, and if not, take the cord of which the form is there:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And insert the most subtle thread into the ear according to the quantity of the patient's suffering, then pull strongly on the whole cord;
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey and come out, then wrap cotton around the cord as I said in the stone;
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	and if they do not emerge as we said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proved in the killing of worms, and you will find them or treat on the distillations;
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all this instrument, of which the form is there as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And it is of silver or lead a large vessel below to small holes, and above over for distilling.
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	and to press inside the distillation with the instrument of lead well-made for that, and if you see take the razor and envelop it around the pointed cotton.
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	then pour out your oil or juice, and whatever you see of your medicines in the pipe, and the pipe be in the ear.
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	then put everything inside the razor to all the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled or dripped out of the ear.
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	and the patient will sense it inside, and let the distillation be placed over a pot warmed by fire so that it can be distilled in the ear.
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	and keep it from being too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stopping of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born without a single perforation in their ears;
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	and this same thing happens to men through the bursting of a wound or a piece of bone within the ear, and these bursting things sometimes go all the way into the ear so that one can no longer see;
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	and sometimes it happens that the perforation is very large and one sees very well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	Then the one that goes all the way in, if one cannot see it, is for serious healing and many preparations; and as for the one that one sees, it is necessary to put the patient's ear to the sun;
et regarde dedens:	and look inside:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	if you see the opacity appearing, then the work is complete in all this space that is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And be gentle and careful on both sides, before and behind, so that it does not hurt the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	If the opilation is of a new-born bone or the flesh of the ear, so hold it with fine pincers and cut it lightly, until that flesh is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the opilation is done perfectly in the ear, then take a subtle and light rasor and heat it slightly by the fire, then put it in the flesh of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you sense the opilation from which the patient feels grief to hear, pierce lightly, and be careful not to wound the nerves of the ear;
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	Then put in the ear a tent according to the width of the perforation, and moisten it with Egyptian pitch.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do this every day until the wound is closed, or take a tent and moisten it with red water, and powder on vitriol brews;
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	And if you see the ear swelling, then it is necessary that you remove the tent and put on another moistened tent made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal him until he is sound.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if there is a discharge of blood, then dip a sponge and wring it in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other cures that stop the bleeding which are found in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	Of the flesh of paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	These leaves that come from the eyes when they are moist and dry, so you should stretch them with tweezers and pincers, and cut off a spatula of its roots;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	then place it on the glassy boil.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if it does not blister, then cauterize with a subtle lens-shaped cautery, and the cauterizing after the incision is good.
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and many times repair, until nothing remains of their roots;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	and when they are cauterized by fire, the roots are burnt and do not return.
de la gresle	Of the Hellebore
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Many times come leaves from the eyes that seem like hoarhound in their shape and hardness, and because of this, this disease is called "grandine", and it is a collection of thick moisture above and below the paper.
li ovraiges est telz:	The works are such:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	Take care if the gravel (or stone) moves from one side to another, and it is a light thing to know;
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Then make the wound then wide, then scrape each part lightly, then take it with forceps and cut.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	If you cannot cut it without piercing a little bit of the paper, it will not trouble the patient;
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	and if the wound is great, then sew it up with a stitch and care for it until it is healed;
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	and if it is small, do not apply force, because the swelling will restore it soon and produce flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the stone is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, then turn it over with the paper, take hold of the stone with forceps, and cut and press it from one side and the other;
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	and if the paper is displaced by incision, this does not matter;
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	and when the wound is cut, let flow a salted water of aqua, and care for the place where the flesh is injured until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	Of the fat of eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a fat that is injected into the sheets of paper above, and this happens more often in children than in adults, and it hurts them a lot, and they come to the catharist at dawn, and cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears hasten to their eyes;
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	and therefore they lie down on their faces soon, and sleep above, and have their papers beneath their eyelids moist that the swelling and appearance have covered with the exinach which appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the lid at your elbows and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the way of the work is that the patient puts his head on the same side;
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains each part, then put it on him;
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press it with your hands on both sides, so that the contents are assembled within the circle;
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	then make in the middle of the moisture a groove about as wide as the incision one makes when opening a vein;
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and cut the skin so deeply that you come to the contents;
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	and in several dispositions the contents come out of the groove, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	then take it out in one piece of cloth wrapped between your hands at the end, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread;
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	and guard that you do not insert into the wound, so as to reach all the way to the eye, so as to cause damage.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the scalpel does not open in the beginning of the wound, so then slightly widen the wound a little until it appears.
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	then pull it as we have said, then wet cloths in oil and water, and place on the wound, and strain with bindings.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if such men who burn their gauze and put it on to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then let them take care until they are healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to the hot joint, then treat it with poultices soothing until they are healed.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When other hairs grow than those that are natural, and are inflamed, they harm the eyes, and cause to come forth habits of diseases such as tears and softening of the papers and pimples, so that it is a cause of the destruction of the eyes.
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	and this is the cure according to four manners:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	or by fire cautery together, or by medication according to what is written in the chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and stitching or by threads, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary that you place the patient's head on your shoulder, then turn the paper of oil to your left hand.
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	If she has changed, it is good.
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	if not, then put a needle on all the thread above;
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and be this on the edge of the paper where the hairs grow below these hairs, and treat the thread above all the paper, and turn it to the razor.
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then make in the part below the paper, below the adjusted hairs, all along the spatula's edge, from the great tear to the small one.
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	then pull out the thread and put below the paper a small tent of cotton and linen, then sign on the paper an image of enema, like the branch of myrtle, and although it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see unfolding the paper which is divided into all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if someone has need, they cut off a great quantity of paper according to what the paper is softened.
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	Then fill all the spatula up above the two lines that you have signed, and start with great largesse just a little.
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	and let one of the incisions be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert the knife into one of the two corners of the key, then scrape all.
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	then assemble the two lips with a stitch of an needle at all the thread of fine wool, and stop the bleeding, and make the excess threads above the two knots at all gluing things, if you see making this.
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	and if not, then don't bother, and leave the stitch and threads just for three days or four.
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	then cure the wound without stitches of things drying and constraining, for the paper comes to life at the closing of the wound and its assembly, but the stitch is bitter (as they said in olden times), and this is work without fear.
et si a une autre maniere:	and if
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and it is that you sign the paper with a figure that is like the leaf of myrtle, as we have counted, at three uncials severed according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what rises above the small forces equally according to the shape that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you have no power to hold the forceps, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle with one thread, and pass it through the shape;
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	and pass the other thread alongside the great gutter, and the second thread alongside the small one, and tie them together equally between your two threads;
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin above where you have signed, as we have counted, then bring together the two lips of the wound by stitching, and care for it until it is healed;
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	and if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with ointment and similar balm calming;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	and sometimes it happens that the hair of the parchment is converted:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	if it is necessary that you use what we have said about cutting;
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the cut in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The treatment of cankers is according to this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and it is that you convert the parchment and make an incision within according to what I have said, then make two cankers by art, and two subtle threads as long as the parchment and the width of the spatula are;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and tie the two ends of the two parts where you hold the threads;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then assemble one and the other subtly on what rises from the parchment of oil, and strain the two cankers from the two parts together;
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and leave it thus for some days, and the skin which is strained will die and turn black and hard, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If he delays, if he needs medical attention, then cure him until he is healed.
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	and when the wound is closed, and the paper (presumably a dressing) has been lifted away, and the hairs can no longer prick.
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	and this is the shape of the two canines that you will make according to this figure and according to this length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	the work is such that you take a fine needle, and insert a soft and fine silk thread into it.
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	then tie the knots together and tie one to the other gently, and let the length of the threads be a palm's length.
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	then order in the chase the other fine silk thread briefly, and tie the ends of the thread together.
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	then put the patient's head on your shoulder;
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and let it be done in the sun so that the work is revealed, for this is a subtle and delicate work, then insert the needle into the whole length of the chase at the root of the adjacent hair, and make it pierce through the paper quickly as you pull it up over the natural hair.
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	Then pull out the hair up to the chase, and push that hair into the chase if there is one, two, three, or more.
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Then pull out your hand so that the hairs grow forth all over the chase on paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not grow forth with it, then pull out the chase downwards to all the thread that you have ordered, until the chase grows forth from the pore above and you can see it by the sight of the eye.
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	Then pull out the chase and the thread, and let it rest for two days or three, until the hair grows back in its place and the scar forms above.
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hairs are small, accompany them with long hair from natural beards, and raise it up with that one you leave behind, until they are elongated and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the corruption of the oil.
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this sickness called "aleacrati" comes to the eye, so there are two ways in it:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or an incision, or a burning, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the way of working on it is that you cut open the suturing, and divide the lips of it, and put inside linen cloths, and tie it until it is healed;
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and it is not necessary that you use in its treatment things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do this, then the disease comes back worse than the first one;
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but your work with softening things, such as fenugreek;
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and rose water or althea and flaxseed are cooked, and oil of yarrow melted in any of the oils, and it is wrapped in a cloth, and cures those.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the treasure of your care is that you take heed to ensure it does not break apart according to its former form;
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And these works that we have said are not far from the remedies of this disease, that it may recover according to its former form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the flesh which comes into the oil.
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is below and is truly called "axacrati", and it is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accident comes from wound and gash and cauterization and similar things;
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	and the way of the work is that you take a needle with double thread, and thrust it into the flesh, and make it pierce from left to right, so that the threads may come out on both sides of the flesh;
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	then cut away the flesh above the needle, and make it split apart at the spatula's broad edge.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the shape of the paper returns as it should, that is good;
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	If not, then take the razor and place it in the cut, and turn the paper, and make two cuts or on the inside of the paper.
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	and be the corners of the two cuts at the two angles of the incision that you have cut, and make one angle such that when they are assembled, the figure is as if it were the figure of a letter that has no "I Grecs";
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	then remove that flesh, according to the quantity of its edges is worn down underneath, from what follows the paper, then join the two severed parts and sew them with a thread of wool.
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply the treatment for this that we have said about softening medicines and tents until they are healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the disease comes from a cut or an opening or a cauterization, then it is necessary that you make a smooth incision underneath the hairs of the paper, and according to what is mentioned before.
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	Then dislocate between the two boards of a tent, as I said.
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	and one must work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters prepare an engine to do all they can to bring back the figure to its natural form.
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the patient himself, according to what it is necessary for treatment and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the suddenness of the paper.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this swelling occurs in such a way that the paper above is stuck with oil white and cannot move nor do its natural works, then it is necessary that you put the tip of a razor underneath the paper, and lift it up.
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and stretch with pincers, until you extract what is stuck in the subtle sputum, which should not be too rough nor too cutting, lest the patient cannot endure that the sputum too rough nor injures the oil.
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	and let your incision, from which you cut away that assembled part, be slight so that the paper returns to its natural form.
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	and let all that assembled part be healed, and make no incision in the salty eye water, nor raise the sweet water, nor cause inflammation.
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	then put a linen cloth between the paper and the eye, and place on the eye a moistened woolen cloth in abundance of egg white.
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	and after three days use cooling remedies and things that soothe until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the grime of the oil.
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	Know that the ring is in two manners:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	it is nervous and resembles a hard ganglion, and another which is not nervous but resembles white frozen moisture, that when one touches it with iron and cools it in the pincers, so it cannot be undone.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	and one and the other likeness begins towards the great sewer, and grows little by little until it covers all the view and all the light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the manner of the incision is that the patient puts their head in your lap, then you work on the eyes.
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and lift the paper to your hand, then curl the finger like scissors of small doubleure, and stretch it upwards.
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then take a needle, and insert the horsehair, or oxhair, or beefhair, and make it strong.
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the point of the needle a little and insert it among the fingers, and pierce through to the entire needle, and tie the finger with thread and stretch it upwards, and scrape off all the hair from the side of the finger that is above the skin and down to the joint, then cut the remaining part at the root of the tear duct into all the subtle spaces and small forces, and leave the natural flesh or tear duct as it was before the incision, so that the body may not come accustomed to tears.
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	and sometimes the nails grow only to the fingernail or to the hair.
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	then one scrapes off all the fatty scum from which this form comes:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And beware that the scum does not touch the fleshy skin and break it, and that the pimple is not pierced.
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	and after the incision pours into the oil a little bit of boiled silk and makes a litargy from it, and leaves it until the next day.
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the doctor does what is needed so that they are healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the nail is not numb, and you cannot push the needle in, and the fingernails cannot enter, many times this appearance of nails is cured by medicine.
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and grow as I have recounted in the division, and if you see it cover, then work with the patient's oil and take the scum lightly according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And gently remove the scale from above subtly; and if you see that it does not decrease and the reason hastens there, then drip from your mouth into a cataract made of litargire and red chili pepper mixture, and stop the eye until the next day.
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	Then resume the other work according to this same work, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If no obstacle is found in the eye, as an abscess forms, then wash it with milk, and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the skin on the eyelid hurts the eye greatly, then suspend it from the onion, and cut off a part but not all, so that tears do not come forth.
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	Then drip into the eye red chili pepper mixture made of litargire.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	from the flesh that grows on the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	The eyes of some men never become red, and cover the prune with a yellowish substance, restrain above the paper, and turn to the backside, and seem like a rose made of pumice stone;
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	and the work is such that the patient places his head on your shoulder, then he works the eyes, and cools all that flesh with suitable unguents to it, and sustains it with strength;
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	then pare the first flesh, and go on paring to the razor's edge until the end, and take care that you do not cut into the eye during the operation;
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	and let the incision be like that of the spatula which we said in the incision of the tongue and with small forces one takes away the shag, just as the form shows after this chapter demonstrates;
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	and when the incision is completed and all the flesh is removed, then apply oil of safflower or you distill a red-colored liquid and similar corrosive medicines, and put on top of the eye a cloth soaked in egg white, so that it may be assured of hot abscess;
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	and if there is no longer anything, and the blood rushes to the surface, and you doubt a hot abscess, then leave off and treat the abscess with soothing things for a hot abscess;
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	then return to your work until it is healed, and thus make the joints set in the oil by this resemblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	But it is also necessary that you ease the treatment of each weak joint according to natural ways;
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and by the accidental way, in iron work;
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	and do not put your hand on any of these works until you see that those members are bearing up under this treatment.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	If there are veins that are red and covered on the eye, and tolerate the work of their sight and weaken the eye always.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	It is necessary therefore at first to observe what the joint is like, in which it swells, and whether it is inflamed, and there is no other disease besides the swelling;
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	then bind the joint in this manner:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	instruct the patient to put his head in your lap, then suspend those veins throughout all the way according to his wisdom, and let the veins be subtle doubles according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let the two ointments be by degrees in one mass according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	then tie those veins subtly and extract the blood hour after hour until you see the veins move away from the eye;
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	and beware that you do not obscure the eye with the points of the spatulae, and perform this work at the hour of noon in front of the sun, and be very hot in your work so that you do not slip up on those veins;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	and when you have done this, then distill in the eye a bitter green and red liquid to corrupt what remains of the sebaceous glands.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you are unable to tie it all up in that hour, then apply a poultice on the eye with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and let it be for some days until the pains are assuaged and you are assured of the abscess being hot, then recommence according to this manner which is before until he is healed.
et c’est li forme des forces:	and this is the form of the powers:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The doctor is called "arissati" fistula:
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	When you cure it by cautery and burning medicine according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is reason to open up the abscess where it should be, and extract all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and blackness, then remove it with all the instruments of which this is the form;
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	and it is called "aspre chief", and make it smooth up to the point where it is not rough again, and be pointed like a file as it is in this present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And put it on top of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your thumbs, and press your hand a little until you know that that corruption is removed;
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and make so every time then restore the place with medicinal remedies.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	if the wound is sealed and there is no bleeding, and the bowels are sealed and remain thus for 40 days, and it does not fester and is not abscessed, and evil consequences do not occur, know that it is healed.
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	but if not, then there is no other remedy than to bring back the fistula to its natural outlet according to this form:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	and it is that you uncover the bone for the second time by fire and by old medicines, and when it has been uncovered, take a file according to this form, and let the point of iron be at three angles, and let the file be worn down just to the head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	then place it on the bone near the socket, and withdraw your hand from the patient's point, then turn all the file until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it as if the blood flows if he holds his hand on his nose.
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	and then restore the place with dry medicines, as I have instructed you, and when the flesh is formed and hardened, then the matter goes to nothing.
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	for it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eyes are fully open and there is no obstruction to sight or decrease in vision, it is necessary that you bind the patient.
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	then heal, then apply cupping glasses or cauterize in order to draw out the blood, then put a poultice on the eye made of aloe and aloes and incense and sarcocolle, and then strain the eye and embalm it with bandages and drapings.
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	and the manner of the drapings is that you take soft drapings, and fold each one into four, and then put one on top of another according to the amount that the eyes need.
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	then strain it upwards with a firm bandage, and reapply the poultices to draw out without wounding.
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	then remove the poultices and let the oil be strained day and night, and if it becomes swollen, then you should compress it tightly.
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	then remove the swelling after a day and a night, and if you see the oil repairing, that is good.
se ce non;	if not;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	then reapply the poultice and bindings, and the swelling and poultices until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	The bursting forth of a grape-like vein
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When disruption comes to the uveous membrane, then it opens up, and comes forth with paper-like flakes like grains of resin, and it is dreadful to behold.
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	then if you see it cover, the work is such that you should insert a needle into the root of the affected part below up to where it is above, then insert another needle where there is a doubled thread from the corner of the eye.
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to its setting;
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then tie the loop of the doubled thread and bind a part of the vein around, and hold it well, then pull out the needle and put on a linseed oil moistened in abundance.
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and leave it so that the thread takes hold with the vein, then apply the oil to things comforting as long as the wound is healed.
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and at no time is the wound restrained by the vein except each part of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the eyes give great appearance, then pierce them with a subtle spatula that comes into the very font of the oil, and dry out the moisture albugine and descend the eyes, and enter it immediately;
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	then pull it out when it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the bottom of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is not far from a boil that is assembled in the eye, resembling a descending water, and it's not water;
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	and the manner of appearance of the work is that you make the patient sit on a well-prepared and straight seat, then take hold of the head with your two hands, and move it so much as you see the boil rise up to your eyes;
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	then let it be fixed, and do not descend, and let the light go away, and see the patient's things just as he used to;
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the boil's descent is not prepared just as we said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	then make the patient sit in your hands, then take a fine spatula and do on the keratinous cloth one piece by the continuation of the conjunctive with the keratinous cloth and the crown, until the boil comes out;
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and when it is issued, then distill in hot water with honey mixed with equal parts of honey and melissa or fenugreek boiled with honey, and then be treated by another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	from the waters of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have the likenesses of waters in the division, and what is needed for piercing;
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	so that it works according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	You should have the patient sit in your crossed hands, away from the light by the sun, and bind the healthy eye very tightly.
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	Then put the paper of the eye on your left hand if the eyes are left-handed, or on your right hand if the eyes are right-handed.
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	Then take in your right hand if the eyes are left-handed, or in your left hand if the eyes are right-handed, the instrument which is called "almagda".
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	Then place the point of the instrument beneath the crown by the width of a thumb in that corner of the eye nearest to the smaller tear duct, then insert the instrument called "almagda" virtuously, and turn your hand so it pierces into the eye, and feel that almagda comes into the empty thing;
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	and it is fitting that the measure of the path of almagda be at the bottom of the measure of the espace which is from the prune to the end of the nourishment;
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and this is the crown of the eye;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	if you see the bone in that paper through the clarity of the corneous cloth, and then place the instrument just below where the water is, then express it under one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	The patient sees what is going on now, if he looks at him and the instrument is in his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	After you rest for a little, and if the water rises again to the second way, place force with the instrument, and when it is fully seated and does not rise, then extract almagda lightly by rotating your hand little by little.
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then put back in water a little bit of salt crystal, and leave it under this oil inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put a poultice or a moist cloth of linen soaked in rose oil and an abundance of egg white on the wound, and bind it with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We and those who are of our time put a common brew with an abundance of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are some men who have very hard eyes, it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", which has this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And then just prick the joint alone, and not go too deep by much, but make it subtle, then put in alum, as we have said.
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	and at the completion of the work, prepare for the patient and the doctor to come, in which it sleeps on its back in this dark place.
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	and be still of all movements, and take light food, and do not move his head to the right or to the left, and remain according to his disposition for three days.
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	then loosen him in that same dark house, and test his sight, and let him see some things, and then put the bandage back on until the seventh day;
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	and it is not necessary for you to do this in the work of the cure or after incising now, but rather that you ease him, because the water rises hastily.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	If an abscess forms, then you should lance the eye before the seventh day, and direct it towards that which soothes the abscess.
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	And when it is eased, then lance the eye and put a poultice on its face for covering any day, and be in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	And then go out of the dark house little by little, and adjust yourself to your condition;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	and know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And one came to us who was from the land of Irach, who told us that in his land he had seen a man with an almagda wound, which makes water come out, but I never saw anyone like it in our land, nor did I ever read about it in books of old.
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	and by chance it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the likenesses of the forms of madness, because one who does not know them sees it;
et soient d’arain proprement:	and are of earth properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the ends of these should be of this same subtlety, and the last in three sharp angles.
de la char sor le neis	From the flesh on the nail.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	Sometimes birthmarks or freckles appear unevenly distributed, which causes some to resemble scorptions in many places;
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and if one has such birthmarks or has one enchanted with fiery color, and another soft of pale color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In that birthmark which is soft and not enchanted, it is necessary that you have the patient sit between your hands facing the sun;
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and open his nostrils, and apply the onion to those birthmarks, and treat them fiercely;
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	then do what you can sustain by the subtle and acute judgment of your part, as long as you know that that birthmark is entirely open.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if there remains anything that cannot be covered, so work on all the instruments lightly, so that nothing remains.
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and if it is not inflamed, or abscess appears, then hasten as is fitting.
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if it's malignant abscesses, then hasten and cauterize as much as the blood is staunched and all the dressings are removed, then pour or apply neat oil and vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the poultice works, and moisture comes just to the palace, know that it is healed.
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if moisture does not penetrate as it should, know that there is new flesh in the bone above, to which instruments do not come to cut.
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	then it is necessary that you put a thread of linen about an inch thick there, and have it soaked in oil for us, and have between each night's space what should be or less.
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and put the patient's head against the pillow in his neck so that it is at its power, and pull towards the scent until it comes down through the neck into the mouth;
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and many times do this to children in schools, and it is a light thing for one who wants to make them do so;
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	then hold the head that comes from the neck in one hand, and the other head that comes from the mouth in the other hand, and tie one after the other as we are on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this as long as you know that the night has not corrupted that flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian oil, and put it back on the neck just like before.
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	do this for three days or more, until the oils corrode all that is remaining of flesh.
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	and then put on him a leather thong for some days until he is healed, and if he needs drying medicines, so he uses them;
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, by which one distills oils and medicines or something:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And it is made of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and leads in the same way;
