et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you see, then make a closed tube, and let the instruments be full to purge the head;
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and have a handguard at the head to hold it when one heats the oil or some liquid.
de la char sor le neis	From the flesh on the nail.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times a disease appears on the head called "telul", and it grows and becomes large over time, until it is visible to look at.
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and therefore it is necessary that you cut off the top at the beginning, and remove all fur, then put on the cautery or burning medicine;
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if you wait to cover it until it is great, then beware if it is hard, of a foul colour, of poor sense:
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	for it will not be touched by iron because it is an enchanted abscess, for when you cut into it at some time, great harm comes to the patient;
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is of soft touch, not foul colour, and you see that it can be completely cut out, then empty the patient and cut it in such a way as to remove fear, and cure the limb of things constricting and binding.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nail is cut and cleaned.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when solutions of continuation come to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, more than in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	It is therefore necessary that this happens in someone, so look to see if the wound is fresh with all its blood;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then stitch the two lips together with a seam, then heal it until he is sound.
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scrape off all the parts of their keratin until they heal, then stitch the two lips together with a seam, and bind them tight, and powder with powdered blood of dragon, and burn incense;
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put on powders a piece of ointment or other ointment suitable, and let it be until it clears up by itself, then cure with oil as long as it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The method of the stitching is that you bring together the edges:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or with needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or with thread, as I have informed you.
des apostemes des levres	Of lip abscesses.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	In the mouth, abscesses often arise within hard, resembling tiny peas, and smaller and larger;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	then it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cut on each one, and take as many pinches and clip in each part;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then apply a poultice to the place after the incision of vinegar broth, until the blood is staunched.
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then treat the area with ointment, and care for the joint of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	Of the flesh of the gums.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Often a white spot appears on the gums which the ancient people called "albulus";
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	so you should hold it with forceps, and cut to its root, and let the pulp or blood run.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	then place on the joint a vitriol ointment, or other drying and constricting powders;
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if the sore returns after the incision, and this often happens, then cut it a second time, and cauterize it;
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not return after the cauterization;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	Of abscesses.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Sometimes they are assembled at the head of teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are foul and rough;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and green, until the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink;
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	so you should make the patient sit between your hands, and his head be in thy faith, and receive the teeth or gums that appear, until there is nothing left;
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and thus do with the blackness and greenness, and yellowness and other spots, until they are cleansed;
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	and if you take away what is at the first reason, it's good;
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	but if not, then recommence on the second day and the third, until you have everything cleansed;
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and know that the teeth have need of various forms of instruments to clean, according to what the work shows, because the scraper with which one removes tartar from the teeth has other forms than the one with which one cleans between the teeth;
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and these forms and others are to be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of its pain that you delay pulling it as long as you can, for this should not happen at all.
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	for it is a very high substance just up to when one has no excuse to regret.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	When the patient is constrained to go out, it is necessary that you are certain about the tooth aching.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the patient's pain was so great that they thought it was in their tooth, and believed that it was a holy tooth, and had the good tooth pulled out.
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and yet the pain does not depart from him on account of this, until the bad humor departs, for we have already wanted to do this with these saints;
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are well certain of the tooth's pain, it is necessary that you scrape all around the tooth with a spatula very strongly to keep the gum from all sides;
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then move it with your hands or fine pincers at the first pace and pace, until it is well extracted, then secure the pincers well.
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and let the patient's hip be between your holy knees, and hold it well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking, and if it does not jump out, then take one of these instruments and insert it inside from each side lightly, and move it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the tooth is perforated and eaten away, then you should fill it with cloths, where the holes are.
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and if you strain it subtly with forceps, so that it does not break while being strained.
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and it is necessary to carefully cover around the gum for loosening the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take good care that you do not break it, and leave one part, and reinsert it into the patient through the malicious root causing greater pains than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And beware that you do not act like the ignorant surgeons who, because of their haste and boldness, sometimes break the carriage and do not bring about what we have described.
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but sometimes bring about great harm through the decay of those roots that remain, or by breaking the carriage, as we have often seen.
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the tooth is loose, wash it with wine or with vinegar and with oil;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and if there is bleeding and it comes, which often happens, then apply the place with a piece of vitriol crushed.
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	and if that does not help, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The forms of the instruments, by which one should extract the teeth first, should be long-pointed and thick-gripped, so that they do not double back when you pull out the tooth;
et ce sont les formes:	and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And have large handles so that they do not bend when pulling, and be made of well-forged iron, and have teeth to keep them from slipping.
de la racine des dens	of the roots of teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the roots remain to be pulled out, it is necessary that you put a moistened cotton cloth on the wound for one or two days until the wound is softened, then insert the forceps called "algefri", by which the head seems like the beak of a hawk;
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and they should be made inside as if with a file and that is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these forceps, it is necessary that you uncover the entire layer of skin around the root, and put in the instrument called "althali", which is a scraper, by which this is its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And let it be large and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out for this reason, it is good.
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	if not, then use all the instruments, by which forms come forth hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you help with this instrument that has two handles, this is its shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in front of the roots of teeth, and this instrument which seems like great forceps, this is its shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let these instruments be such that they cannot break, and know that many instruments of dent are;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other instruments which are not counted;
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and wise and subtle masters find by themselves the instrument that is suitable for each patient's disease, according to their work and the malady they present, for there are certain diseases where ancient ones did not teach an instrument due to the diversity of cases; and if it does not break the bone or any other bones, or where it can be done, then he seeks out the instruments that are needed, as I have told you, and helps with gestures, by which the form comes forth hereafter:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be large and well-holding to hold the bone, that it may not escape but can be held and removed.
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then restore the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is putrefaction in the bone and it is small, so that it returns to all this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural shape of the body, and its form is ugly, and especially in young girls, then it is necessary that you know if the tooth is next to the other tooth, and is not in its proper place, and cannot be straightened or trimmed.
adonques lou raie;	then draw it;
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it is stuck with the tooth, then take this instrument whose shape is like this and looks like a small beak, and has an iron point sharp to the tip.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the edge grows gradually day by day due to the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others; and if it is apparent that one can file it, then use a similar file as this is its shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and it is also like the file with which one makes needles;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and in a little lime, the tooth peels away bit by bit over a few lighter days, so that it does not move until it falls out.
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then the gum is smooth at the end and there is no rough edge, and if the tooth is too sharp and hurts the tongue, then it is necessary to file down the roughness until it is even, so that it does not hurt the tongue nor corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the tooth in front is loosened, either by percussion or falling out, and the patient cannot bite down on what they eat without choking, and you have treated them with restricting medicines, and this does not work;
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	so they must be restrained by a thread of gold, for the sons of silver become green and perish, but the gold does not change once.
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and let the thread be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the proportion of space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	et if you see the teeth to be aligned, then take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then put the jawbone between my teeth, if there is one or more, until you reach bleeding just to the healthy tooth on the other side;
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	then start the covering just to the part where you began, and strain your hand subtly and carefully, until it does not move anymore;
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then tie the jawbone with thread to a pair of tongs, and assemble them, and reposition between the healthy tooth and thus so it does not hurt the tongue;
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	and then leave it so tight as long as it can stay that way, and if it comes loose or the thread breaks, then strain it with another thread;
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	If it remained and served thus for all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the shape of the addressing of the two healthy teeth and the two molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth falls out, if one puts it back in its place, little by little, just as we have said;
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and does not intervene except for one who is wise and enduring, and sometimes one makes the shape of a cow's tooth of bone, and puts it in the place where there is a defect, and holds it so as we have said, and stays and serves thus long.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the link of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Sometimes this fault comes from under the tongue or by nature, which is born in this way;
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or through the accidental wound that has been healed;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the work is such that you work on the patient's mouth, and have their head in your healthy hand, and lift up the tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	Then tie the nervous ligament of the thigh, so that the tongue is released from its station, and if there is stiffness or swelling, and it's a sudden wound, then insert the unguent and tie the ligament;
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and take care that the incision is not too deep, because of the artery that is below.
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done, then lift up the wound of rose and easy water, or cold water, and put a linen tent under the tongue;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and dress the patient's wound each night, so that the swelling cannot harden.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if there is a flow of blood, then put vitriol powder on the wound;
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if the bleeding increases, then burn it with a slow-burning cautery, which is good for that.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then treat it with another treatment until it is healed,
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see it is a foul or black or hard boil, so that the patient does not feel it, then do not touch it, for it is a carbuncle;
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it is declining towards the bladder, and there is moisture, so that it discharges pus, and makes a fine sputum, and delivers from one side and another;
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if the blood flows at your work, so put on a vinegar poultice until it is staunched, then return to your work as long as you are drawing out all the pus;
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then lift up the head of the neck and shoulder, and treat with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Sometimes a lump comes into the throat which are called "godath", and they are properly called the two tonsils, and when you cure them as we have said in the section, and they are not healed, then beware:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	If it is an abscess of long duration with little sense and a dull color, then do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and the root is large, then do not touch it with iron, also for the avoidance of excessive bleeding;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but let it remain until it is dead, and then you will lance it, or it will burst on its own;
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	and if it is of white color and reopens, and the root is subtle, then prepare the instrument to cover it, but first see if the abscess has calmed down and is pacified.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then have the patient sit in front of the sun, and his hands be in thy hand, and the servant hold the mouth open and take the tongue between his hands, and press the tongue downwards onto all the instrument, so that it takes its form.
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and let it be of silver or refined lead, just as sharp knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	Can't you press the tongue on all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the pincers and fix it in the almond, and draw the thread above as far as you can;
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and don't touch anything with the cloths, then cut at the instrument, of which there is the form, that seems like one force;
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and yet the head is curved, and from one side to the other, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or of steel;
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then use pincers, by which the form appears:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And be cut on one side and on the other named;
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and when you have cut one of the almonds, then cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with hot water, and warm and easy, and if bleeding occurs, then gargle the patient with water or cooked skin of pomegranates, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stopped;
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then care for the patient until they are healed.
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	and sometimes abscesses arise in the throat besides those two almonds; if so, then cut them as the two almonds grow together.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was born inside her throat, namely the abscess of little sense;
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and I had already well closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the constricted passage, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had stayed like that for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that it had forced its way out through both holes of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I then hastened at once, and placed one onion in it, then the tumor burst open and a large portion of pus came out;
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	then I made another incision on the other side of the abscess, and opened up her mouth and pressed her tongue.
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	After incising these abscesses, and cutting off a part, and only one drop of blood issued forth.
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	And thus the passages of the throat were dislodged from the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not cease cutting off that abscess for a long time.
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	And the abscess re-crossed again, and filled the place that I had emptied, until it became very large.
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	Then I bound it and cauteryed it inside the throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	Thus it remained without growing;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I departed from those parts, and only God did something with them after me.
de l’uve	of the vein
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the swelling goes down to the vein, and it is emptied and it is long, then it is called "perpendicular".
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is under a thick and rounded one, then it is called "vein".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the abscess has been calmed, and it is subtle, so you must cut.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and she who is roundly assembled and is not long;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and she is sanguine or of a flesh color or black, so you must avoid cutting into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	Because there is great danger on the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	It is necessary then, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its swelling and length, that you make the patient sit before the sun, and press his tongue onto the instrument which we have mentioned above.
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	then stick the onion into the eye, and train it downwards, and cut with the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural boundary;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	for if you intervene more, so it troubles to voice, and to word;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and care for it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear to cover, you should use cunning at the cauterization of their sense of fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp as an edge.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And it is that the patient places his head in your hand, and then presses the tongue to the instrument that we have said in the chapter of cautery, and confesses with hot water, so that it is not too thick nor too clear.
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and use the handle of this instrument, which has this form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And there is on the head a covering or where one puts the medicine, just as the hairs of a cauldron, and put the instrument over all the medicine on the ulcer.
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the patient should sit on his side, so that the saliva and mucus flow from his mouth into the medicine, so that it does not descend to the throat and the wound.
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	Then hold your hand on all the medicine and press it onto the vein, for the amount of time equal to half an hour, until you see it congealed and the medication's abrasions are soothed.
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	And if you see, take cotton and envelop it on any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and fill the instrument with all the cotton in the cane above, until the cotton is applied to the vein.
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often, until the cauterization is perfect, then leave it to dry, and check after four days or five.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to reapply the medicine cauterization, then reapply it, and after the cauterization, apply a poultice around the vein, with cotton wrapped in butter, and cleanse all that is around the medicine.
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let them be bathed with cold water, and treat with gargling so long as they are cleansed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This cure is safer than incision, not the fire cautery;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calament and ysope and origanum and rue and camomille and avronne and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them in a pot, and put air in it, and make it boil.
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot should be well glazed with hard earth, and inside the pot have an instrument carved according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And it should be of silver or lead, and one of the ends sealed in the patient's mouth so that the vapor rises to the eardrum through the canal, until the eardrum is numbed.
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	afterwards it often renews itself, until the eardrum is dry, and be sure you do not do this at the beginning of the abscess's heating up, for many things happen there.
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not cause any harm except at the cutting of an abscess hot.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, take a cord and put a goose quill inside the head, so that the mouth of the patient does not have too much heat.
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	for the goose quill does not allow the steam to weigh on the mouth, and it is good care together with health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Often one should secure a piece of neck bone or fish spine, or nothing;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	so then you should test what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you may see the thing.
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and what does not appear to you and is returned in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach;
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	by chance if the things are thrust out through vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of bread, or a root of lettuce, or a fragment of dry bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and then thread is attached to the sponge and then it is swallowed again;
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it comes out, if it gets stuck, and then you will pull it out;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come out as we have said, then take the instrument of purling according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And the instrument should be curved at the head so that it can enter the throat more easily, and have the head lifted upwards;
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, lest all life come to it, nor push the bone inside;
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and make sure that the patient pushes the instrument, for thus the thing is forced out;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	If the ball is below, or he pulls it far away from all the instruments evenly, so that it is far.
de la sansue de la gorge	Of the sweat of the throat.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	No bloodless remedy is medicine for the without-sense, as I have said in the division, by the treatment of remedies;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and when it does not help at all, then look in the throat of the patient to the sun, and then press the tongue to the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the sweat, then take it away with all small needles or fine forceps that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this doesn't work, then take a braided cord, and tie it around the patient's neck, then heat the iron rod at the end of the cord, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is troubled by water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	then take a full view of cold water, and open the mouth, and spit it out without swallowing, and move it to his hand often.
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and as soon as the blood feels the water, it should be stopped.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not stop as we have said, then suffumigate the patient with asafetida, to the instrument that I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye.
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	It happens many times, for it will fall without a target.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the method of fumigation is that you take a pot where it has burning coals, and the opening should be covered with a perforated cloth sheet in the middle, and on that hole should be the head of the instrument.
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	Then you cast your fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane in their mouth and closes their mouth, so that the smoke does not come out but comes just to the sweat.
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and the sweat will now fall, and if it does not fall, then you begin the fumigation again many times;
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and the patient suffers thirst, and takes bitter things and salts, and does not drink water at all.
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and then it is necessary that they issue forth by this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	The shape of the instrument with which one draws out pus is such that when it can be seen, it resembles curved tweezers for inserting into the throat;
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and has the resemblance of a doctor's beak, and has the asperity of lime, so that what it takes, it cannot let go;
et vez ci la forme:	and thus is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters on abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Many likenesses of abscesses are, according to what the memory brings forth on this side and that in this book, and they differ in perforation and cutting;
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and it is in two manners, one of which is its own likeness, and because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for the bones that are at the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the fatty tissue are different from those that come together in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if abscesses should not be pierced at all, until the pus is fully formed according to its completion;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and if there are such abscesses that it is necessary to pierce when they are hard and do not die according to their completion, just as those abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come beneath joints, and one leaves it until it is rotting all around, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Where the abscess is located below the main member, and if you delay the piercing until it is mortified, so it will harm the main member.
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	where it is located at the foundation, if one pierces it when it is dead;
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and it is not necessary that you pierce an unripe abscess without complete digestion, except for one located at the foundation, which cannot be pierced to its depth and becomes elongated inside and thus a fistula forms;
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and it cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And it is necessary that you know the time of perforation of the abscess which is dead according to its fulfillment, and this is when the pain is appeased, and the departures of fever, and the reduction of pain and redness, and the swelling and hardening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and it is necessary that you make the puncture sit or lie dependent on the abscess, and where it opens up movements;
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and the puncture should be long in the body, and if the abscess is at the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no swelling.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those who ache, by consequence of that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the skin hardened, so it is best that you leave the puncture until it is confirmed in completed digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce before that, the body will be lengthened with the venom from it, and will be filled with much foul matter;
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and by chance harden the lips and the inner parts of him.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is any abscess that is pierced according to the breadth of the body, according as the members may need it.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And it is necessary that you bring out small abscesses, small pustules;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in great abscesses, great pustules, and many fissures according to the appearance of the size of the abscess;
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut the skin, and cover;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	When he is become as grey as the flags, and is wasted away, so it is necessary to do likewise as one does with infants:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if they are split into three angles, and if there are those of which one cuts in the manner of myrtle leaves, just as abscesses of angels;
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if they are those where one makes a round cut, and other cuts and similar trimming.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who do not have a head, like a soft abscess on the surface, it is necessary that you make an incision completely.
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and it is necessary when the abscess is large and has gathered great pus, and you make an incision, so do not draw out all the pus at that hour, but only some part.
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then stop the abscess just until the next day, then do not touch anything above it;
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	Make them so repeatedly by degrees, until the bowels open completely.
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Meanwhile, if the patient is of weak virtue, or a woman bearing, or small children, or old men decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the pulse beats quickly sometimes with the issue of pus, so that by chance the patient dies, and you are not aware.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Therefore, exercise great caution in this chapter, and when you have pierced your abscess, if the wound bleeds, and look to see if the wound of the abscess is small.
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it's a clean incision, then try to apply linen or old cotton.
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it's a large abscess and there are many perforations, then you must bind each one with a tent so that they come together.
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have cut away a part of the abscess from the skin and wrapped it around, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or a dry cloth made from linen, free from moisture, and bind it just to the third day.
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the surgeon and the oil doctor until he is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs at your work, then administer cold water and vinegar, and damp cloth, and place it on the bleeding spot repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the purging of blood persists, and he is administered government and care, and the powders that I have said are used in this book, and it is during the time of winter, and the lesions or abscesses are very nervous, then you should put on tents and wet cloths soaked in wine and hot oil.
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is in summer, and the lesions are fleshy, then you should put on wet cloths soaked in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said.
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then dissolve the abscess and the scab and the wound, as it is necessary, until he is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this must be known universally in treatments of abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	I have told you how to proceed before treating abscesses, and see this chapter.
des soros	of boils
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where small abscesses come from the head, and they are like little nests that we find in fabrics, just as a sparrow's nest is woven with threads, and there are many similar ones.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some fat and such that also have moisture like boils;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and if there are those which are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt that the artery does not go against it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the works of cutting are such that you try out all the instruments which are called "entromissoires", from which the form comes afterwards, whatever thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then let them make an incision above the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is drained, then scrape off without leaving anything the skin that contains that moisture, for it comes back again if you leave anything.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	then plunge cotton in Egyptian oil, if present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	if not, in water and silk, and dress the wound, and let it be just until the next day;
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and those who are left of the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then rebegin with cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain of the night;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the wound of oiling as is fitting, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess is not very swollen, then cut it according to this form, long-wise;
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and tear off the scabs, and flay it all around, and put all your care in drawing out the abscess where it lies;
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if the arteries resist you, then do as I told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do this with the abscess if it is pustular, and to cut and cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the cutting on the pustular abscess and the moist one is lighter, for they are full of blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if some of these abscesses or boils have no moisture, and those abscesses that I cut open on the head of an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and found the abscess just like a dry, rough, and white stone, and could not break it.
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if one had broken any of them, one would have made as much a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses coming from the head, greater than those that come from the heads of children and the roots of ears, let the opening be always at its most dependent place so that the pus may issue.
et les cure si com il covient.	and treat it as is fitting.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur in the neck and under the armpits and in the groin, and sometimes they come elsewhere in the body, and are many and are intertwined with one another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each scrofula is properly located within its own coat, like the boil and abscess of the head, as we have said.
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and the likenesses of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and also there are evil ones who do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	then look for one with good disposition to be touched, and it is similar in color to the body, quiet on each side and is not inflamed towards the neck veins nor arteries nor canal, and is not deep.
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	then you should scrape it above and remove the scab from each part, and if you need, take off the two lips of the scab on the nails, just as we have said in abscesses of the head.
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	et the wound is small and small, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or vein, nor let the spatula touch or press, lest the hands escape, and do not go too far, lest you cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or artery, and what you do does not let you proceed, then put in the wound a bit of vitriol or some powder that stops bleeding, and hold back the wound.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and let it be until the abscess is calmed, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the blood is stopped, then return to your work, until you have completed it.
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	then look at what remains as if there were no small ulcers, and cut them and clean them out.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if it has a great vein in the root of the scrofula, it is not necessary to cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and let it fall down without harm.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	Then wrap the wound in an old cotton cloth soaked in Egyptian oil, then apply treatment.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cover the entire scrophule, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them up now, then there will be no remaining superfluity due to the greatness of the scrophule.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you understand to cover the root of it, and pull strongly, and sew it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scrofulas that have superfluity, puncture there where it becomes moist;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and puncture it in the same way as the one mentioned before, depending on the case, then apply poultices with oil and similar things, so that what is left of the corruption may corrupt.
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well cleansed, apply an ointment to promote flesh growth until it is healed.
de squinance	of squinancy
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their speech.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	To those who have suffocated, it is necessary that the incision in the throat called "epiglote" be made.
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and one does not help by doing so, because all the veins and major blood vessels of the patient are inflamed at the abscess in the mouth or in the throat or in two armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the pore, it is necessary to cut the epiglote in order to avoid the peril that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is necessary then, when we wish to cut the epiglote, that we cut it below three circles or four small cuts across, between the two circles or by the quantity of the cut from the suture, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and this is necessary for the cutting of the epiglote because there is no flesh and the vessels are long in inquiry.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is fearful, then it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat to all its extent, then cuts the leather so that it comes to the chin.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and avoid shedding blood vessels if you see anything, and then cut the suture so that we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the incision of the vein of the chin which jumps forth through the broken place and by the lack of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed of which one doubts strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound of the skin, and sew it all by itself without the cartilage.
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer medicines that cause growth of flesh until he is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	On does not make this just so long as the throat is completely swollen, and the patient is judged to be dying, and death approaches.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut the epiglottis because the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and therefore the ancients command to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it has passed in three days or four; then they commanded to sew up the wound and heal, until it is healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a maid take a knife, and thrust it into her throat, and cut out part of the channels of the womb;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to cure her, and I found her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that was issuing from it, and I knew that she had not cut her throat nor conducted anything except the throat, and the veins were flowing out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, and sewed the wound, and healed her until she was sound.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and it happened to the maiden that she became hoarse of voice, and returned afterwards to her normal condition;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	therefore I say that in cutting the epiglottis one should not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This is a dislocation. It is called "hernia of the throat" and is a great abscess in the color of greenish copper, and it occurs mostly in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	and it occurs in two ways:
naturez, et accidens;	natural, and accidental;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	or natural has no deceit.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental is in two ways, of which one resembles fat to us, and the other manner resembles an abscess that comes from an artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and if there is fear, and it does not behoove to work with fire except in one who is small, and test and examine through all the intervening flesh:
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it thus as I say fat, and is unable to be moved by any means, so cut it, as one cuts fat, and treat it all with its own cloth, if there is none.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and examine well everything, and treat it as it should be treated, until it is healed perfectly.
des nous	of the nose
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	We have many methods among us, which I will say all are similar;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it is fitting that I tell all the difference that is between beginning and end.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that end is heat and fever remaining, until the ebullition has passed, and the corruption is completed;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	then restlessness of fever and heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the new one there is no heat or fever or pain, and contains the pus, which are its own sacs and correspond to the color of the flesh, and begins like a jaundice, and becomes swollen;
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and are according to its appearances, either fatty, or moist, and have many colors as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the nose, that you examine and inquire first through all the instrument which is called "interstice", according to what its form will be or the chapter which comes afterwards.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiring into abscesses is that you take a more moist place than you find within the abscess, and turn your two fingers in and out, so long as you know that the instruments have pierced the core, then it should be according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then extract the entromissoire, and take care that it does not jump away.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture comes forth quickly, regardless of its color, then do as I have said for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the entromissoire no moisture comes forth, know that it is hard, then do as I have said in a cross shape, and take hold of it with pinceures, and gently scrape off each part and watch the coat where it lies so you can lead out the pus without harm.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot pull it out whole, then pull it apart in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, then the wound comes back many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if there is still a little left and the blood grieves, then apply a wound with some corroding powders, and stop the bleeding, and put hot soothing things on the abscess, and cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the wound is large, then cut off both lips of the wound, and cure what remains with whatever flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the vein is contrary to you or another thing that hastens and applies vinegar mixed with vinegar, and lets it be for two days or three, until the wound purifies, and let the boiling of blood settle.
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then come back to closing what remains of the cut.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	Behold here the forms of the inner instruments, and they are of three manners:
grans et moien et petit;	large and middle-sized and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three squares which are called "albaret", one of which is called "breb", and there are three kinds:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	great, middle-sized, and small, in order to encircle the abscesses of fistula;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like the needles with which one sews sorcery, and they are of citrine stone, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are most proven for encircling the abscesses of fistula;
et sont de III manieres:	and there are three kinds:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	great, middle-sized, and small, according to the quantity of the breadth of the perforations.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The forms of the probes are of many likenesses, as you see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	large, medium, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and if there are those who have two kinds of three types also;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and if there are those who have three kinds of third type, and are also of three ways;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and if there are those who have two kinds, and some with only one kind, and are of three types;
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these is sharp, and there are some that do not cut more than from one side, for which we castrate the nerves, so that one cannot draw blood or touch the nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and from these instruments are made bandages that respond in strips, so that the patient does not feel them when opening abscesses.
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three kinds:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	large, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and don't use more force than in the natural joints, such as legs, arms, shoulders, and similar places;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling scissors for flintstones, according to this form, by which blood is staunched;
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and one puts it sometimes in the location where veins and arteries are healed completely, and sometimes according to this great form;
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men become inflamed when they begin to be corrupted, so that they seem like women's breasts;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and inflamed, and whoever wishes to cure them, it is necessary to boil according to this form of the line from b to g;
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with medicine injecting flesh, then close the two lips of the wound by stitching, and care for it until it is healed;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if the nipple points downwards and is concealed because of its great size like it has in women, so cut it into two folds above, by two similar incisions;
