de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one is attached to the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. up to line .g.;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then flay the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about dressing and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed or the incision is not entirely done because the patient will not rest or due to the bleeding of blood, then you must fill the wound with damp cotton in corrosive oil;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave him so long as he wastes away the remainder and fat, then cure him until he is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the armpits are kinds of hard scrofulae or those with nodules, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture need to be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess has been emptied, then fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and care for it with oil suitable to this purpose until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of the same kind as scrofulae, then cut it as we have said in incisions for scrofulae, and if the wound yields pus, then apply cauterization as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the arteries are blocked, and the skin above is bound together, so there often arise abscesses, and it happens just as frequently that a vein becomes inflamed and forms an abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one knows thus when it is due to the artery, then the abscesses are long in the back and front.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and when you feel it at your joints, then you feel a straining.
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and if it is due to the vein, then it appears as swelling.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolish to cover this abscess, and especially when it is under the armpits, in the groin, or at the neck and many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is then necessary to avoid the iron treatment, and the one who is at the head also needs to avoid it, and in the one who is swollen from artery trouble do not make a cut above the long skin.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then work on the shape so it becomes one with the skin, and gently separate the artery from the threads, until it is uncovered;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	then push a needle underneath the one, and make it pierce just to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread in two loops, according to what I have instructed you about the extraction of the two arteries that are in temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then insert the point that is between the two loops of an introducer until the blood flows out that is there, and loosen the abscess;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then apply the treatment as the bowstring tightens, until the bandage falls off;
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat those with ointment suitable for them, until they are healed;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	and if the abscess is due to the cutting of a vein, then it is necessary that you wet with your hand all that part of the skin where the abscess is, then push a needle underneath the point you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and let there be one double thread, so that you pull it from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	Then apply the aposteme, as I have told you, to one of the two parts at the two joints of the shoulder.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	And if you doubt that the thread will not come out, then replace another needle on all of the thread below the entire aposteme to the incision of the first needle, and hold the threads in four places.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then cut the aposteme until the excess comes out, then cut the excess of the cure and leave what is attached.
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put a damp cloth soaked in vinegar and oil on it, then administer poultices and ointments until he is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nails
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also just like abscesses come in the artery and vein, abscesses come on the nails when they are worn out or from excessive work and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this often happens at joints and in the shoulders and in all places where there are joints, and it is a grievous aposteme, and its color appears like the color of the flesh, and it occurs in many dispositions without pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when one constricts it strongly, then the patient feels pain, and is not entirely in the depths of the heart, but beneath the liver;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	and it is well from all sides, and does not go forward or backward, nor below or above, and he who is in joints does not consent to be cut by iron;
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	by chance there may be contraction;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and he who is in the head or on the forehead, forms the leather at the scapula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, one should take hold of it with forceps and cut its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, one should suspend it with a ligature, and scrape, then cut and reassemble the wound to the seam, and care for it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of large boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	At times it happens in bellies and not elsewhere so much, and it is a disease which is called "fungus" by its resemblance to those things, and it has subtle roots and a big head;
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	and there are both small and very great ones;
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw a man who had two on his belly that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had a small root, and they had split open and were oozing moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I copied them and found in one 18 ounces weighing, and in the other 6 ounces, and the work of incision is such that you consider whether the patient is moist, and the color of the articular flesh is white and moist and has a subtle root;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	if he cuts in the spatula-like area wide, and there are cauterizations with fire present before you.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For when cutting comes often too great flowing of blood, and if the blood overflows, then hasten to cauterize.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the iron incision, then take a well-made linen thread, and bind it to the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	and then restrain it, and do not cease to restrain the linen thread until it cuts through the artery, and let it be guided by its own work;
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	and if the roots are thick, then have fear not to cut it at all for the belly's sake, but you can well cut off the half, and then cauterize so that it does not revive;
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then treat the wound, and be sure to cut off the thread which is of a fuzzy color and has poor sensation and little regard.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an enchanted abscess, and I will come to the cure of chancres later.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil is full
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the boil comes from a wound or a split in the syphilitic abscess, and it is on the belly and is accompanied by some swelling, just as it happens in other ulcers, or from blood which flows from veins or arteries according to what has been said before, or from inflammation;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	et if it is due to the rusting of the sores and by the exit of the bowels, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and appears through various exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the discharge of the intestine, then it is much more diverse, and when one presses it at its base it swells up, and then returns, and by chance becomes hardened, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and through strong labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it's because of moisture, it's a light thing, and it shows well when you press it with your hand, not at all constraining.
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	and if it's because of blood, then it shows by these signs the abscess is large and hard, and it's fixed according to a quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it's because of windiness, then it is sensitive to the toucher, and the work is that you look to see if the appearance is due to blood from the artery, or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	You must leave off the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, because of the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the bowel, then it is necessary that you instruct the patient to hold his reins and be stretched out straight, then sign around the belly.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	Then instruct the patient to sit comfortably between your hands, then go around the joint you have marked for all the surrounding tissue, then cut off the top half of the abscess to the great unguent.
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	Then bind it around with a strong thread or a cord of strong silk tightly, and let the bow be thoroughly secured.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	Then work on the half of the abscess that extends over the bandage, and thrust your finger into it, and cut the intestine.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it caught on the bandage, then release it, and insert the intestine back into the belly.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	And if you find the bowel, take hold of it at the intestine, and cut away the superfluity.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	And if the artery or vein resists you, go around it gently, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert two threads into them, and tie the two needles around what you have done in a cross that you made pierce.
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then strain the abscess with four leaves above the needles; and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the leaf until it can bear, and let the dead flesh perish by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you cut it when it is subtle and can bear, then cure with whatever is needed, and leave the abscess as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the leaf with whatever is needed, and bind the leaf.
dou chancre	of the chancres
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have said in the section about ulcers, and how one should work with them by medicine, and how one should avoid iron treatment.
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	and say that ulcers in the groin are very bad and require great care in treatment, and the ancients said that when ulcers are on the leg or can be removed like those in the armpits, and in the crotch, and similar places, one should remove it all at the beginning when it starts.
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	and when it is great and old, you must not approach it, for I have never seen any healing from it;
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	no one has ever healed before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And the work, when it is in place or can be removed, as we have said, is that you purify the patient sometimes with black gall;
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	then make it healthy if it has evident fullness, then place the patient in good condition to do the work;
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	then throw out your clamps or chancre, and the hair from all parts, and the bone from all parts leaving nothing behind;
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and let the blood flow freely and press well on the place with your hand or something, and if the decoration of blood makes you contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, then cautery until the bleeding is stopped;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the doctor will treat another wound until they are healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have said in the division the likenesses of dropsy, and how the gathering of water is done, and the signs of each likeness, and the cure made by medicines, and that which is cured by fire.
si est eclites soulement;	if it is only illuminated;
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	and one should not touch with iron in these two likenesses:
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	it is to know, tympanitis and hydropsy, for it is mortal.
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	then when you are using medicines for this likeness of dropsy which is called "eclites" of medicines, and the cure does not help, then look to see if the patient is weak, or if they have another disease other than dropsy, such as diarrhea and similar things.
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	if one should not touch with iron, for there is doubt;
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	and if you see the patient with strong vigor, and he has no other disease except dropsy alone, and he is not too old nor too young, then thus you should proceed:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	hold the patient upright on your hands, and the attendants press the belly with water at the lowest part of the stomach, then take the spine thorn according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it cut to two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	to the point, and even if it is not so deep that it can reach just to the intestine when you insert it, and cannot harm it;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	then look to see if the dropsy is flowing towards the intestines:
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	then it is necessary that you cut on above of the third tooth, straight downwards from the lip;
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	and if the dropsy is due to the disease of the liver, then your incision should be on the left side of the third tooth;
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	and if it is due to laxity, whether to the right or not, and it is not necessary for the patient to lie over the fissure so that the superfluidities do not flow to that weak place;
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	then pierce the whole skin with the instrument, and stop it, and lift your hand away from all the spatula-like substance between the skin and the scab just as when trimming to the quantity of an eyelash or around;
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	then pierce the scab until the spatula-like substance comes to a natural outlet, and that is the exit of water, then wash it thoroughly, and put this instrument away, and that is its shape;
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	And it resembles a subtle silver chain, and it is of gold or light lead, and in the part below there is a small perforation;
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	and on one side, three perforations;
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	and he of another part, and one of another;
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	and the head is cut off like a feather, and it's the shape of the incision that writers make on a feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	at the top is the alembic, so that when instruments come to water, they now flow on the instrument;
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	then drain the half or third part, because if you drain more than is necessary at that hour, by chance the patient may die from the release of their soul from the wound, or they may fall into a faint, or approach death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	but drain it according to the quantity of their virtue, and according to what the patient's vital signs indicate, and their pulses;
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	then take the instrument and hold the water, and it is held now for the reason that stops the perforation which is above the syphac, of which I have spoken, so that you pierce in this manner;
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	Then resume using the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and take a small quantity of water.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	Do this any day, and be careful not to wash so long as there is still but a little water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	And if you doubt the patient, and leave too much water, so that the wound or sand becomes hot, and through excessive sweating or bathing and sun exposure, and it turns into drinking;
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	and treat with drying medications until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach, on the liver, and on the spleen after the extraction of water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the stopping of the urethra
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born who does not have a hernia in the genital area, or the hernia is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If he must then pierce through all the skin layers very subtly according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	then put the small plug of clay under him, and tie it and keep it thus for three or four days until he wants to make urine, then remove the plug, and let him urinate, and then put it back.
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	and by chance there is no need for it, because the urine that comes forth does not allow it to remain closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	That of whom the pustule is small, it is treated with a poultice of cloth, as we have said, and will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have the fistula in its place are wounded, because none are born with the fistula at the head of the penis, therefore they cannot urinate unless they lift their penis high.
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	and they cannot flow because the material cannot come just to the margin, and that is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the manner of the operation is that the patient lies often on his back, and then takes hold of the head of the penis and cuts it like the shape of a quill, so that the fistula opens in the middle, as it should.
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and beware of the flowing of blood that comes many times, and if it happens, then stop the bleeding with what stops blood, and care for the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	Of the pustules on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	Many times these things come to pass in the vulva, and there is an appearance of bad flesh.
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	and among them are malignant ones and not.
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	so it is necessary that you take them with subtle medicine, and cut and clean all of them, then apply damp cotton in Egyptian ointment.
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	then anoint with divine ointment until they are healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the boil is malignant, with foul odor and putrid color, then it is necessary that you apply a cauterization.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	When you have cut it off, and the excrescence is in the vulva, and some part is within the skin and some part outside, then it is necessary that you remove the excrescence which is inside first.
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	and when it is healed, then anoint the outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	For when you anoint it all together, it is not at all assured that the head of the vulva will not be pierced, and there will come blackness and corruption in its own vulva and on the skin.
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to heal all that is black and corrupted, then lay upon the plaster of honey and flour which is made from the rind of green apples and vetches, then cure with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding comes from it, so apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	The fire cauterizes in two dispositions together:
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	that is to say, by the purging of blood and by corruption;
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	and if the head of the foreskin is corrupted and retracted, then it is necessary that you tie or guide a piece of cloth to the foreskin, and make the patient urinate in between;
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	and when the skin is inflamed at the head of the foreskin which has not been circumcised, either due to wound or abscess, then it is necessary that you cut away with a sharp instrument, until the ligaments are loosened, and the head of the foreskin be released from all parts;
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	and if it is a great thing to divide them, then you should skin him at the spatiumile about a little below the head of the penis and scrotum;
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	then sever them nicely between two, and place a thin cloth of moistened linen in cold water, so that it will not stick again.
de la circoncision	Of Circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Circumcision is not the disconnection of continuity as with other wounds;
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	although we do this work of our own will and properly with children, it is necessary that we make the best and most gentle work for their salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancient ones did not speak of the circumcision of their children, because they do not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	For I have seen that the greatest part of masters and seniors who performed circumcision were around me, by force, and all alone.
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	so that the skin would break because there are two layers, and by chance if you cut the one above and leave the one below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	The wound recovers slowly, and there is doubled pain, and the member's tip is not assured at all.
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	and the abscess is cleaned by chance and escapes the iron, and the work runs, and many times it happens in this way that there is no need for cleaning and I have seen.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the mundification which is done with force I have found the goodness of experience, for the forces cut equally well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	For when you press your hand, if it is cut equally in all the fingers to the same length;
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	but that the thread be well tightened around the skin;
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	and the manner of the first work is such that you make the child think, if it understands, that you are only making him bind the thread around the rod, and then let it relax in all ways that you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	then make it stay between your hands straight, and reapply the forces between your hands or beneath your feet so that the child does not see them nor any of the instruments.
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	put your hand on the handle and blow or squeeze, and pull it up until the head of the handle is in place;
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	then clean it well from the dirt that is assembled there, then tie the place marked with a doubled thread, then tie it underneath one link and the other.
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	and hold it in place by the second thread at the pouch and the pointing finger, and cut between the two links, then lift the key above hastily and pull up the head of the handle.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	then let the blood flow little by little, because it is purging.
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put powder on top and on the powder a cloth glued with a hen's egg yolk cooked without water, mixed with rose oil good and fresh, and leave it on until the next day, and then treat it again as long as it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The form of the forces at the time of confluence thus is:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	the two heads should be held and pressed together, and the heads should also be as large as the hands in equal measure:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	the mistake at the time of confluence is when the humors inside flow during the incision;
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	therefore it is necessary that you spread it to your finger, so that the swelling makes an abscess;
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it to your finger, then hold it with forceps, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	And if they continue for three days, and what is under the scab is swollen, then let it be until the abscess is appeased, and scrape it lightly.
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	and cut as you can move, and take care of the part of the scab, so that it will not harm anything.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Cure then the joint of sudden injury from powder, which we have said or treated of powders, and if it is cut too much outside measure, and it goes above, so it will not harm.
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	of the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to stoning of the kidney, or blood congealed, or bladder, or new flesh, or similar things, which we have said in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to a stone or knot in the bladder or at the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary that the patient be bound on his knees.
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	and let their feet be placed on the back, and stretch his belly from above the back, and bind the patient's arms as tight as he can.
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and then the collar of the bladder is constrained to the expression of the stone above, so that the urine is loosened.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you should administer extraction with all the instruments that are called "syringe", which is this form:
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it should be a fine, thin, silver thread, like the quill of a bird.
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and it should be the length of a palm and a half, and fine at the head.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the manner of urination is that you take a doubled thread, and tie it at the head to a piece of linen or cotton, and insert the head of the thread into the syringe.
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and remove the excess of the linen and insert it just to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and hen's gall, and make the patient sit on a siege, and raise the bladder and the urethra with moist oil and olive oil and lukewarm water.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	Then put the syringe lightly on the vein, until it comes to the root of the vein, then fold the vein upwards towards the mouth.
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	Then insert the syringe almost to the bladder, and feel the patient's body come almost to the empty place, and this is not done according to this order unless because the guide or director of it is twisted.
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then draw out the thread slowly and slowly along all the woolly parts, and the urine follows the wool, then pull it further, and make the urine flow.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and begin the syringe again until the bladder is empty, and the patient be eased.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scorching or blood comes into the bladder, or putridity is assembled there, and you see distilled waters and medicines, then make all the instrument which is called "clepsedre", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It is closed, and if there are three perforations:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	One on one side, and one on the other, as you see;
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	and the warts fall out because the medicine is such that it stops well the vein without addition, so that one can draw out the moisture and insert when needed.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	and when you put your medicines in the bladder, place the head of the cauterizer in the moisture, and draw on the drawing that is inside.
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	if you pull out the moisture to the cauterizer, and then press hard on the drawing that is inside;
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	so the moister will go inside, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	and this is the form of subtle enema by which one enemas the bladder:
si est ci:	so that it is this;
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	And it is made of silver or archaust, and the head is higher up;
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	and below at the navel or where the bandage falls;
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	then take a sheep's bladder and put the moister in it that you use to enema the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts with a good double thread, and heat the pot over the fire on top of that moister.
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	then put the head of the catheter into the urethra, then strain your hand on the bladder to all the moisture that happens, until the patient feels that this moisture has reached the bladder;
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	and if you don't have a bladder, then take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it roundly around;
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	then put a strong thread into these perforations, then assemble the circle as one assembles a door, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument;
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and do as you have done with the bladder, by pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have said in the section the ways of stone, and the extraction together with medicines;
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	and I said the difference between a pierced stone and one that has been struck by rain, and all the signs, and in which stone one should work with a chisel;
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	and in the bladder, and in the urethra;
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stone that is lodged in the bladder happens more often to children, and it's a sign that the urine jumps out of the bladder resembling water in its subtlety.
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and I will advise heresy, and instruct the patient to scratch his penis, and he will do this many times, and then become inflamed.
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	and as a result of these jumps, foundations fall away;
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	and the recovery of children is light until they are 4 years old, and it is very grievous in old men, and it is in middle-aged people, who are between youth and old age.
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	and the cure is more light for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient through purgation, in order to draw out all the bad blood that is within the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often hinders from seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Take the patient by the feet, and lean him back and move him down below, so that the heel descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes comes out from a high place.
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	Then make him sit between your prepared hands, and his hands be below his thighs, so that the bladder is all leaning downwards.
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	Then question and touch it inside;
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	If you feel the stone in its place, then hasten now to cut on the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it does not yield to the touching at all, then moisten your two fingers with oil from your left hand, if the patient is feeble, or your middle finger, if the patient is young and accomplished.
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	and thrust it into its foundation, and question the stone, and when you feel it with your fingers, then apply it to the neck of the bladder.
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	Then press above on your kneecap, and bind it to the outer side away from where you will cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and tell him to stretch out with his right hand the membranes above, and with his left hand remove the skin that is below the membranes in the part where you will make the incision.
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Then bind the spatula tightly, so it forms:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	And make a space between what is between the membranes and the foundation, not in the middle but on the left side of the right flank.
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And be straight on the stone, and your knees should be at the foundation, and the incision should be wide on the outside and narrow within, according to the size of the stone, not too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	In case the pressure is such that the knee which is at the foundation jumps away without effort;
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	and know that there is such a stone where there are angles, and margins:
si est griés a issir;	so it is grey to issue;
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and if there is one that is worn out, resembling a flint, and rounded, from which the issue is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	To this then where it has angles and margins, make the cut larger;
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	and if it does not jump, then it is necessary that you strain on the pincers which are also like a file at the top, in order to strain the stone so that it does not escape;
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	or you put below the said instrument a subtle curved one at the top;
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	and if you cannot shape it thus, then enlarge the small hole and if the blood flows out, strain it with vinegar;
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	and if there are more than one stone, then insert the largest first at the neck of the bladder, then cut on top, then file it straight, and the small ones afterwards if there are several.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if she is very large, then it must be sewn, and a greater wound made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	Because two things happen to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	or he dies, or his urine flows forth soon after, as the flesh cannot heal;
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	but nonetheless force it with a file or chisel with pincers, until you cut it into pieces;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	and when you have completed your work, then apply the wound with frankincense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and cover it with a damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot aposteme;
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	then rewrap the patient on his neck, and do not untie the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you untie it, then rise up very well with oil and water, and then cure him with balsam of diaphaneikon and balsam of basilikeon, until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if hot apostemes come to the wound and ulcers, and congealing of blood in the bladder, and it stays the urine which is known in this manner as not leaping with the urine:
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	Then press your thumb into the wound, and draw out that blood, for if it remains, so will the bladder be corrupted, and it will perish.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then wash the wound with water and vinegar and silk, and aid him in all ways that you know, until he is healed.
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And it is necessary that all the works that you use to cure him, that you bind his two hips together, and assemble the medicines on the site.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	And if the stone is small, and it is in the urethra of the penis, stuck inside, and the urine cannot come out;
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	So do as I say then, cutting it many times, or excuse cutting for this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I've already experienced it thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron fork according to this shape and let it be fixed at three angles in one handle:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	Then take a thread and wrap it around the penis below the stone, so that it cannot come down into the bladder;
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	Then insert the forest (cauterizing iron) into the lighter limb, so it comes to the stone.
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	and turn the iron back to your hand in small strokes, little by little, until you can pierce the stone from the other side.
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	then soon the urine will come, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the limb.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	So it is then broken, and jumps forth with the urine, and the patient is cured.
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	and if you cannot do this for any reason that hinders it, then place one thread under the stone and another above, then make the limb meet the stone between the two threads, then pull it forth, and release the thread, and cleanse the congealed blood that is in the wound.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and heal him until he is sound.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	Stone is often lodged in women, and when it does occur, it is a grievous cure, and it is forbidden for three reasons:
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	One reason is that perhaps the woman is a virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	and the second reason is that one cannot find a well-informed woman who reveals herself to mirrors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	And the third reason is that perhaps one cannot find a well-informed woman in this art of surgery;
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	and the fourth reason is that the stone in the woman's body is more inwardly placed than the stone in a man's body, so one must make a deeper incision and there is great fear. And if necessity demands it, then you should take a well-informed midwife, and once you find one, she will guide you, and if you cannot find one, then choose a subtle midwife;
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	and the present one shows a wise woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and commands her to do what you command regarding the incision of stone;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and look closely if the woman is a virgin:
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then it is necessary to strengthen her dowry or foundation and seek out the stone;
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if she finds it, then she forces her to put the stone underneath her dowry, and commands her to strengthen her dowry with the patient, and presses her left hand strongly on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	If she finds it, then it is necessary to move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder down to below, until it comes to the root of the thigh;
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	then press on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the groin, where it is most manifest, and feel the stone in that part;
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	and does not move his two (joints) above or below the stone or soot, and is the size at first small.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	then bind the linen on the wound, if you feel the stone so close to the sore that the stone can come out further, and know that there are many kinds of stones:
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	it is to know, small and great and rough and smooth, long and rounded, and those which have ridges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	know the likenesses to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if the blood flows, then apply a glass-like powder to it, and keep it there for an hour until the blood is stanched.
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	then return to your work, until the stone is further out, and have the instruments that I told you about in the extraction of stones from men to help you in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	and if the blood flows, and it's from an artery that is cut, then apply powder to the wound and tie with tents and bandels, and do not re-start again, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, lest perhaps the patient would die.
puis cure la plaie.	Then heal the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed and the place has been dressed, then return to your work until the stone is out.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshly hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	Ramie's water is nothing other than a gathering of moisture or white mucus that lies beneath the skin of the groin, which contains the egg.
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	and it is called "white spawn", and never is properly contained in the eggshell if one believes that it is another egg.
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	and it is the skin of the groin between the white spawn that we have said.
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	and this does not happen unless.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the genesis of this Ramice is from weakness that comes to the scrotum, and spreads that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And never if it comes from percussion on the groin, and this moisture has many colors:
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	or it declines to yellow, or it is without red, or black, or watery white, and this happens more;
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to know this assembly, for if it is the white spawn that we have said, then there is the abscess swelling, as long as the shape of an egg, and does not open the groin, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the proper wool, it seems that the abscess rejoins with part of the egg, and so one thinks that it's another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white shin, he feels well;
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	Therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, examine all the surrounding quarters thoroughly, in order that the shape is as it was before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to these things then that come after the introitus, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we cure it with iron, it's necessary that the patient be cleansed according to his power and the replenishment of his body;
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	then apply a poultice on his back, on something slightly high, and place many cloths under him.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit on his left side, and instruct the attendant to sit on his right, and extend the beam onto one of the two sides of the skin of the testicles;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	Then take the spatula and let it lie on the skin between the long part until it reaches the nail, and make your incision straight while cutting through the skin of the scrotum just to where it becomes white, and scrape it subtly according to what is possible.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	Then pierce the scrotal skin with water at the largest opening, and extract all the water, and then put in your fingers, and cover the scrotum above.
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	and do not touch the skin of the scrotum, but only the scrotum itself;
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	cut it all or in small pieces yourself, as well, so subtly that it is on the other side, because if you do not cut it well, the water will come back;
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	and if the testicle jumps away from your work, then reset it in its place when you have finished the work on the scrotum;
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then gather up the two books of keys of joints to one seam, then care for it as for other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary that you bind the vessels that are suspended, fearing the depletion of blood.
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	then set the joint back to all its suspensions, and extract the egg, and care for it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if the water is gathered together in two parts together, know that they are two branches;
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	then set the other part in equal manner as you did the first, then stop the blood, and put a linen cloth moistened with rose oil into the wound.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put another linen cloth moistened with wine and oil on it, and set the two joints together, and put a doubled napkin over them, and tie it up all around according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	Then take two cloths, and employ them to be made of wool yarn according to this resemblance and let them be assembled by sewing in the girdle of the breeches, and one of the cloths takes place on the foundation up to the back, and the other at the part of the hand.
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	and the other two cloths take place on both armpits, and let all be assembled in a binding at the buckle of the breech.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and at times this medicine of cauterization takes place in lieu of iron cutting, and it is that you take a subtle cauterizing knife, and cut the skin of the scrotum, and let it be heated as we have said, so that the white syphilis-containing water descends.
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	so take the cauterizer according to this form, and pierce that white syphilis-containing water once, and scrape it off with this subtle hot cauterizer.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	And set the bone in all ways you can, until you have fixed everything.
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	and make sure that fire does not touch the egg;
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	and know that this work is more safe;
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	and beware of bleeding, and be careful with the works of cutting;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if nothing makes you contrary, or an abscess forms or bleeding occurs or anything else, then cure what makes you contrary, according to what is said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to endure this work because of its horribleness, then persuade perforation, as I tell you, and make sure that when you are certain through the signs we have said that the abscess is gone, sit the patient on a light bed.
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	then pierce the abscess in the part below all along the spine, and make the perforation as long as the body.
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	and let the ulcers be large, so that all the liquid runs freely;
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on the wound, and bind it, and let the remaining liquid flow out, then care for it until the wound is healed;
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	and if the white cloth does not let the liquid come out in the mouth of the wound, then it is necessary that you insert a pin or the instrument used to drain the water from dropsical patients, by which the swelling will be thus;
et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and enlarge the ulcer, and know that the liquid returns, and is assembled after six months or in as much as it was before, and when it is assembled like before, and thus will the patient spend their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the cutting of this reed, there is more fear than many preparations, because it seems to me that it is better to leave it alone;
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you about the work and similar things of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	I say then that many abscesses come from the body, and indeed also from the kidneys;
et c’est par mout de cas.	and this is by many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is to be known through excessive acidity and biliousness, which spreads to the kidneys, or from blows;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body;
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and there is no pain at all, and it is a grievous abscess;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and by chance some abscesses are grievous, pale and flabby, with a dull color, and sometimes it comes from the obstruction of an artery or the swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it's due to the obstruction of an artery, then it is known by the hot appearance of the abscess when you press it with your fingers;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and it does not behoove you to touch there.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	He who is skilled in the art of bleeding from a vein is known by his ability to express the pulse at the wrist, and can well perform the incision according to this likeness, and on other animals.
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you should cut open the shell of the egg, then lift it up and take out the yolk from above, and deliver the suspensory ligament from all parts of the yolk.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the egg is already softened with those juices, then it behooves you to take out the yolk and cut open.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is in the sac or in what is inside the vessels, then it behooves you to deliver all that tension and cut open again.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the scar is at the back, then it is necessary that you cut away all of it and extract the yolk, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, then dress the wound with damp linen in rose oil and wine, and then care for it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	This is an abscess enveloped in a wrapping similar to a fig leaf, with the softening of the shell, and the patient becomes grievously ill when he goes.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and the treatment of this disease is equally frightening as the one before, and yet we will tell you how to do it, according to what the old ones did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on an elevated seat, then put the suspensory device of the testicles down to your knees, to all the vessels that are near the penis, and take hold of them, and stretch them firmly.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	Then cut the spatula-like instrument sharply wide on either side of the vessels, until they are uncovered, and then scrape from each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in the temples.
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	Then insert an awl where there is the doubled thread, and tie it to the first place where the vein has come forth, and then tie it again at the other end.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then straighten out the skull in mid-division, according to the length of the body, and extract the corrupted moisture.
