et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize;	and when the medicine is inside, bind it with the instrument before with a strong thread, then purge.
et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	and be the medicine not too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the purge with oil or almond oil or egg yolk or similar thing, then put it in slightly.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	then press the ministers with both hands together until it is all empty, then pull out the purge, and lift up the patient's legs to the sky, and if the medicine wants to come out, so tighten it as much as it can.
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if he sleeps a whole night, then there is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you enema him in the illness of belly decoration, and the medicine hastens to come out, then repeat it until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are at the fundament or abscess, then the fistula is as subtle as for an infant.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and that is the form of the fistula which constrains the skin.
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have said in the division, the treatment of wounds;
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	and we will tell you the remedies by hand and by medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse depending on how they are made, and depending on the places or locations where the wounds are made, and according to how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by striking with stone, cutting with sword and knife or lance or club or arrow or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or that are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or back, or belly, or liver, and similar members;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and begin with simple head wounds, because the reminder comes in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, so be careful if it's from stone or similar things, and the skin is torn and the wound is great, and you lightly doubt hot apostema.
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	so make it heal quickly from the head itself if the wound comes forth with blood from the injury, and let the healing be contrary to the damaged part.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and instruct the patient to be full of wine and thick meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if it doesn't want to heal, then make his meat less, and don't let him drink wine, nor eat flesh.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound if there comes a hot apostema, a moist cloth in rose oil alone, or in wine stiptic.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no abscess hot, so he sets on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it has not been moved by air or powder that I will say a little more later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the fire has moved it, so he sets on some unguents, until it is cleansed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is great, such as a sword cut and similar ones, and the lips cannot come together by stitches, then bring them together with stitching, just as I will say about belly wounds, by stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is exposed to the bone and bleeds, and holds only by a small bit, then he should cut it off.
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	then he should treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh instead of skin, and instruct the patient to eat thick meats, such as testicles and cooked wheat, also like fowl, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find putrid flesh and it is not attached to the bone, then cut off all the putrid part, and pour away the pus, then treat it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, without delay, and it cannot be stopped by medications, then let the artery bleed, and if you find it severed, tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if that does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light:
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and that you put this powder which unites as soon as the ashes have cooled.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the manner of the powder is:
pren encens une partie;	take half a part;
sanc de dragon II parties;	dragon's blood two parts;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	take three parts of gall and mix it subtly, apply the wound and bind it firmly until it is well healed and joins with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then tie it well, and let it be without unwrapping, unless it swells;
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	because medicine is not abandoned until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with live coal only, when one has neither incense nor dragon's blood, but the air has disturbed the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the burn has changed the wound, even though it seems to be the same, do not put this powder on.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply some digestive ointments, or poultices made from barley flour mixed with water and honey, until it runs clear.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with other treatments until he is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the bone break comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you afterwards about the breaks of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there being no difference between that and one of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the navel, then there is no other remedy than to leave the wound alone and not put anything constricting on it, for it harms the navel and causes it to retract.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the navel is cold and its continuance with it is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	But let the medicine be thus mixed, as if chalz were washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and also washed the chalz in sweet water, and other minerals according to this manner, and moist anointings.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is great, then cut it and bind it with bandages, then treat it until he is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and the flesh is cut and full of pus, then pierce or make a deeper incision.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut and bleeding comes forth, then close it, tie it, and cauterize as necessary.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the gullet, and the conduit is blocked, by which the flesh flows, then cut the gullet on the neck of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural shape.
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then restrain it properly, and let it be for some days, then treat it with drying ointments until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, so it seeks.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and if there are pieces of bone, so treat them all as well as you can and those that you cannot, leave until the wound has healed, and let the opening be closed up.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, so powder it with the powder I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and it has a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of a lance or a sword
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a wound from a lance or sword, and the wound is deep, so examine whether there are signs of fever in the patient's pulse.
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	know then that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it is not deep, and it is fresh to all its blood, so do not put powder on it in the first hour, nor bind it at all for the blood that does not stay deep, but revives to the heart, and kills the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	but I mix an attractive ointment, and apply it twice a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you don't have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound three days, or four, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	if it doesn't come to vomiting, nor evil trembling of the heart nor excessive sweating from fever.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good conditions, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure it with tents and other remedies, until he is healed.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if she cannot heal, nor work, then know that there is a fistula.
si la cure si com on doit.	if you must do the cure as it should be done.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a cut or slash of a sword or knife, and it is simple, or worse on the back, then treat what is in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	If she is great, of sewing;
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	And if she is small, of powder; and if she is pressed into the bone, and has broken pieces, then one should cover the wound, and apply fires to those that are severed;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not severed, then let the wound remain to putrefy, so that it will ease the extractions;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and of other wounds on other members is the judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the belly are great and middle-sized and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from the great wound sometimes an intestine or a membrane of the intestines is torn, whereby their introduction is hindered;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the sewing is more troublesome, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the great one, therefore it is better to put in stitches gradually rather than all at once.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu'il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus à poinnes, et pour ceu vaut mieux les mouvoir li moieinne plaie, pour ceu c'on ramoine mues l'intestine à son lieu que aux autres II.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And you should know that the rupture of the belly is according to four manners:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	the two common wounds happen in the wound of the belly, and the wound of other body wounds and two other proper wounds are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and although they are more proper with the wound of the belly, I will say one by one and declare each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestine has come out, and a gentle thing is to be done, it is by one of the two manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are inflamed due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it up in this way:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	soak a sponge or cloth in hot water only, or cook one in boiling water with cypress and spikenard, and apply it to the intestines until the inflammation is removed.
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and at times make a wine restraining, and is good that has only one purpose to deflate.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the inflammation departing, then moisten the intestine with water or have it cooked with mullein and marshmallow, for by this is the entrance freed of almost all obstruction.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used for cutting off hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first remedy is to put a bandage on as one would on a wound, so that no one should cut there unless there is great necessity.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument for breaking:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if it cuts deep into the curvature and does not pass through, and you see where the shape is:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is expanded, and the intestines jump forth, then set it right again according to its natural form in its proper place, if you have the power, for this is good.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is wide and it is on the part below the belly, then you should make the patient lie on their back, and place their legs higher than their head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is on the part below the belly, then put the head and breast higher than the parts below, and also when there is an ulcer of the belly in one of the two parts, put your intention so that the wounded part is higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to administer what I say in great wounds and injuries.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	Put what appears small on the wound, then have in your hands the miserable minister who holds all the rags at his hand, and gather the lips.
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	and that is the common manner of stitches, and it is that you take a needle or several, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave at the head of the wound some space, and insert a needle where there is good strong thread.
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce the two keys of leather with the two keys of siphac, which is underneath the leather inside, as long as you make it pierce from that part, and gather the two heads of siphac together fourfold.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	then strain with a double thread around the needle in two parts, then gather the two edges of the wound properly, and then leave some space, and insert another needle.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	then tie the thread of the string just as you made the first needle, and do not stop making needles according to what you need them for until all wounds are restrained.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	and let the needles be moderate, between fine and thick, for the fine needles pierce through all flesh, and those that are too thick cannot enter well.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore it is necessary that they be moderate;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and it does not behoove to push the needles too far into the flesh and skin, lest they pierce and work the wound before the healing;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then cut off the ends of the needles, lest they disturb the patient while sleeping, and put threads or cloths on the ends of the needles to keep them in place, and leave them like that until the wound is healed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this way of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because it suffices to use one or two needles.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second suture is common, and it is that you join the two buttons of leather and the two buttons of skin together with a needle where there is one strong thread in between;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and when you have pierced these buttons all four together, then withdraw the needle from the part where you began, in the manner that one sews cloth;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put a space between each suture the thickness of a minor denier;
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	this suture is good for men, and I sewed a wound that one man had in his belly, which was wounded with a knife, and the wound was more than one palm long, and the intestines were two palms long, and the wound was inside the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been out for 24 hours, and the wound was closed in just 15 days, and I cared for it, and it healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the physician had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where one could not find any, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and put gauze on top of the wound two times a day, and wash it with honey water until it is healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and sew it from the outer part to the inner part;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	when it has pierced the corner in a straight line, then take the end of the thread or suture and pass it through to the other side of the inner part up to the outer part.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and the understanding of this suture is that you should sew as the furrier makes pelts, and that you leave once the thread on one side and pick it up again on the other, until the suture is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second manner of suture, which Galen says is proper, is such that some people do who assemble the two parts together naturally, and tie one end of the thread to another end in this way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Pierce an arrow or the tip of a needle nearby, and make it pierce only that point, and leave the two joints of the skin.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	Then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outer part up to that point inside, through the two joints of the skin.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Then make it pierce one and then the other from the outer part up to that point inside, in two other joints of the skin that are on the opposite side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	And this is the most natural way of stitching and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galens says this same thing, and many testify to it, so one should sew the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one should push one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew leather.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	and knows that when the rupture is within the belly, so is the cutting more grievous than at other places in the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgments of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, and if the burn has changed it, then restore the intestines, and the cloth;
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	then put powder on top of raw flesh, and if the burn has changed it, then put on any salve that is available, until the wound closes;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and sew the thread, and join the stitches, and the threads;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal the wound as with others, until it is healed;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and if you don't have medicine, then put on, as soon as it starts to close, old cloth, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	You don't need any other medicine for many injuries when the wounds are simple.
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	And if you doubt that the wound does not cause community with the main members, it is necessary to apply a small amount of linden oil at warm temperature, or rose oil, and place it around the wounds, and below the shoulders.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	And if he feels pain or purging in the bowels, and it happens many times, then purge with black wine tea, and similarly if the purging comes just to the intestine.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and let it penetrate inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is injured, and this is because of the plantiness of the veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the approach to its nature from the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the hernia jumps from the wound, then put it back in place just like the intestine, while it is fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	and if it is old and becomes green or black, then you must tie the part that is black, so that blood does not flow there, because there are veins and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	Then tie up what is between the ligament, and place the two bones hanging from the part below the wound until it reaches the end to ease extraction when the splints fall, and the wound is bound.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the belly
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestines are torn and the wound is small, then it can be restored in some people, because I saw that a man was wounded in the belly with a spear.
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it was the wound on the right side of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and there was diarrhea and flatulence.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated him accordingly as I could, and did not cease to refine the treatment until he was healed, and the abscess closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it close, I feared that the patient had a bad thing in his belly.
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no harm, but he remained in better condition, and eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and certain experimenters say that when one has a small wound in the intestine, he should be tied in such a way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	take fresh from great stones, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the plaster has opened the mouth, so put it on the two lips, so that it stretches its mouth up.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then bind the head, and it will stay so that he cannot undo it, then put another plaster after in that manner as before, until the wound is completely covered.
et cout la plaie.	and bandage the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	If the thread is applied to the intestine and causes no harm to the patient, and one can bind the intestine with a thin thread that is made from an animal's intestine, in such a way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	take the end of this thread of intestine that is well separated, and then tie at the end of this thread a thin linen thread twisted, then put the thread in the needle, and bind the intestine, and pull it back into its place.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of sewing of flesh is not far from according to the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, even when it is in one of the internal organs, there is no reason or health, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whatever
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it becomes inflamed, is universally called "fistula", and similarly when it breaks open and runs down.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is according to the greenish nodulation, hard and white, or where one does not feel pain, and it is also shorn like the feathers of a bird.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes in clear bowel, and at other times thick.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes thin, and at other times sufficient;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed and there is no flesh, except it is through one of the nine causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by the littleness of blood or body;
ou por sa malice;	because of his wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh inside and above the lips, which does not allow for new flesh to grow.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	because there is too much fat.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the skin is rotten and the matter is of poor quality.
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is a manner of plague;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property in the region delays digestion, and delays health, and flows by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and signs, and remedies of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	or it is necessary that I make you aware of the treatment for fistula which is done by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in every member of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	for there are fistulas that come from the great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or from the sinew, or from the intestine, or from the bladder, or from some of the ribs, or from the spine of the back, or from any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it comes to the property of the main member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the abscesses that are in this manner are of severe healing, and there is nothing but hard work, and lack of understanding;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if there is any abscess that does not come just to the place I said, and you have faith in the cure, and you recognize it, take a tent of earth or iron, if the abscess is straight, then dig.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if the abscess is twisted, then search for a subtle tent of lead, because the lead bends and wraps around the twistiness.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if the abscess has many openings and you cannot well search it with tents, then cleanse it through one of the openings, because the moisture is so short from one opening to another, and it purifies.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	then proceed with bleeding according to your skill, knowing if there is bone or nerve; and take note of the depth; and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you press on his arm with your hand, and where he feels it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you truly know the location where it is, and if it is far from a joint or nerve or artery or vein, or in any of the places I have told you, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove the false humors and corrupted matter that are inside.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	and then continue the treatment until it is healed, and if the fistula is well-filled with right matter, then it is necessary that you cut deep, as far as you can, then insert moist compresses in medicine aloe, and bind them up to the head of the fistula, so that the medicine may corrode the superfluity that remains at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then you apply poultices to the healthy skin, until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if it's not healed by that, then you cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the abscess, then you excise.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If vein or nerve does not grieve or main limbs, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, then you scrape it away until all the corruption is removed, then treat with poultices on the healthy skin until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if it's not healed and returns to its previous state as before, know that you are not yet at the end;
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	so uncover and seek until you reach the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then set it back in its place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it's thus healed, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If this is not so, know that the corruption is too deep inside, that you cannot come there.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other remedy except from the natural course of things;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can draw it out with forceps, then draw it out with an instrument suitable for this, and if there are many bones, then pull all of them out, without leaving even one;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if the moisture makes it difficult for you, and there is no error or fear, then cut through the moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then put on the wound a poultice causing putridity, and leave it until the pus has formed around the bones, and then the bones will come out more easily.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	and if it is a large bone, such as one from the leg or thigh, then remove only the corruption until all the blackened flesh is gone, then restore the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a great part of corruption in it, and comes just to the marrow of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	so it should be washed and covered all the way to the corruption, and then it should be cured until it is bound together;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you of a fistula that occurred in a man's leg, so that you may take it as an example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	He was a young man of about thirty years old, who had a pain in his leg due to a reason that came from within the body, so that the matter came out at the leg and became swollen with a big abscess, and there was no other way but to open it;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but the doctor, through their foolishness, overlapped so much that the abscess opened, and a lot of matter flowed out, and became a fistula, and there came a lot of pus that all poured down and moisture from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many doctors had taken care of him for two years, and there was no skill in the art of hands, until I was summoned, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated, and what flowed through the pores to great profit.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and became red the body of the youth, and had a citron color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of those tubules, and then searched all the tubules, and found that some were coming together in front of each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I hastened then, and cut into one of the pores as far as I discovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption came up to the bone inside.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I removed what appeared to me from the corrupted bone, and thought that there was no other corruption except for that which I had removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to restore the wound with medicines over a long time, and could not heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then began again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and removed it, and then removed it, and thought to close the place.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	But I couldn't bear to touch it except around a palm of bone, and the wound went all the way to its marrow, then I restored it with medications.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and he was healed and sound quickly, and it did not require further work except for the patient's weakness, who could not endure, and because of my fear of his death.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Because of the blood evacuation it often happened that one was healed completely, and in place of the bone a hard flesh arose, and it had good disposition and caused no harm or opposition whatsoever, neither when going up nor when coming down.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, then it must be set thus:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	take a linen and strain it to the open end of the bone, and have someone stretch it upwards;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and put another linen strip, a bit thicker than the first one, and tie it on top of the flesh that is below the bone, and stretch it upwards, so that you pull away the rotten flesh below, and uncover the flesh above where you want to set the bone, so that the bone does not harm the flesh.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place a hot iron or a heated tablet under the bone to cover the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to clean as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and to clean again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open up, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it, then uncover all the flesh.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then place a hot iron underneath, and then clean out the corruption from one part to another, and be sure to clean up as much of the long side of the corruption as possible, just as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut out the corrupted joint, and clean the bone where it contains from the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is no other way than to cut.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	and if the corruption is in the fingernail of the hand or the toenail, it is very strong that thing, but nonetheless you must inquire about that corrosion, how it appears;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in all the ways you can, but let the vein or nerve not hinder you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and know that the incisors and sutures for covering those bones are many, according to the structure of the bones and their appearance, and their size and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and therefore it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each kind of work;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art and the testimony of the ways of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If you think about the instrument you need according to what it is suitable for.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulder can be dislocated due to a cause inside or due to a cause outside.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	And when you have tried medicine to cure the corruption by treating with medicines, and it does not help, then it is necessary to cover that member up to where the corruption comes from, so that the patient escapes either death or the greater evil, which is the loss of the member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	And the signs are that the member becomes black, as if it were burned by fire, and afterwards it appears to be inflamed, then this corruption spreads from member to member, and takes hold throughout the body.
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	So hasten to apply a covering, and if it is due to the bite of some venomous beasts, such as sea scorpion, viper, and similar ones, if the corruption is in the head of the foot, then cover it, and do not give it space to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes just to the hand, so cut at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it comes to the arm, so cut at the elbow;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the elbow, that's deadly, and there is no remedy except for the quantity of his virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and so it does when the corrosion comes to the foot:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it comes to the first joint, then cut after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, then cut all the foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it mounts up the leg, then cut at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, then there is no other remedy except to let the patient die from lack of treatment;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the manner of cutting or sewing the member is that you tie it above and below, and stretch one minister down and another up, and you detach the flesh which is between the two ties with a spatula wide enough to reveal the bone;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	Then the surgeon takes the thread or silk, and places a linen cloth on each side of it, so that the thread does not touch the healthy skin, and another lesion and abscess will come to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if bleeding occurs while you work, then cauterize the wound hastily, or apply some restraining powders.
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then return to your medicine until it is complete, then bind the injured member with a suitable ligature, and care for it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to him at that time:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	he got a boil which seemed like burning fire, and that ulcer came first in his foot of the leg, until it consumed the whole leg.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the ulcer, he hastened to cover the leg, and was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and long time after it returned to him the corrosion or boil of the hand, and he came to me, and I put on him things responsive after the purification of the body, and he could not cease from the corrosion.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he asked me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of causing the matter to recur;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, because the vital force of the man was weak;
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he became desperate entirely, and returned to his land, and hastened to cut off his hand, and he was cured;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I don't know this story except because it is done on occasion when one has need of it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	No abscess ever comes to the fatty part of the body and remains so long that it makes a great gathering of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then they roast and pierce, and the bowstring snaps, and the light remains white, just as with vassals.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and the skin above is just as subtle as delicate drapery, and they do not run right to the bone, nor right to the nerve, and such diseases are called "sain", and are not called "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it comes right to the bone or very close, then it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is such that you cut all around it, and just as with delicate drapery;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it does not heal because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you have faith that the skin will heal, and the corruption is not in depth, and the skin is full of flesh, then treat it with a poultice thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Look if the breasts are large, and the bowels which follow are of a foul smell, then use the Egyptian medicine that is prepared thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Take lard, and oil, and litharge, in equal parts, and put them to cook in one vessel over the fire, until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey.
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	And then take of this mixture according to your need, and make it into water and honey, and use it as a pessary for the breast, and restrain the hernia.
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine remain for two hours, then strain it out saying.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the breasts are cleansed, and the foul odor is removed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and at no time use the water of ashes when this medicine is present, and it is that you take ash of vine wood, and pour water over it, then let it settle, and strain it, as long as you know that the breasts are well cleansed.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patient cannot tolerate it, nor Egyptian medicine nor ash water, so they liquefy with water and honey or add a little bit of lard.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	or you liquefy with honey and mead wine, so that the honey has the property to purify and cleanse, and the wine makes the blood flow.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and when you have done this, and you are sure that the skin is well purified, then liquefy with what brings forth flesh in it, and it is that you take defined ointment, and mix it with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you liquefy with some medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken the properties or to treat with ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and if the boil on the skin is small, and the catheter of the liquefaction cannot enter it, so you enlarge it with a little iron, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is enlarged.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the wound is too wide, so that only a small area at the edge or in the cleft can enter, and the purulent discharge that flows is above, then cut or move it below where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the pus is very deep, so that no flesh remains to become infected.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	And if you cannot cut the skin below as you see fit, arrange it in such a way that the pus flows down to the lowest part where it is, for when the pus is very deep, so that no flesh remains to become infected and if you cannot cut the skin below as you see fit, arrange it in this manner:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	so that the pus flows slowly down, and do not leave anything of the pus.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidative medicines to cover the wound, and place a cloth made of linen that covers all the wound.
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	After the wound in the breast area becomes larger than the first one, then apply ointment so that it is soft on another cloth according to the size of the wound, and place it on the wound in the breast to relieve the bowstring, and do not remove the large cloth until after many days once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	And the one who is on top of the wound in the breast area takes it away often to relieve the bowstring, and knows what comes from the bowstring, whether it's venom or pus or enough or undigested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and take heed if the patient feels pain or not, and if there's an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in this manner and you see nature bursting forth on the wound of the breast, then know that the breasts are already healing, and approaching health.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then loosen it in the morning or the third day, and when you open the wound, then change another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts discharge undigested breast after many days, know that the breasts are not hardened.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons come after a long time, do not despair at all of health, for the health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	There are men who tarry unnecessarily with pitch in their wounds, and those who do the opposite.
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if his stomach is indignant, it jumps out of his chest after many days, know that his chest will not heal;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if his chest is slow to heal and is far away, then add medicines that are wet in substance and dry in virtue, as ointment defines, for there is a great part of vitriol, and it's the last medicine.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take defined ointment, and mix it with rose oil, and add equal parts of old wine in substance;
puis le confit et en use;	then cook it and use it;
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and make the same thing with cooked honey, when defined ointment is not present, or take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind it, and powder it on the honey when it is over the fire;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and then in the cloth I apply a poultice, and stretch it over the chest, and sometimes administer a remedy that is aristolongue long, and roots of lysis celestial, which is also like flour of violets and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and in use of simples or compounds:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	crush them, and make powder, and put the honey I said on it, and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the wound is prolonged and not healed by this treatment, then know that corruption has penetrated deeply, and makes an impression on the bone, or in the hard parts of the limb, or in the tendons;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if it is a wound of a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the thumb.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Panniculus is an abscess that arises under the inguen of the armpit of the hand, or of the foot, or perhaps arises in other parts;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when it is neglected and one does not take care, so the abscess becomes inflamed, and runs and discharges pus as long as it will run its root to the bone, and by chance all.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes to the corrosion just to the bone, as long as it brings stinking pain, and is the shoulder joint wide, and is the color red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit at all, then it is necessary to remove all the superfluous flesh that remains of the finger, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauterization is a great help if the bone is sound, and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the nail presses against the flesh and begins to prick and bleed, it is necessary that you put a bandage under the nail that pricks the flesh, and bind it tight above, and cut away this flesh subtly and lightly, and put on the remaining flesh medicines burning and corrosive in order to remove all.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with ointments until he is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, so cut it, and remove the flesh, for as long as the bone is corrupted there, it cannot heal;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if you see the joint being corrupted, so cut into it as before said, then care for it until it is healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is inflamed, and swollen, and he feels great pain, so you must heal it first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	then cut the swelling on top of the spindle-shaped abscess by cutting across it, and be careful that the knife does not come to the flesh which is underneath the swelling, for the patient would feel too great pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, then put something on top that soothes;
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The vertebrae which are born in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshly, and by chance there is one or it has bones, and sometimes it has an angle, and one of these is born at the root of the jointure, or the birth is in some of the vertebra.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	He who is born in any part of the joint does not move, and he who is born at the joint of the joint moves by chance;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The size of one who is fat is light, in such a manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	the measurement is taken from the root of a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	He who is born in the root of the joint is grievous to cure:
si te tien dou coper.	if it holds too tight.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or has it in the back night, you should first cut away the fat around to the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable thread for them, then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The sores that come to the toes together come by birth, or by sudden wound, or by burning of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If you need to repair that wound, so that it should be restored according to its natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two tents or wet cloths soaked in rose oil, so that they do not stick together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two thin pieces of cloth, until the wound is sewn, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If sores come to any of his toes with the palm, then cut off that sore as is necessary.
des vils	of evil people
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Vessels are swollen and greatly inflamed with excessive melancholic humors that come to many members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more often occur in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary then that you administer to them sometimes purging with oil of cole, and then the remedy of the basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The ironing cure is according to two manners:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	One is how they bleed, and draw out the black blood.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And the other manner is that you open a vein, and drain it completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The cutting is according to this manner:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	First, rise the leg of hot water very strongly, until the great blood is thinned, then strain the patient's leg from above the hock joint to the part below the knee.
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then cut the vein in one place or two or three, with a wide incision, then lift and drain completely the black blood to your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the patient's virtues can withstand.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bind it, and command that he hold off eating meat until black blood flows freely;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and recommence evacuation and cleansing when the veins are empty, and it is harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The remedies for him are according to this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	wash the leg of the patient, if it has many hairs, then put him in the bath, and raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and fill the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, then heat him by the fire, and then cut into the vein at the long part of the thigh or in the area below the knee;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then apply ointment to the wound, and scrape the vein from each side, until it appears when you touch;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems just like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	After placing the splint below, so that it is raised from the skin, and then bend it to a light angle, and then place it in another position above three folds.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then skin the flesh above the vein until it appears, then lift it to the splint, just as you did, and bend it to another angle, just as you did first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	Then make another cut, or more if you need them, then lift it, and cut to the joint of the foot, then pull and lift up to the second angle.
