puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then stretch it from angle to angle, until it is all loose, then cut.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And if you can't pull and lift it, then put an awl on all the strong doubled thread, and tie and pull, and put below the splint, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and guard lest she copes, for if she copes, one cannot then draw or lift her, and harm comes to the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and when you have treated it all, put a moist cloth soaked in wine and rose oil on the location of the wound;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and care for him until he is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and bent together, and it's not straight, as we said, then you must cut it irregularly, but don't block it;
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron used to cut the vein is curved, and does not cut, so that it can open the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is of thick curvature, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is set in legs, in hot places where there are no herbs or tree, and on land where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and by chance it is elsewhere than in legs, and this happens because of the corruption that comes from below the skin, as serpents and worms are born inside the body and are set between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this flux are that it comes to the leg a very great inflammation, then the pustules change, and the flux begins to come out, just as a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the wound opens, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of cloth from one foot and a half to two feet, and tie it, and leave the cloth on the leg, and every time it becomes inflamed again, wrap it around the cloth, and tie it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part and wrap the remaining part, and do not cut it at its root until it is entirely removed.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, so it enters into the flesh, and brings forth an abscess and inflammation where it is, and a bad illness;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	for which reason it is necessary to treat it little by little up to the head, and leave nothing behind in the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	and it sometimes happens that this vein when treated with ten or twenty palms in length, and one man came to me, whose was twenty palms long, and when you cut it, so it bursts forth or becomes a perforation, and the incision goes all the way down to the bottom, so that everything flows out;
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and the matter inside is emptied, and bring back to its place medicines that prevent inflammation any day, then cure it as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And sometimes at this vein many streams flow forth, and even when it opens up in the joint of the foot or on the foot, and it comes out a great deal of pus, and from which it leaps.
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Heal then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Veins that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This illness is called in our land "disease of oxen", because it often afflicts oxen, and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body rising and falling, and one feels it well as it moves from limb to limb, until it bursts the skin where it goes, and jumps forth.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is caused by some bad humors, such as those that come from venomous creatures, worms, and lice or ascarids in the stomach.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and one doubts its wickedness, for when it goes through the body and rises to the head, and comes to the eye, by chance it enters and destroys the eye.
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and pulled out, one cannot escape except when it moves:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	If it is necessary then tie the place above and below with a strong cord tightly, then strike upon it and treat it well, and if the vein is deeply embedded in the flesh, and you cannot find it, then cauterize it with fire until it bursts.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it causes is that it runs to the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or near the eye, then hold a small circle firmly below it, then strike upon it and treat it well;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and it is necessary to use the patient with cleansing of the body by soluble medicines for wicked humors, and beware of unwholesome foods that cause corruption.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	from the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to some members, and can move from member to member;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was summoned to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm.
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and after that, I saw it rising as quickly as a worm on the shoulder, even sooner than anything, like living silver when it cuts from one place to another.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain departed from that place and settled in the shoulder, and then a little later it ran throughout the body, until it reached the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it was circling around the body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very surprised how she moved thus from member to member, for I had never seen this disease in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	However, I had always thought that the pain would move from one place to another, but I did not see it, just as I saw it in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought that it was because the woman had a thin body and her veins were uncovered, and because of this the appearance of forced constriction appeared.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and they do not appear according to this reason to those who are healthy, and who have moist bodies and veins responded.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens up as we have said, then bind it above and below hastily, and then strike on top so that those vapors are constrained to return.
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the joint;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it to your eyes, then use the remedy of those who restrain vapors, such as stinking pills, and viper pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they fall.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of their kind is that there are those who have great points, small ones, and bearded, and soldered.
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those who have two angles, and of those who have tongues, and of those which are in pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and that which falls in any member if it falls according to two manners:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in principal members such as brain, heart, liver, womb, reins, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls then in any place of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you next, warn you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	so it is necessary that you beware of the extraction of this arrow, for death comes after in many dispositions;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad sign does not warn you at all, and the arrow is not very deep, then treat it, and care for the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the brain when the arrow hits and pierces the bone, and jumps the sphenoid which is above the brain, is when it causes scotoma, swelling, vertigo, and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and mixture of understanding, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perchance it lacks force of the nostrils, or of the ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it affects the speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and jumps out of the white moist wound like pustules, and similarly bursts forth as if in a boil;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if you notice this sign, then hold back from the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is not stuck.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it is stuck in the heart, are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were driven into something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the arrow becomes motionless like boils, and with dark bloody discharge, and brings coldness and cold sweat, and a fainting spell.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then know with certainty that death is impending.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that strikes the liver is that without foam it bursts forth from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's face turns color, and he sighs high and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow hits in the covering of the chest, then it is near the small ribs;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and it gives great alarm and great pain and sighs;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and all the members of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow hits the stomach, perhaps something from undigested food bursts forth from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow hits the belly, and bursts forth a small amount of pus through the intestine route, there is no hope for the cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow hits the bladder, and the urine jumps and comes out, and the patient feels very much pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	knows that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and the neck and the throat and the shoulders and the shoulder blade and the spine of the back and the nape and the hips and the knees and the feet, and similar members, are safe according to many dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to one man whose arrow hit the well in the root of the neck:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and pulled it out on the other side under the ear fat, and he was healed without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And I pulled out an arrow that had hit in the fat of the eye under the paper underneath, and the arrow was bent, and could not be pulled out except for the point towards it, and the arrow was as big as a Turkish bowstring, easy to pull without ears;
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The patient was healed, and no bad accident befell him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And extract an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrowhead is Arabic-tipped at the ear.
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I extracted the splinter, and refined it to such an extent that I pulled it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And extract an arrow from a man whose belly had been pierced by it, and who thought he was dying;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then, after passing thirty days, his condition did not change at all.
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrowhead, and extracted it, and pulled it out, without any bad accident occurring.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if the man to whom an arrow fell on his back has a wound that is stitched up above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the arrowhead remained inside him, and his natural disposition did not change at all, nor did he find any harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I saw another man, to whom an arrow struck his face, and was stitched the wound.
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and remained thus without suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many others similar.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And treated an arrow wound on the king's man, who had been hit in the leg and was slightly bent to the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was fully embedded.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to the treatment after it had been struck three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I searched for it in every subtle manner and did not feel it;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt piercing and pain below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the point of the arrow I applied a poultice on the spot to attract and digest, because the swelling did not grow.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the bowstring of the arrow appeared to me.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I put the ointment on it many days, and healed the wound above, and so the patient remained long, until he felt the arrow one day inside his house.
et il le me dist.	and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I put on the wound a medicinal agent with corrosive properties for many days, until it was open, and I tested it, and felt the head of the arrow which was fixed in its place.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I pressed into the opening of the wound with that medicinal agent, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and it crossed the boundaries for about 4 months, and then it abscessed so that I put in forceps, and pulled it from one side and the other, and could not come out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Then I did not cease to invent and devise various ways of instruments, until I took it the next day with well-made forceps, according to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, as long as I carried it and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the physicians judge that the nasal cartilage cannot restore:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was closed, and the patient was entirely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you put your care in what I do not say, for books cannot take it all;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but wise masters compare a little with a great thing, and find nine works and nine instruments for the descending of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not exit the limbs where they are fixed except by two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the entry point where they enter, or through another place;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumps out by the side where it enters is an arrow entering a fatty organ, and sometimes it jumps out now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it doesn't jump out now, then leave it until the fat is cleared around, and loosen the exit point;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it's stuck in the bone and can't come out, then leave it like that for some days, and move each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it jumps out, and if it doesn't jump out, then pierce around with a very fine instrument, until the surrounding fat is widened, and then extract it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is stuck in the skull bone and goes just to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said befall the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If one does not pull it out, but leaves it until it is equal after some days, for if the arrow comes so close that it breaks through, it is deadly.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not come close to the sacral bone, and the patient remains some days without a bad accident, then it is expedient to pull out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is very well embedded and cannot come out further, then administer herbs around, as I told you.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the joint until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is stuck in the body and cannot be seen, then search for it throughout the tent.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then pull it out with any suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then cut it so that the wound becomes large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears on which it holds, then remove the flesh that is stuck for two parts up to where you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, until you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully make sure you don't break the arrow, but rather draw it more tightly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't all at once, then leave it until the flesh around is melted, and then pull it out, for the extraction will be eased.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flowing of blood makes you opposed, then follow what we have said in its chapter about the treatment.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and beware of cutting the nerve and vein, and consider how you can pull out the arrow without danger, either soon or late, or firmly or gently.
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and place the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow hit him, for that is the greatest aid there can be, and if you cannot do so, then put him as the signs show you should.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another side, if it leaves anything of itself behind, or the skin is swollen where one can see or sense it.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	cut then above, until the forceps can take hold, and then pull it out.
si saut fuer maintenant.	If it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if she cannot come out, then let her stay a bit longer and then start extracting again until she comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the arrow is stuck in it, then push it all the way through.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if the arrow falls, and you see fit to administer poultice, then administer an instrument that is hairy, so that the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then push through, and if the arrow is stuck, then push the instrument with the entering point into it, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is stuck, so you should cut away all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as it needs to be treated.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow falls or breaks or is in the stomach or bladder or chest, and it is nearby, and you can cover over it, then cover it.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and take care not to cut the vein or nerve, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and the treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps with which one treats arrows are similar to a bird's beak, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	great, small, and tiny, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is also like the plumage of a bird, to push against the tip of the arrow, as it is shaped:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the forceps for pushing and for pulling out if it is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	There are thirty-one veins for healing, out of which sixteen are in the head, that is to say:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two veins that are behind the ears, which are called the "herbech" pair;
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and two arteries that are in both temples appearing;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the inner corners of both eyes, which are called "aspirés";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the back of the neck;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and two veins that are in the throat;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and two veins that are on the upper lip above the mouth, and these are called "augeherich";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and there are two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins which we commonly use are those in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, and it is on the left side of the chest, and people commonly call it "the vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the middle one is called "femoral", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and people commonly call it "the vein of the heart";
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilic is on the right side, and people commonly call it "the vein of the belly", and it is above the fibula, and it is that one which we use when bleeding, which opens up clearly above the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the saphenous vein is the one that is between the wrist and the ankle, and it has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and foot are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	One is under the curvature of the pouch of the left side, and the second is at the ankle of the right side.
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein called "nesse" that is in the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The vein of the veins that are after the ears so helps the ancient cathars and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the quality of the bleeding is such as I tell you, and it is that you lift the head of the patient and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then tighten the patient's neck with a string, until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places dependent on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	which then returns to your thumb, and where you feel the pulsation below your thumb, then press down;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Then take the lancet, and thrust it under the vein until you reach the bone, then lift your hand up to all of the vein above, and cut and loosen the skin and the vein well so that you can traverse it, and make blood come out until you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then strain and bind it, until it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already spoken of incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The veins of the two arteries that are in the two temples, are worth for an old headache, and sode, and accustomed ophthalmia, and to the eyes that are filled with aged tears.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the blood are such as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient strains his neck, until the two veins appear openly.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pulse below your shoulder, and then signs to cease;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	Then lift the key on the vein above to your two fingers, and put the lancet underneath, and lift the vein up and cut it, just as you did in two other veins, and make the wound bleed according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then release the patient, and place your two fingers on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on top.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then bind it firmly, and let it be until it is healed;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have spoken of their cutting and extraction, at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The vein on the forehead is worth just as much as the cephalic vein for diseases of the face, ancient migraines, and rashes.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and its quality is that the patient strains his neck in twisting, until the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument called "fossor", which has this shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And put the point on the vein, and press down with your hand or something else, and let two drops of blood come out according to how much you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then loosen the patient's neck and tie the vein until it is well-bled and not once does a wide flame appear.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, it is not fitting that the flames be too large;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and let it bleed across, because the bone is near, and by chance break the blood flow when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The blood from the two veins that are in the armpits so helps the eyes, and the pustule, and the rubor, and the oriel in the eye, and the diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their blood is such that the patient stretches his neck by twisting some ligament, just as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then health, and let the wound be of the traverse, a little bit long of the flame, a little wide, for there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flames are subtle, by chance they will break.
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	Then make a bandage of blood, as much as you need it, and then bind on cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The blood of the vein of the neck is valuable for ague, and for excessive sweating, and for facial diseases, such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, and especially when it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the quality of the blood is that the patient strangles his neck, then strains his head to the left hand side, and takes the subtle long flame, and inserts it into the gap between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well there, and the blood will begin to flow now.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too far into depth, and make a bandage with blood according to your necessity, then tie it for one night, because it is very quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The sap of the two gum trees greatly helps in the tightening of the vein, and at the beginning of inflammation, and with many diseases, and with swelling, and with corrosion, and with sores, and boils;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the sap is that the patient stretches their neck between one and the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and let the master be standing on the head of the patient, and the patient take a seat, then open the vein of the long one a little bit wide, then draw out the blood temperately, or as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then repair the other side on the other vein, then loosen the ligament, and hold it gently with moderate pressure so that the patient does not choke;
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and let him be until morning, when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the healing of books
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The vein of the veins above the lips so helps in bleeding in the mouth, and in corruption of gums, and splits in lips, and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of healing is to have the patient sit before you and hold his neck as I said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by their black color and by the small black veins around them;
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	then cut one and the other, and if you don't recognize them and are in doubt, then cut the thicker one on each side, and do the same with both veins above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the healing below the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The wound of the veins that are under the tongue so helps after the wounding of the cephalic vein, and it is at the constriction of the throat, and with mouth diseases, and with eye diseases.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of the wounder are that the patient takes between your hands before the sun, and lifts up their tongue, and gazes downward in each corner at a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	heal then both of them, and do not go too far into the depth, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the throat that are commonly cured are cured in two manners:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or with a blow of all the flame mercurial large, or olive subtle as cutters cutting, and it is called "anasil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are large and subtle according to the largeness and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the fine gash is very renowned, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	It is necessary to have a device for opening veins which are full of thick blood that appears on the surface and contain thick blood and turmoil.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of olive oil.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtly pointed, and is for bleeding the subtle veins where there is subtle yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are under the throat, and at the neck, and at the breast, and at the belly.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the surgeon to bleed profusely, and to beware of the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and a great flow of blood comes forth, it is necessary to staunch it, as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and one must not pierce the flame, but rather cut as with a sickle.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open clearly, it is necessary that you manipulate it, and change another.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	where you want any blood to come from him, or you let a vein open up in his arm instead:
elle apert manifestement;	it appears obviously;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the skin of the ankle is numb, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to know the place of the vein, then it is necessary that you stretch out the arm, and touch the place until you feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place of incision, and then bind the arm, and open up the vein at the numb ankle.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and watch that you do not hit the artery when you see the place inflamed, for it is of the artery:
eschui la donques.	then avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it come out at the top like a child's urine, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is blood from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	 Hurry then, and place your knife on lengthwise, then remove your knife when the blood is still, as it often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	if he takes up his arm, and leaves it thus, and does not move the patient's arm;
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be on fear, and do not move the patient until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the blood is not staunched, and he complains, and medicine is not present to you, then cut the artery if it opens, because the head of the vessel will shrink.
et estainche li sans.	and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a wrapping of linen, and cut it, and take one half and bind it on well until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if the bleeding stops, that is good;
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if not, then cure it as we have said, with powders that stop blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the swelling is not at all diminished in many dispositions due to the small size of the wound, and the force of the ligament of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The vein in the arm is so well-aided that it bleeds from the head above and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it is necessary for the surgeon to be wary of the nerve that is below, and if he goes too deep, he will find the nerve, and it will swell and the bleeding will cease, and by chance cannot heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in certain men due to its subtlety, then it is necessary that you close the veins with the instrument anusil.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and avoid hitting the nerve at your peril.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The surgical treatment of the cephalic vein helps, which draws blood from the head and assists with healing.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary to bleed into the olive vein or the myrtle vein, for this is the most saving of all veins, because there are no nerves nor arteries beneath.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to seek the lighter place, and do not distress anything if it does not work the first time, and one recommences.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance the places swell in some people, when one tries the first time, but it does not distress anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the vein is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that bleeding is ordered only to preserve health and to forestall future illnesses.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and let the bleeding be done in one of the three veins that are on the forehead:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	It is to know, cephalic, swift, and basilica;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should purify oneself at the beginning of prayer in summer, and after eating in autumn and winter when signs of repletion appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one should purify oneself on the first day or the third, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The purification that is administered against diseases has no fixed duration, but whenever need arises by day or night, in all hours and at all times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not necessary to purify children until they are 14 years old, nor a woman carrying fruit except for less than seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the elderly who have passed 60 years not be cauterized.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when someone wants to purify themselves, in whatever way it may be, it is necessary that he cleanse the intestines with a gentle enema, if they have many retained farts, so that the veins do not attract superfluous substances from the intestines which are harmful to the main members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	That which is too full of meats does not heal well, nor one who is drunk, until he is sober again, nor dropsical.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And one does not heal well after passion, and vomiting, and purging of the belly, and frequenting with women, and toil, watching, and worrying, and all that comes from a fault in virtue, or through something of arm or body.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then balance the humors, if the blood is thick, by means of foods and drinks and medicines, if you have the power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	Then enter a bath, if nothing hinders you, to subtlety the blood, and to heal the wound around the third rib, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep that day free from labor, and toil, and lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and be calm and joyful, and let the surgeon be higher than the one being operated on, and stroke the arm two or three times, then loosen the ligament above gradually, because when it is too tight or loose, blood cannot flow.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then stroke the joint with hands, until the veins swell, and feel it;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	then moisten the surgeon's hand with an old piece of oil, then put his left hand's thumb on the vein below the joint a little bit where he wants to cut, so that the vein does not collapse and fail from being cut.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flow like strings to the surgeon, and those that are full of windiness, so that when one puts the flame upon them, the flame retires, and cannot open the vein, and thus it is with such people.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if the vein is opened too much, then the wound is too narrow, therefore it is necessary that the surgeons be informed about these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens for the first time, it's good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	if not, then it recommences again a little below or above that place, if the swelling is not present.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the swelling is present and the patient is frightened, let it stay one or two days and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	in case an abscess may form;
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	do not enter the bath, then the healing begins again if it pleases him;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the wound is small, or the blood flows subtly and you doubt that it will not bleed as much as you see, then trust in that same wound to flow right throughout.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and work with some haste, yet when the swelling subsides;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for it often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the joint swelling, do not recommence the bleeding, and put on a little bit of oil, for it lightens the body's blood, and is good in this joint with the mixture of oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the oil mixture to each wound that you treat veins for to stem the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and the same thing is done with a triangle and a bow of eyes when one puts it on the joint;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	so that the blood flows and separates when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there comes a great abscess, which often happens especially when it is not cleansed except at that time or the opening of the vein is small, so hasten and put on the joint a moist sponge in water and a little warm, and restrain it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the issue of blood from the vein, and if it remains at its place for several days with no blackness or greenness, then it does not harm him.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put on top something of aloes or myrrh mixed with camphor, ointment, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And often there occurs abscess and swelling at the joint of the temple.
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	put then your hand on it, and if you find the place soft to the pressure of the hand, that is the bad swelling.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Therefore do not put on top anything of what we have said, for by chance there is a cut short of the artery.
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but make it dry with an embalming agent to harden the place, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each blood according to its quantity and virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	Since the blood is black, let it flow out until it is red.
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	And if you see pus, let it drain off until it becomes subtle.
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for the person who is weak and feeble, and has need of bloodletting, to make a larger wound, and have the incisions wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for someone who is feeble, do the opposite, and make them well gradually and often, and one should heal them by cutting across, not piercing.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this way of healing is preserved from the disfigurement of blood and the compression of nerves, and it is more effective than the healing of a long or wide wound.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And for the person whose body needs healing, it is necessary to give moist bread in apple juice.
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If he is fevered, treat with blood three times or four. And if he has a cold complexion, bleed him before the surgery and use a moist poultice in a sweet syrup, or in a syrup of aromatic honey with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he beats on the vein, after a lot of blood has come out, it is necessary that he drinks pottage made from bones, and subtle fragrant syrup, and uses other things that we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to blow on his arm and heal another time, it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bleeding, that he heals little by little, according to the quantity of his continued virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to blow on his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, then heals in 7 hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to heal on another side, then should heal on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For there is much blood inside the body that is already fevered, and it brings on a fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	if it needs to be bled out in large quantities, and to dilate the pore so that it can reach as far as the navel;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	then you will reward all the conditions of health, and place your hand on his pulse as he recovers, so that death does not come in lieu of navel, and this happens many times when the surgeon is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it's not necessary when you see loosen the arm, and make blood come out the second time, and the pore is closed, that you press strongly there;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If he is bent, let him stretch out his arm quickly, for it would be wrong.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but let him leave it until it heals the second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you puncture at the tip of the flame until the blood that has congealed comes out through the vein and put a poultice on it and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, then let it be and do not constrict it, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity demands drawing out blood a second time, then let it be done in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein on the arm is healed at the site of the wound because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of healing is that the patient dips his hand in hot water until the scab is red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then bind it moderately so that the vein opens well, then heal it now by piercing across, not along or lengthwise.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the wound be wide, and heal it well near the joint of the hand, and if the blood does not come out, then put the hand in hot water again, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in winter, then do not put the hand in hot water at all, for it stays colder than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the vein of this wound is safer than all other wounds, for there is no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The vein of the gallbladder on the right hand side is worth more than all other diseases of the liver, and this is how:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	strain the hand and put it in hot water until the vein is emptied, if one sees it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the vein crosses over, and you cut it from end to end, then nothing will hurt.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and don't go too far in depth, for the nerves are underneath all the stripped flesh, and then put the hand in hot water if the abscess is frozen in the wound and can't come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have bled the blood as much as is needed, then put oil and seal on the vein to close it quickly, and do the same with each section.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The wound on the left hand side is worth as much to the disease of mice as it is to the illness of the right side; and does just as I told you there.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The wound of the Sophene is worth to all the diseases that are beneath the body, such as diseases of the marrow, and retention of flowers, and disease of the reins, and of the hips and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the qualities of his urine are such that the patient pours their foot into hot water, and rubs on the vein until it bleeds, and lies above the ankle joint.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the vein is at the ankle, and from above the foot they go out much water.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	then the urine will be either more abundant or larger drops or at the ankle, which is worth more.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you take the urine from the foot, then beware of the worms that are below, and the urine should also pass as it is in cutting.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the flames be extinguished.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the pus cannot come out, then put the foot in water and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the urine fails the first time, then it should start again a little above, because the bone is salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	nor doubt of nerve, as we have said, and thus do the same to the other foot in equal manner.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The flesh of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of force, and its incision is worth to the pain of the haunch when it's for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the qualities of his blood are such that the patient goes into a bath and strains above the ankle four times while twisting, because otherwise the vein does not open.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it opens, let blood flow in all ways that you can, and crossing over;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and be careful to stop it, for the wound is clean, and it has been opened to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not stop it, let blood flow from the part that opens on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and take care of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and let as much blood flow as you see, and then untie the bandage, and put on a cloth and bind it tightly;
ele est maintenant sanee.	it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	Of purgations by suction
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Poultices are made from horns, or earth, or glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and ventosity is done in two manners:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	or by wounding and drawing blood, or without wounding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this ventosity which is without wounding is done in two manners:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	or it is all fire, or not on fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and ventosity which is done by wounding and drawing blood is done in 14 parts of the body, one of which is all on the top of the head;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the others are in the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two others in both sides of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the ventosity below the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the ventosity between the shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the ventosity above the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the ventosities in both arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the ventosities in both legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the poultices of the two ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and the bleeding is not treated with blood, except for small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh, and therefore it has not weakened anyone much, just as one does when treating a wound;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not necessary that it be administered, nor at all fire or sense of fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if due to necessity of diseases it is necessary to bleed, or for habits, then we should administer each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and every time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they need to bleed, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if there are those who become replete and ruddy in their face, and on their head, and at the neck, and darken around the eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and are bleeding;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are such people who think, and see by looking at blood and injured and dead and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it's during the month, we order them to bleed after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The mixture of the medicine helps with the headache that comes to the eyes and does not belong after the evacuation of the whole body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this purgation is instead of the medicine for the head, and does not belong to someone who has a cold complexion or has cathartic, for it would do them very great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and therefore it does not belong to the elderly or those who have cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often bleed themselves become forgetful, and because of this it's necessary to put the venesection a little lower due to the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The purgation in the neck is instead of the medicine for the head and the throat, and therefore it is good for constriction of the belly, and for opening of the channel of the womb, and for all, and for repletion.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is necessary to press gently, for if she holds too tightly, so one incurs obstruction of the bowel or stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The vapors of the two chest cavities of the neck are equal to the pains of the head, and obtalmia and emigration, and strangulation, and pain in the roots of the teeth, and it is in the place of the health of the basilica.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is necessary that you instruct the patient to stretch out their hand to put down, lest they compress the artery and let forth streams of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The vapors below the chin are equal to sickness of the mouth, and corruption of gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and it is in the place of the health of the two lips.
