Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The venesections of the shoulders are worth for diseases that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The vapors of the sides are equal to those of three veins of the arm, for they bring forth blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and command the surgeon not to cut too deeply by fontanelle, for the bones are full of flesh, and there is knowledge below nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The poultice that is on the buttocks is good for hemorrhoids of the fundament, and for diseases beneath, and it is necessary that the poultice be large and made of earth, so that it can do well in drawing.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and by chance, if she were subtle, she would break;
et i fai grans plaies.	and would make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The poultices of the legs are very good, for they draw blood from all the body, and are valuable for old pains in the reins, and kidneys, and bladder, and restore flowers.
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and are in place of the two soffens, and the two shins, and yet they enfeeble the body after long use, and bring forth faintness in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The way to put the poultice is that you put it first empty, and then suck it temporarily, and put it quickly, and move it equally, and do not stop doing so, until you see the red place and swollen, and appear the red of blood.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then be bold, and put on poultices, and take heed of the condition of bodies, for there are some who have tough flesh, and clear pores.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	It is necessary to wound only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and one a little deep.
et suce legierement.	and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to wound twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to subtlety open the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to wound a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to draw out a little blood little by little, if we can only suffer it once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want much blood, if we often start again;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the blood is thick, then pierce it deep, and make sure that the veins are pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for those who have hard skin and are robust, with numerous pores, that you anoint the sores of the oil drops which are appetizing and dissolving.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or seed of cucumber oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in winter, with oil of wormwood, or lily, or chamomile, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the surplus is large and cold, then take bitter oil, or balm oil, or aniseed oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person has tender skin and large pores, there is no need to put oil on them, but it is necessary to wash afterwards with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And the one who has much moisture, should rise up with ease, or with water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have excessive swelling rise from old wine, or water of sycamore, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and it does not become well without a poultice before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath an hour or two;
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it does not sleep after the poulticing, and it is necessary that he be warned, when he should be poulticed and when he is being poulticed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware of him who is healing is choleric, and his blood is too hot and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	so it is necessary that he take cold things, such as pomegranate seeds and endive and lettuce at ease, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and drink a little, and hare's flesh, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, so take honey syrup, and scented wine of medium age, which is between old and new, and drink little, and drink a little, and eat small birds and small capon.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and when he gets winded, so must he drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some men at times treacle or muscat before the ventosation, or after, to comfort the main members.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the blood be thinned out, but it is not necessary for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The cupping glasses that are applied without hurting are those that are applied on the liver, and on the belly, and podagra, and on the stomach and bowels and reins and hip, for those members do not tolerate being hurt elsewhere, and one does it only to draw blood from member to member, just as we apply them to the breasts when milk flows.
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to remove the viscosity that is in the member, just as we apply cupping glasses to the stomach and bowels to reduce the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and stops the pain when there is ulceration or stone, if it stops by its attractive virtue by chance the ulceration, or removes the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and thus it is done when one applies it to the liver and to the spleen when there is retained windiness, and these poultices are administered empty so that they suck only.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes plain water, as in diseases of the eyes, and in such a way one fills the poultice with hot water only, or with water in which herbs suitable for this have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the poultice administered to fire is this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it should be two fingers and a half palm long, and have on the edge around the middle one small pit, like to lodge an awl, and be of clay, soft before so that it does not wound the patient when putting it on the member.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and it should have in the middle a rod of cross-sectioned clay or iron, to put a candle holder on, and great and small ones according to the diseases and age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for children's poultices are different from old people's, and thin ones from fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should thus put this poultice on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	take the candle of wax or linen, and put it in the poultice across the rod that is in the poultice, so that the light is at the bottom of the poultice that it may not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the limb, and it should be on the ulcer that we have said, so that when you want, if there is moisture, and one removes the poultice;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take the linen as before, and repeat it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cupping glass therefore which is administered in a disease of pleurisy, all aquosity, has no horn nor pierce, and is not administered more than once when it is full of aquosity, and is placed on the member so only;
et c’est li forme:	and that is the shape:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Cups are not administered more than once except in members where one cannot put cupping glasses because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar parts;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in bony limbs stripped of flesh, such as the head or neck, and other similar ones;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the user is that when you find cups that are in sweet and clear water without perturbation, then take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put one in sweet water, until they are familiar, and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then let it be bled with vein and poultice, then rub the member until it is red, and put on bandages;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are clean and dry, if it is a place where you can put a poultice, then put one there, for this is very good afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the limb slightly and then with water, very well, and then tighten it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the swelling heals too late after the application of bandages, soak a linen cloth in cold water and put it on, until the swelling is reduced.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the swelling is multiple, put on crushed Vitriol or gall, and similar things, until it is reduced.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put a handful of peeled peas on the limb and let them stick to it until they are dry, which will stop it now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more supplies, take other bandages.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and if the bandages don't want to take, wipe the fresh blood on the wound, or stick an awl in until the blood flows out, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will adhere.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are falling off, powder on a small amount of alum and salt or ashes, so they will stick now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is for restoring fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that foolish men will despise this chapter, for they have never seen anything like it in the ancient books nor read a letter about it.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and because of this reason is strange the science in our land, for I never found any good;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing, except by the science of ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the habit of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, and I have described to you what is contained in this chapter
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say the prologue to this book, the summaries of the words and the chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who have been proved may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a break or dislocation or twisting or crushing comes to anyone, then it is necessary to hasten to heal the sick person from one side and the other, unless something prevents you, such as weakness of the body, or children, or old people.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the weather is not very cold, or too hot;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and to abate cold cholers, that is to say, cold joints, and hare's flesh and deer's flesh, and not drink wine, nor eat fat meats, and not fill oneself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt of hot aposteme, or spreading of matter in the member;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	so that the patient may recover under their previous government, as they had used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one nourishes the patient with flesh that makes good nourishment, or if they have viscosity, as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and testicles, and peas, and pork belly, and sheep's fat, and fresh fish, and big wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For good nourishment quickly heals the wound and the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well set or united according to their nature because of the wasting away of the members, nor those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but there is no care, reset on the broken bone with large clamps that bind and join the member together, until it becomes strong again as before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not leave him from his work, and for that reason he must be nourished with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is one thing, and the fracture of the breast or leg is another, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that occur in a rounded shape, and others in a curved one, like the cut of a quill to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if with wound, and fracture into a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each person should have their own instrument and proper tool in the restoration, according to what the memory comes into its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and the breaking of the bone is known by what the joint is twisted, and it opens well through a gap, and sounds under the pressure of the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twistiness nor creaking, and the patient does not feel great pain, since there is no break;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have twistiness, or a split, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So do not move it by hand, but put on medicines that come later, and then restrain it now subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the breakage that goes in an arm, and are the two parts separated, it is necessary to put them together evenly, so that abscesses do not come to life.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if abscesses arise, he should leave it alone for a day, until the abscess is pacified;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then put it back together evenly as you can lightly and skillfully, and know that the restoration of this is lighter than the restorations of one who has pieces.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then bind it, as is necessary afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, and they stretch from two parts, whether it be hand or foot, or at your hand it is small members, or to two strings, or to one string and to your hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the member according to its natural figure, so that when the broken parts of the member are separated, you will join them by all means with their places as best you can, and take care that through your work the patient does not come to harm or pain.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and set the two bones of the skull according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And he feels well with his hand if it seems to him that it is not well.
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	so that it is set straight and not strained too much, nor pressed as those who bring them about by their abscessed work heat and contraction to the member, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is fixed, then punish the patient well so that he does not move it, whether waking or sleeping, nor turning or in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and take care that the member is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, then it is not yet fixed, and it must be put in such a condition that he feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and take care that it is set straightly, lest twistedness comes to pass when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member is as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and greatness and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small members, such as wrists and thumbs and similar things:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	so it is necessary to wrap soft and subtle linen drapes.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are large, such as thighs and legs:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: so it is necessary to wrap with a wide and strong bandage, for the broad bandages encircle the whole great member and restrain it evenly from all sides, so that there is no crease.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then bind around with light bandages, three turns or four according to the member, and strain your hand a little on all the bandage, then go up above the break and bind it less, so that the break will soon move away from the break.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the bandage a little and a little, until you take hold of a great part of the healthy skin, then take another bandage and wrap it around again above the broken member.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then return to the part below the break, and strain it moderately, not too strongly nor too gently, as we have said in the first chapter above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place between the stitches strips of linen or cloths, until it is entirely even, then tie all above with bandages, and then put well-made bands on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if it has swelling or abscess, then put something soothing and hot on top that removes the swelling, and let it be like that for a few days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then strain on top of the bands, and be made of a quarter of a well-waxed cane, or of fir wood from which one makes nails, or of palm sapwood, and be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that the band that you put on top of the break is a bit bigger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and let it be as long as is necessary for the member of small or great size;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then steady it above the stars just as you did at the first joint, then place a thread smoothly above the scar;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	the tighter it is above, the looser below;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it is necessary that the thread be middle-sized, not too thick nor too thin, and made of fine linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is thick, as I have seen in the works of those who make their joints from twisted linen threads, and it's a great error, for the joint cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it is not necessary that there be less than a span between each star.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the edges of the splints after the straining in their healthy skin, then put underneath them linen cloths or chopped wool, so that he does not get injured.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the breakage and the ligaments are torn, I will say the treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to bind with splints all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the member is large, it is not necessary to place stars more than after IV or VII days, or more according to your security and depending on the heat of the abscess.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and here is the way of ancient poultices to restore breakage, dislocation, and twisting:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and it is that you take flour that is left over from the mill walls, and mix it with plenty of egg, and put this concoction, neither too clear nor too thick, to use, and this is the common manner of the poultice restoring breakage in various ways, and likewise for women and little children, for it is not too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another manner of poultice restoring breakage, dislocation, and twisting:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	take aloes and ladanum and balsamum and asafoetida and gum arabic and myrrh, in the proportion of one to ten.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	myrrh and aloes, in the proportion of one to five;
alechil VIIII З.;	aloe eight times;
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make powder, and mix with egg white;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	if the complexion of the man is hot, then use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly restore broken bones, and is worth to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another manner of plaster that is good for twisting:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	take mugwort and balm of meadow;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	mirror and aloe, to the amount of nine [parts];
acaice VI З.;	acacia, to the amount of six [parts];
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	bolic Armenian, to the amount of ten [parts], and grind it well, and mix with water or egg white, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another manner of plaster for joints and bones that are separated from their places, and soothes the pain that occurs, and they use it to shape the bone, and to break the brisement:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take a new linen, and boil it in ash and oil, and put it on the place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore at all, but they are good for soothing hot abscesses and properly removing pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another way to plaster that restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dried leaves of fig tree and earth leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to plaster for the restoration of bone breakage and to ease the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take the root of wormwood, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of wheat, of each a part;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limbs are heated, mix it with moist water of coriander or water, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to plaster, stronger than the first one, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take the root of wormwood, and seed of flax, balm, melilot, and henbane, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of each a part;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and grind, and mix with saltwater or sweet water or with wine, according to the warmth of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates writes in his book that one should not put on the broken limb to restore it anything more than a wax and oil mixture, and nothing else, and says that it should be between two, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one should put on the broken limb, to restore, things slightly hot and dry, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another way to plaster that is worth for wound and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take mugaith and sheep's wool, or owl feathers, and vermilion, and equal parts, and grind them, and make a plaster out of it and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then loosen it a little afterwards, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved out of its place;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if you do not loosen it for several days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, with no rest or swelling, then hasten, and loosen it, and remove the plaster now;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take lighter cloth, and moist sea sponge, and dip it in water, and lift the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is appeased;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, moistened in water or rose oil, and bind with a nutmeg, until you are sure of no heat apostema.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and let the inflammation of the member cease, and may the pain be removed, then resume the subtle binding, and add a little poultice, and do not bind it as tightly as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and bind it subtly until he is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that apostema has ceased to be hot and red, and pain and swelling are gone entirely, and you need poultice and bandaging, then begin again, as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if nothing of what we have said comes to the member, then do not remove it until after 3 days or 4 or 5.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and at no time leave it for 20 days, according to what we see, until the swelling subsides and approaches the skin's surface.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then bind it more tightly than before, and increase his flesh, as I said beforehand.
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the place drying out more than is necessary, know that no nourishment can come;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	then arise hot water and temperate it, every time you loosen it, and adjust the temperature a little bit each hour;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	through this work therefore cut off the nourishment from the member, and immediately amend what foolish physicians do, who leave the member in a twisted state;
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	it's bad, and if it's painful work, and I don't see anything else except to ease the pain and work correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways of breakages, and diverse shapes, and the causes are assigned;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	for there are breakages that are made by the percussion of a sword, and the collarbone takes away all the bone up to the notch which is below the bone, as happens in a hatchet or a fist;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and therefore this manner of breaking is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Where the sword cuts through bone above its surface without piercing, and this manner of breaking is called "absolute".
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and it is the wound from these two breakings great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded percussion, or splitting or collarbone of stone, or falling on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a persistent breaking, which approaches just to the skin that is below the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound that is opened in the bone is as fine as a hair, and it is a small crack, and therefore this breaking is called "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound that is made by piercing with a stone, or by falling, or by something similar, and makes the bone fragment enter downward, and it is so loose as when blacksmiths strike sparks on the forges.
si entre li piere dedens.	so the stone goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often to those who have moist skulls, as is the skull of an infant.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and happens to all these types of breakage where small pieces are torn away as they are.
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak to him in his place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of breakings by the detachment above them, and the inquiry is made through probing, and by the corrupted flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary likeness is known because when one has uncovered the bone and rubs it gently above, then opens up the black break.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, take care to note the accidents of the patient, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, extension, numbness, fever, and the eyes issuing forth and turning red, and other similar things in many dispositions, then it cannot be healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no unbearable accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to take out the bone before the 14th day of the moon, as soon as you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to take out the bone before the seventh day, as soon as the skin below the bone is corrupted, and the accidents that we have said come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the breaking of the bone comes just to the skin that covers the brain, then it is necessary that you cut the broken part thus:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and then you take the patient's head and uncover it above the bone in all ways that you can, and above the wound as soft as you can, and if bleeding comes to reveal the bone or abscess, provide the aid that is necessary, and then you fill the place with moistened cloths soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and make the wound rest until the abscess is appeased, and be sure of the cessation of bleeding.
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin to remove around the bone, and it is done according to two methods of work:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	One manner is that you compress at the narrow part beforehand, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then put another cutting even larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second manner is that you have various sizes of compressions, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and they are made of iron indeed;
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and work lightly so as not to bruise the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and tough, it's necessary that you pierce around it, so that you administer compressions with tapers, not too deep lest they penetrate beyond the bone of the skull, and there should be above the tip a margin or circle, so that the point does not pass beyond the bone.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and it's necessary that you have many, so that each one becomes its own place in the shape of the bone, so that you have tapers for all tests.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and this is the form of three kinds of boils:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you put a boil on the bone, and turn to your two [sides] until you know that the bone is pierced.
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	Then put the boil somewhere else, a little bit away, and do this all around, then cut into the bone space between the protuberances, and do it more subtly than you can, and lightly, just as we said, until you bring the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have, such as pincers.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and be careful not to touch the brain or the sacrum.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, it is necessary that you take up the force that remains in the bone to any other instrument similar to an incisor, but it must be more keen and more subtle than the other incisor.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	And if there remains no small bones or scales, then remove them gently with the instruments.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	Then treat the wound with tents and ointments that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And another way of working is as the Gauls say, which is more wholesome;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and the load is very strong, and that's his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the break appears to move, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place beneath the head of this lenticular incisor, whose shape is:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut from one side only, and have the parts torn in two directions, so that the cutting is towards the bone.
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	Then strike with a small hammer above, so that you lightly chop all around the bone, and take good care of the skin that is below.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is attached to the bone, then remove it lightly, for one removes it without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not reach to the layer, and the bone is cut only above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to reassemble that roughness, and remove the scales with a subtle scraper which you should have various quantities of, in order to administer in each place the most suitable thing, according to the work and figure of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	So scrape with great rasps, and afterwards with more subtle ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other hair-cutting and subtle breaking, it is necessary that you bring about a cause in accordance with its direction.
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and this is something that is not answered to him who has put his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the sores are uncovered, then you should take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and put it on the wound.
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another cloth doubled in two or three layers, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and put it on the first cloth.
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and make it as lightweight as you can, so that you do not burden the sore, then administer above the other linen, and do not strain it too much except until it holds the wound alone.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and let it be thus for one or two days, until the abscess is appeased, then remove it, and administer medicine as with roots of linden, and wheat flour, and incense powder, and aristology, and similar things.
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and make powder of these things, and put it on the wound, and administer medicines from time to time without biting.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and take care that the wound is clean from time to time, so you do not leave the ointment off or allow bowels to gather on the linen of the brain, for when bowels assemble above the cerebral cloth, they will run and burst forth, causing great harm to the patient.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when you put a biting thing on the wound, it festers above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care therefore, if any evil accident befalls the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if no swelling comes from it except because of the medicine you have put on, which has that virtue, then you should take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and mix one cloth with it, and put it on the wound.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then perform the cure by methods that are necessary until he is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that sometimes are broken the two parts of the nail above, or one alone by itself, because they are two bones.
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and that one below is cartilaginous and does not break, unless it is forced or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should insert your small awl or perforator into the nail and place this break even with the tip of the index finger and at the edge by pushing forward, until the nail regains its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, and beware that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the neck, and the finger cannot return to its place, then it is necessary that you put it equal to the head of a small rod.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, then do it again, and hasten to restore the first part the next day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess is appeased, then insert a piece of linen into the tip of the nail, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Where you push one apart from the other, if there is a break inside.
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and be so large that they fill the pores of the nails.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some physicians say one must grease the tents with butter, and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary that they be moistened with the making of a mixture of chicken broth and mill powder;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then leave the tent, as long as the bone is firm and the ligaments are hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And sometimes put in or near the nail pens of goose, instead of tents, and if there is a soft draping around, and holds the breakage, and blows the patient around.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	or make what you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the neck while you are working on it, then put cerate or moistened cotton in rose oil, or in a small amount of diachylon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if the abscess does not come forth, then apply a poultice by deferral, made from barley flour and incense powder, mixed with chicken broth, and then place it on light cauterizations, and do not bind the nail.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	et if the breaking of the egg is small and it is broken into little pieces so lead them to suitable instruments for that then sew up the opening and take care of things by cauterizing and binding as with suitable poultices and ointments for that
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no wound inside the egg so treat it with tents and put in plugs of cloth until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	This appears to be a title or heading, rather than a translation. It would likely translate to "On the Fracture of the Jawbone" or something similar.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured below and there is no wound outwardly, and the break is only outwardly so far as to be felt by the tongue inwardly, one can hardly recognize it.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the breaking is on the right side, that you put your two index fingers in the mouth of the patient.
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the breaking is on the left jawbone, put your two index fingers of the right hand and put the breaking inside gently and secure it with the other hand by pushing forward and make even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the breakage of the jaw is dislocated in .ij., it is necessary that you administer an extension of .ij. parts, until it be equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if the movement of the teeth causes displacement or routing, then restrain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put on top of the broken jawbone a poultice and put on top a doubled cloth.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	and place on his shoulder a great strap well made, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the jawbone, and tie it on at the muscle that you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and serve light victuals.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the swelling changes, then loosen it on the third day, and then replace with what has changed.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and apply poultice on it, with powder of the mill mixed with a plenty of egg white or semolina flour, after you have removed the cerote.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and put on a light linen poultice, and if the poultice dries out, and the patient's condition does not change, let it be until he is healed.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	many times are healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes forth, then administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a break and wound together, remove no part of the bone that has been taken out;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	if subtlety of osteum comes with suitable instruments to this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it by fire according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there remains none, then cover the wound, if it is large, and put on .i. suitable plasters to promote flesh, until he be healed.
de la forcele	of strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The shoulder is broken many times beforehand, towards the shoulder, and the breakage is in three manners:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	or it is broken and separated into two, with pieces, and it is the easiest to restore.
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	where there is breakage with wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work is when the breakage has no wound, that you have two ministers, so that one holds the assistant which feels the broken shoulder.
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other stretches the neck towards the part.
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then set the breakage evenly to your knees, so that the form is as it should be, and there is no appearance or defect.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to stretch further, then put under the shoulder of the patient a rounded ball of cloth or wool, and it should be as thick as your necessity requires.
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and lift the forceps, and hold the spear to your hand, so that you put equal the break, as it is right.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder away from the back, because it comes out too far, then it is necessary that the patient lie sovain on his habitation, and put under the shoulder .i. middle pillow, and have the ministers press down on the shoulder, until the bone of the shoulder be lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then address the break to your knees, and if you find fragments there, so it is necessary that you cut on.
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and pull out the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot join by any adjustment, then cut it at one of the chisels you have.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but put under the forceps this instrument, to hold down the splinter.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and make it like a spoon, and is not cut off, and be as wide as it should be, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work.
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and have two heads, as you see, and be one wide, and the other long, such as is the shape of the wound that you made when you pulled out the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are assured of a hot abscess, if it is to be cut open, and the suppuration is small, or you doubt the abscess, if you use bandages and tents according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess comes forth, then soak one cloth in rose oil and lard and wine, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The treatment of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cutting, is that you put powder from the mill and equal egg yolk on the bone, and put light poultices above, and place a stake under the splint, if you need one.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	then take a very wide band of palm width, then put the doubled cloth on top of the poultices and the emplaster.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	then take a thin strip of three fingerbreadths in width and length, and wrap it around that band, so that the head of the band are hanging down.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and place the steel on the bruise, and turn the bandage on the good shoulder, and below the healthy armpit, and below the sick armpit;
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and reset each part, and when you see that the ligament holds the bruise well, and you clearly see that the steel does not move above the broken bone, then reward it each day, and when the ligaments slacken, then restrain it;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the patient lie on his back, and place a small pillow under the armpit, so as to lift the shoulder up high;
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	so that the bruise of the shoulder blade will be alleviated by the alignment of the shoulder, or you bind his arm to his neck, and do not release it unless bad accidents come, until twenty days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then start the poultice again, if you see that he needs it, and strain it and leave it so, until he is restored;
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and she is restored to the greatest extent in 28 days, and less at some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder break
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It often happens that the shoulder breaks or becomes loose, and one cannot feel it except by touching;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	if the appliance conforms to the shape of the breakage, and you reset it according to its natural form, in all the ways that you can;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then put powder of mill on the place with a great deal of egg-white, and gentle poultices, and cover it with a double cloth;
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	then put on a wide and subtle bandage, a little bit wider than the shoulder, and underneath the bandage are strips in some place of the shoulder, so tie that hair with linen bandages, so that the bandage is even;
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	and then bind it all with a great tight bandage, so that the bandage does not move from its place, and look at the tie each day;
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and every time he stretches, if it is strained, and sets the thread equal if it is far from its place, and lies the patient on his side.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder has been reset in 20 days or 25.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number is complete, if he loosens, and be sure, for it is not the bone that becomes lighter quickly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone projects forward and points downward below the knee, then do so above and below it, making the bone that we have said in the breaking of the forceps to soothe an abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	Of the breaking of the ribs.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The weight is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it breaks often at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in mid-air, so it falls below, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks strength, and all, and by chance vomits blood, and opens up the veins in the broken bone, and it seems to be well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back, and he puts one cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and brings together the ribs of both sides with your hands, and takes great care to set it equal in all ways you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be.
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then put on plasters and poultices above the fine salt estuary or other light wood, and envelop it in a cloth, and tie it to the broken bone so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and turn the tie back around to the back, and strain it gently, and reward each hour with an oil, and if it relapses, then restrain it;
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it is necessary to remove, due to corrosion or pruritus that comes from the place, or pain or abscess, then hasten and remove it, and scrape off the plaster, and treat what has come out with methods of cure;
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then reset the plaster, and restrain it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of the breaking of the ribs.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the breakage of the ribs does not occur except in large places after the back and within the head, and do not bend except because they are slippery;
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and he feels well in the inquiry as one must.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you set equal the break, as it is necessary.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply plaster, and bind with a strap, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the break in the ribs is declining inwardly, then the patient feels very great pain and piercing, as with a palsy, for the bone pierces the flesh.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and it leads to punctures, and all and vomits great pouring of blood, and this is from grievous health, and the old men have put great artifice.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that one should administer foods that fill the belly to push the break backward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do so, lest hot abscesses come there, if it has not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then let it heal.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And some of them say that you should apply poultices on the place to suck strongly, and this seems reasonable;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	however, there is doubt whether the poultice will attract the superfluities to the place due to the weakness of condition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of us say that one should cover the site with wet wool in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to put equal pressure on it, then be careful with the treatment of pleurisy, of meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear by the bone which pierces the flesh, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut above the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put an instrument underneath to guard the cavity.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then one must cut the bone, and draw it out lightly, and then sew the two lips of the wound together if it is large, and treat with poultices until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if an abscess comes forth, one puts moist cloths soaked in rose oil on it and applies them to the area.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and cures the part where the abscess is located until it is healed, and makes sure to apply poultices on the outer surface where it needs to be, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	Of the breaking of the neck.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes a crack occurs in the bone of the neck, and then it swells.
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also on the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, then take note if you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and they cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.
