Know that he is mortal in many conditions, and if they are numb and feel well when they are strained and pricked, know that the joints of the bone are saved, and that the patient is healed, if one applies care.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if a similar thing happens on the spine of the back, and you see that he is not healed or not, then take care to see if his feet are softened, and if there is an accident in his hands, and on his back there is windiness and evacuation without his consent.
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when one has sewn it onto his belly, there is sudden ejection without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is oppressed on his back and wishes to rest, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that it is deadly:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	if he does not toil much in his treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these accidents do not come to him, then the thing is easier.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the treatment is that you apply heat if there is a warm abscess, and smear oil of rose or oil of hen's egg on it until it is pacified.
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then put on one of the soothing and drying poultices, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest.
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone is exposed, it is necessary to cover it with a kerchief;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and extract the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a seam, then treat with ointment applying flesh, until he is healed.
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the bone of the head is broken, which is called the "kowe", then put your pouch in your left hand and place it equal to the other hand at your power, then apply the poultice and steel on top if you need.
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then strain it, and if there is devoured bone, do so above, and extract the bone, and heal the wound until it is sound.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the breaking of the hipbone.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	Sometimes the bone of the loin is broken, and if it is, then there follows a slight diminution to the head;
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and make it two long, and decline at the parting, and come to the patient's pain in place, and pierce, and swell that which breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is that you stretch your hand up, as far as you are above the breakage;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and knows what kind of breakage and shape it is;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the breakage is only in the head, then set that breakage straight away, until it has its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is of great length or it declines inwardly, then cause the patient to lie on his belly until the restoration of that break is accomplished.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have set it straight, then apply a poultice, and then apply a linen or leather bandage, and hold the breakage in place so that it does not move.
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and bind the limb beneath the ribs, until the joints are equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if abscesses arise there, do not touch them, until the abscesses are appeased, and then apply what we have said before.
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then come back to restoration, and hold it as is necessary, if there is no bad accident.
et c’est li maniere.	and that is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the break of the shoulder.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The aid is what is between the shoulder blade and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then one must restore it according to one of the two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	Take one fist full of my own growing moss, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And take two threads, and weave them up high, and bind the patient on the throne;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then throw the broken arm on the fist, so that it comes to rest, and have in my hand one bundle of cloth, then weave up onto some heavy thing or have the servants spread it down below;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	then put the mirror on the splint equal to his hands together, so that the splint returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is that one supports the patient on his hatrail, and ties the hand to his neck, then instruct two attendants to have one hold what is above the break with their hands, and the other to hold below each string, and stretch each one to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is stronger, hold the linen under the bandage, and above the bandage, and extend each of the servants to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the splint is near the top of the shoulder, then it is necessary that you put one thread below the throne, and the other towards the side, below the splint;
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	and also if the splint is towards the side, then it is necessary to put one thread lightly, without effort, so that the splint is even on the place and on the side;
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then set the break even as it is necessary, and hold it, if abscesses do not come forth.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if abscesses do come forth, then do not hold it tight for seven days, and apply a moist compress on linen in a sitting and in rose oil, until the abscess is appeased.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	Then hold it, and the manner of holding is that you put an emplaster on the break, then bring the arm onto the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the breast.
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and wrap it in cloth, and hold onto the shoulder, and onto the arm, so that the arm is in its natural state, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not broken.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone is not broken, then use splints, and put on the break a larger and stronger splint than the others, with two inches of space between each splint, and have each splint so large that it passes across the break three inches from each side.
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	Then strain on the stars, as I have said at the beginning of this chapter on binding, stronger and less straying.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the setting of the stars and the constriction, as we have said, in the time that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the apostema is hot, then let it be until the seventh day, as we have said.
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	Then look every three days at the swelling, lest it not increase or come to a head, or the numbness cannot reach the member because it is too narrow.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it addresses, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accidents occur, then do not release it until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back, and have their hands on their stomach.
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and put under the aid a clean linen cloth of equal thickness, and look every hour of the day or night that the shape of the broken member does not change or become loosened.
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	If he is directed by the virtue of medicine, and gives him food that we have put before him, in such a manner that the food is to the first subtle.
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when it begins to take hold, let it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is common that the aid and leg should be reset in forty days from start to finish;
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then one must untie it and administer bath and ointment medicines to direct the limb.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is ugly and swollen, so it should be unbound after 7 days or 2 months.
de la brisure du bras	of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "humerus", one of which is small, and it is that which supports the socket.
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is great, and it is that which lies below, towards the little toe.
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	by chance the great humerus breaks alone, or the small one, and by chance both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small bones are broken, restoration is light, and healing.
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	And when the great ones are broken, then healing is bad, and more grievous than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only a small bone that is broken, then one must stretch and extend it slightly, and set it equal.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is a great bone, one should exert oneself stronger;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and stretch it above the cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the little ones lower than the others, and let the patient be crossed over himself, and the cushion in front of him higher, that the patient suffers no toil.
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	Then stretch out the ministers' arms on either side of his hand, or at the joint, and another minister above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then set the mirror equal, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the break has pieces, then put each one in its place, and if there is any that is loose and can be taken by the horn, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make a splint and an osteum, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with the wound there is a blow, I have spoken about it in the singular chapter;
si pren la cure.	Take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if in the beginning of the treatment apostems appear, so take a mixture made of rose oil and white wax, not too hard nor too soft.
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and apply the mixture gently above, until the apostems are calmed down.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then remove the cerote, and put on the ointment of flour with a lot of egg, then place the poultices, and let the poultice of the breakage be a bit stronger and slightly larger than the others.
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and know that it should have six poultices or arms in various positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	whether the breakage is in one bone or two.
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and hold it more above the breakage than elsewhere, and always less as you move away from there, as I said at the beginning of this chapter.
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and let the cloths be soft and moist on the burn wound, and not hard or dry.
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and let the son (thread) be of flax, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the ligament after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if any evil accident happens to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, then it is necessary that you bathe the member with hot water, until those itchings are appeased.
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the member not rest too tightly.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then continue the stretching, and if the ligament is weakened and the bone loosened, and similar things, so address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling cannot come to the member because it is too tight, then it is necessary that you loosen it a little bit, and let it be like that for some days, until the swelling comes, and then restrain it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, then do not release him until 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	or around him, then put his hands to his neck, and let his collars be even, and beware of movement and disturbance, and sleep on his back;
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and know that this burn is restored in thirty days or in thirty-five, and by chance in twenty days, according to the mixtures and combinations of virtues.
de la brisure de la main	None! It seems you provided only a title "de la brisure de la main" (of the bruise of the hand), without any text to translate. Would you like me to wait for the actual text to continue translating?
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and in the fingers it often happens that there are bruises, and only pleasure comes many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the plant of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary that the patient sit cross-legged and sit straight in front of him evenly.
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	Then place his hand on the stretched cloth and stretch out the broken bones, and make them even with the mirrors, until they are well joined.
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and apply the plaster and poultices, if there is no abscess, then apply an oil according to the quantity of the wound.
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the break is around the parting of the plant, make a sphere of cloth and instruct the patient to wrap it around his broken hand.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then wrap it in a long cloth, and apply the oil of good quality as much as the hand of the patient, and wrap it, just as is fitting.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the bruise is at the back, then it is necessary that you put an elevation above and another below on the plantar surface, so that the hand be open and straight; then bind it all around the hand, and stop the ligament between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if a fracture comes to any of us on the thigh, so it's the pouches, then set it even, as it should be;
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and hold with the sole, and if you see that one sets a straight little splint to lift the fracture, and does not move;
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the fracture is on another thigh, such as in the index or one of the others, then set it even, and bind with the sound thigh that is after;
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	or tie them all together in one holding, as much as it is worth, or set on a splint, such as the pouch;
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and take heed in the restoration and disposition of hot abscess, and heal those who come to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	None! It seems you provided only a title "de la cuixe brisie" (of the bruised toe), without any text to translate. Would you like me to wait for the actual text to continue translating?
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bone of the hip is often broken, and well one sees when it turns before and behind;
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and the restoration is such that one ties above the bridge and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies on his face, then each minister stretches their band to its equal part.
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and that's when the break is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the hip, so that one of the ligaments points towards the finger, and the other ligaments are below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And also if it is near the knee, and then have the band below the knee, and have the stretching downward.
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	Then put the mirrors on the bone to its two hands, so that it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster, and the band, lest abscesses do not come there.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is a hot abscess, then let it cool down and then return to your work and treatment.
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The splint is made in this same manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	You should wrap above the bridge with double-layered bandages in two or three layers, and remove any superfluity, then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the knee, and tie a long thread between the crotch and the leg, below the knee downward, and let the end of the thread come up.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	then turn back on the leg and on the groin the bandage, then put on the breastplate stars, and put one star on the bone of the leg;
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	then place the lead between the leg and the groin of soft cloth to put equal tension, then start to bind strongly three times or four on the breastplate;
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and when you go further up on the breastplate, and loosen the tension less;
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	then take the two knots of thread that you have put between the leg and the groin, and bind three stars that are above, then go back down to the lower part of the thread, until you come to the foot;
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, and if there is no abscess or swelling or similar thing;
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it happens, then disconnect it, and address what comes next, as we have said many times;
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are fragments of bone that prick, it should be smoothed over, if possible;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if one cannot, then it is necessary to split the way, and pull forth;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And sometimes the bone is broken in such a way that one must put splints in, as in an emergency and on the arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	nevertheless, in this restoration made, the patient does not recover.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the toe is restored in 1 day, or a little less or more, according to the various complexities.
de la ruelle dou genoil	None! It seems you provided only a title "de la ruelle dou genoil" (of the ankle of the knee), without any text to translate. Would you like me to wait for the actual text to continue translating?
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the ligament of the knee there is a small break, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, then it is only a crack or a hole, and it occurs in every wound, and without a wound, and this seems quite good.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is such that one sets equal what is torn to its place, so that it can be put together and moved as possible;
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	then apply the plaster, and put a rounded splint in it, if necessary, and restrain it as is fitting, then reward all the preparations that we have said for other breakings, such as boils and similar things;
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he puts on each accident what is necessary to him, until he is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the breaking of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Know that in the leg there are two bones, because of which one is called "tibias" and the other is called "fibula".
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	and it happens in just the same way as it does with an arm break, and therefore the restoration is done equally for both leg and arm, and all work is finished. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns from all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the slender bone is broken, then it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the big bone is broken, one feels great pain and sees it well;
et torne desoz.	and turns underneath.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then administer extension, and set it straight, and bind the splints evenly;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	but nevertheless, it is necessary if the break is ugly and there are many pieces that the extension be less and more gentle;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and be according to your virtue
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed your work, take two strips of wood that surround the leg on both sides, and be as long as the leg from the knee to below.
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	Then wrap the two strips around the leg above and below, and bind them together in the middle, so that the leg cannot turn to the right or left, and thus it is well.
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and some attend the splints as long as the leg, and it is of wood, and place the leg in order to prevent movement, and properly do so at the break or where there is a wound;
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess or some other accident;
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if it cures as long as it remains sound.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the breaking of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	The ankle does not come to breaking, but the bones of the foot sometimes break and there are two or three positions; and there is no remedy except in more or less conditions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if there is a break in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlapping one another, so place the patient's foot on the earth, just as if it were flying, and then put your own foot now where the bones are lifted, then press down until they return to their places.
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	Then place the poultice and poultices above, and put a small table under the foot of the bed with two full pillows, then bind the foot accordingly, then that you have wrapped it with bandages around and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, then loosen the tie, for you will find the bones equal, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if any of the toes are broken, restore them, just as we have said about the fingers of the hand;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	Then place the splint on the broken toe according to its length, and make it slightly wider, then put that table under the foot as I said, and bind it accordingly;
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	et if there are two or three, or more, break them, and place on each one a splint according to its size, enveloped in one drapery of linen, and hold the table under the foot.
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and let it be placed on top of the head of the table so that it is held well by the stomach of the foot.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things I have said about other breakages, since we have discussed them;
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and treat each accident as it requires.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the breaking of the bones of the thumb
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bone of natural childbirth is broken, make the woman sit upright, then incline her to the part of the back, and hold her by the rear.
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then fill the woman's natural opening with cotton, and put in as many pieces as there are stitches.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then put the woman upright, and lift her back little by little, and then let the cotton jump out until it reaches the natural entrance, and return the bone to its place with the stitches.
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	and when it wants to urinate, so remove the cotton, and when it has urinated, put it back, and thus do for seven days or thereabouts:
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	so the break will be restored, and if you see, take a sheep's bladder and tie it to the penis with a string, and fill the whole bladder in its natural way;
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	then blow into the string strongly, until the bladder is emptied inside:
la nature si revenra li brisure;	nature will return to the break;
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then fill it with cotton, and let it be like that for some days, until he is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone of the hand or of the woman is broken, so restore it as we have said in the shin bone;
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and these breaks are not hidden from one who sets their study and use to them, and pays attention to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the break signifies the right way to restoration in more than one disposition.
enten le donques.	Then understand it.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	In the bowstring, when it is broken, take a goose quill and insert it into the bowstring;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	Then wrap it in cloth around, and leave it for three days or as much as possible, and it will be healed promptly.
de brisure avec plaie	of breaking with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a breaking with a wound, whether it be great, such as the bones of the hip or shoulder or similar, to be healed now, so that the wounds which we have said bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then remain it with vinegar, or if you have no other remedy, then start to restore the breakage in that same hour or day, unless abscesses arise.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses arise, then leave the restoration just to the ninth day, until the abscess is pacified, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible above the skin uncovered, it is necessary that you set it in place lightly with your hands, to a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the extension is not prepared to equalize your hands, then remake this instrument of iron, which has seven or eight fingers in length, and its width is according to the quantity of the wound;
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and therefore it is necessary for the surgeon that he take three or four of them, according to what he may need in each treatment of breakage;
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and be rough and slightly large, so that it does not bend at all under the compression on the member during your work, and be hollow in front, and thick from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And it is called "paleinche", for which reason it is necessary that the curved joint be placed on top of the visible bone.
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and bind it once, until it recovers, and let them be equal to each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle, and the instruments cannot well take hold of the bone, then it is necessary that you cut away the top of the bone, until the instruments have power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot bring the bone back, as we have said, then use a suitable instrument, such as a chisel or saw, to your ability.
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then remove what remains in the bone from sharpness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	So do this until it is back in its place, then soak the rag in black vinegar and make sure it is well saturated.
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not put on the wound any ointment or other substance that has oil in it, lest you cause rot and corruption.
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	then administer these remedies when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut away the covering all around, according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not constrained with the breaking.
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and many times has this been done by a foolish surgeon, and he has brought it upon the patient who is dying or being consumed.
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and let the ligaments be softer and more gentle than other breakages.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is foul or large, and you doubt that bad accidents may come to it, as we have said, and you find pain at the site, then it is not necessary to put in candles.
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but wrap around it, instead of candles, hard cloths and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days the bowing of the wound, then remove what you have put on top all wine, and put healing balm on it, as ointment of four drugs and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you loosen the member twice a day, in the morning and at night, until it is set and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the members be aligned in such a way that the bow strings down lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the bone breaks every day, and it cannot heal but keeps returning to its bow-like shape, know that there are small pieces of bone; therefore it is necessary that you gently probe the wound with a tent, and remove all these splintered pieces that cause that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place or another manner of corruption, then it is necessary that you treat it, according to what is written in this chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken and open on the limb, such as the hip or shoulder, and other similar large members, do not pull it, for many times death comes from this, but leave it until it can be reset.
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	by chance it may fall out after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound if you can.
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of the boils that come on the swelling
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	We often come after the wound has healed, especially when it is near the joint; and it is a sad thing to see the shape of the limb.
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and by chance the member cannot perform its natural actions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Take care then if it is fresh to us:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if it is fresh to us then administer medicines such as aloe, incense, and myrrh, and sarsaparilla, aconite, and similar others, either one of these things or all together, and mix them with stiptic wine or with the white of an egg or with oil.
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and put it on the back in hot poultices, and keep it well, and do not remove it for several days;
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then remove it, and begin another one, until the knots are removed;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	You strain on a piece of well-made lead;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	for the property of lead is that it absorbs all swelling above the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the swelling has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, so scrape above, and make the excess appear;
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	or you receive it at any scraper until it is removed, and care until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the member which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the breaking of the bone is restored, and remains after weak and subtle limbs, which happens for many reasons:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	because one is because it was tied too tightly, and was not tied as it should be;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or because there were too many ties, and could not come the nourishment to the member;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	or by excessive inflammation;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or for too great movements, nor indeed at his hour;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because he has little blood in his body, so he is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the treatment is that you make the patient eat and cause the body to be tender, until the blood is multiplied in him;
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and administer bath water, and give him joy and ease;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then put poultice on the member, so that the poultice attracts to the great swelling, and wash it often with lukewarm water, until the swelling comes to the member;
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and return to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the twisted member after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the member is twisted after restoration, and the bone is broken apart, and the form of the member is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function:
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	so do not believe the foolish who say that you should break the member all over again, and many foolish men have done this in our land;
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and this work is blamed, and many evils come, and by chance death.
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	nevertheless, if the swellings and tortures are fresh, it is necessary that they be poulticed with hot water or moist herbs cooked like nettle leaves, and roots, and melilotus, and similar things.
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and the poultice is made with a mollifying plaster, like dyaquilon well made, and you take the juice of nettle, and cook it with goose grease or sesame oil, and make a poultice on top.
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	or you take fig tree fat, and grind it with hen's hair, and similar medicines that reduce the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the swelling is removed by continuous and prolonged rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And there should be movement to each member every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the stiffness is hardened and stubborn like stone, and it is necessary to open with a file, so it must be covered just up to the bone, at the subtle edge of the incisor lightly.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and put caution and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to someone, then it is necessary to bring it back into place immediately.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if one delays, the swelling increases, and by chance, one sets it right with sharp points at the joint;
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	therefore it is not proper to move it until it has deflated.
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	many times brings shame and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	however, when this happens, one should make the patient well again, then leave them until the abscess is calmed down;
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then apply the member with hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each limb as the treatment comes into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of dislocations to an end at this point.
des mandibules	of jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	Often happens that the jawbones are displaced downwards, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	or they are a little pulled out of their place, and softened a little;
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	when they are dislocated entirely and hang towards the belly, and the saliva from the mouth cannot be held, nor can it close its mouth, and wraps its tongue with words.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by several gentle movements.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if she is whole and complete, then you must reset her quickly, and do not delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in such a way that the minister holds the head of the patient, and inserts the mirror's pouch from one of his hands into the root of the jaw dislocation inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts.
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other two hands should be free, in order to set it even.
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and instruct the patient to relax his jawbones and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the mirror adjusts it so that it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if it is stuck, all the more so if they are both jawbones together, then raise them with hot water and oil, until you gently reset them.
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	Do not neglect to bring back, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the patient is well closed with a sense of softening, then place moist cloths on them in a poultice made of rose oil and wax, and bind it lightly with soft threads.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and the patient sleeps on his back, and their joints are between two cushions, so that they do not move either to the right or left, nor do they try to manipulate, but take light food, until the pains are gone, and the jaws are loosened.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then moisten what they want lightly, and do not trouble themselves to open their mouth for eating and drinking, until the jawbone is well relaxed and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be returned to their place within an hour and are not converted back to their natural state, it comes to fever and accustomed sickness, and by chance, belly upset, and by chance, vomiting pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see that, then know it is a calamity;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and many times has he died to whom this has happened, within nine days.
de la forcelle	of the shoulder
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The shoulder cannot dislocate from the side inward along its continuity and of the chest, and is dislocated sometimes backward, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back, and stretches out his arms.
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press the joint firmly into your palm, and it will return.
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then put on the poultice and the bandage, and tighten it;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the part that is near the shoulder cannot dislocate.
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	if not, and if it dislocates at any time, then reset it to its place, as we have said;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	then put on the poultice and bandage, and tighten it, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and thus also the shoulder joint is brought back into place when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder blade
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	The shoulder is dislocated in no more than three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	which one is that from which it dislocates at the lower part of the socket.
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second is at the part of the chest.
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and it dislocates above, and this happens rarely;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, nor does it dislocate inside for the nerves.
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and it dislocates below towards the socket, especially in those who have little flesh, for they leap forth suddenly;
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	to those who have enough flesh, it leaps forth slowly and returns slowly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men that they suffer a blow or fracture, and the shoulder blade swells up with a hot abscess, and thinks that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	It is necessary then that you examine it, until you are certain.
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that a dislocation is when it is below towards the socket, and makes a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them manifest diversity.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	and you will find a hollow at the head of the shoulder, and below it, on the touching the head of the shoulder, just as if it were an eye.
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot bring their hand back to its place or move with any movement at all;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you find it clearly by touching;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this kind of dislocation is not difficult to reduce when it is new or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the way is that the minister lifts the patient's hand upwards, then places their fists below the shoulder, and lifts the joint upwards to its place with force.
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	and the minister lifts the hand and extends it upwards, then puts it under [the patient's arm];
si venra hastanment.	so it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it doesn't come as we have said within eight days, then the patient should be bathed in hot water.
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and the poultice should be applied soothing and calming, like a decoction of althea and fenugreek and melilot in water.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then the patient should be placed on their back, and a layer of wool cloth equal in thickness, neither too soft nor too hard, should be put underneath, then the nurse should place their thumb under the shoulder blade and lift it virtuously, and pull the patient's hand.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and another minister should hold the patient's head so that it does not move downwards.
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	the shoulder comes back immediately, and if you see that you reset it in this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and that you make someone larger than the patient to be present.
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and place the right shoulder directly under the patient's armpit, and lift the armpit upwards so that the patient hangs in it.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and another assistant draws the patient's hand down towards their belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, then he can carry with him something heavy, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And reset it in another way:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and there's a long poker in the earth, whose head is as hot as a pistol, and is not too big nor too small.
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then it should be placed under the patient, but only if he has fallen asleep on top, and the patient is lying along the length of the wood.
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then stretch out his hand downward from the other side, and the joints will return to their place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if it doesn't want to return for all these things that we have said, then do this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	Take I a tallow from two arms of great and four fingers wide, which has the head rounded so that it may fit to enter deeply under the armpit, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	Then place it on top of the wooden beam draped under, so that the wood does not wound the patient, then put it underneath the armpit of the patient;
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	And stretch my arm on top of the long wooden beam, and place the aid on top of the beam, and the arm at the head of the hand, then put the arm on one shoulder of an easel wide, and let the hands hang down below, and leave the body hanging from the other side:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	The joints now relax.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is so, no matter what way it may be, then you should put under the shoulder blade a woolen sphere equal in size, then apply the plaster with powder of the mill, with incense and a little egg yolk, on all the shoulder and around, then hold it under the shoulder blade gently, and turn the lien on the plaster, and wrap the hand around one's neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is necessary that he stays still a little while the limbs are comforted, for he will heal more quickly;
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then stay still for four or seven days, and then move him;
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	and if he is firm and is not softened, it is sound.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come in or for another reason, then you must apply cauterization to three parts, as it is written before this chapter on cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all this and he loosens after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift his arm above, then know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder are cut or stretched or softened.
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and know that the joint will never be set in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation which is towards the breast, and shoulders, or behind, is caused by force, stretching of hands, and another kind of handling.
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat him until he is sound.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes grief and tardiness of movement in the limb, then the patient should bathe many times until that grief is alleviated and returns to its original nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	Know that the joint of the hip is dislocated to points and returns to points;
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and it is dislocated in all parts, and just as much before and behind, and the dislocation is not repaired, because one can see it well and feel it well;
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	and dislocate according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick limb with sound, you can then see clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And it is necessary that you reset it as soon as an abscess forms, for if an abscess forms, it would be a great difficulty to reset it.
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	and by chance it cannot be completely reset from top to bottom, especially when it is at the back.
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	it is worse than other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and by chance many die.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And the restoration is such that when it can be reset as is, you stretch out his hand with your two hands.
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	and his arms are spread out, and the hands of the mirror according to the cut all around, above and below, and bind the jointure to his back together, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, then it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and sets the shoulder that is dislocated back to its root.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not want to return to its place, then administer strong stretching;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and it is that two ministers stretch out the arm, and hold it steady with two ministers, so that it does not move in extension;
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	then turn the arm on each side, then having enveloped a cloth double long and wide;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the surgeon joins the joint to her hand, so anoints it with some oil to soften the joint, then bends the joint firmly until it recovers;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, so applies dry plaster with some egg, and holds it firmly, and places the arm on the neck of the patient, and leaves it for some days, then releases it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the joint is firm in its place, so releases the bandage and lets it be;
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	and if you see that the joint does not hold well, so repeat the plaster and bandage, and let it be thus for some days, until it is firmly set;
puis le deslie.	then loose.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if the patient feels stiffness after repositioning the joint, and it seems to move, then bathe and gently rub well, and press until the pain is alleviated.
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	Or you put a layer of fatty sheep's wool on the joint, then let it stay for a day and a night, then remove it, and cause it to enter into a bath;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	and when he sweats, gently rub the joint, then put the wool back on, and then enter into a bath;
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and thus do it two or three times, until he is healed.
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	and if you see that, put on a moist wheat poultice warmed with butter, and strain it on;
si revenra a sa disposition.	so he will return to his normal condition.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The joint of the hand dislocates, and the recovery is light, more than other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	Toutevoie, it is necessary to bring it back to its place quickly, in the same time that it is dislocated, so that the flesh may be swollen or a warm abscess may come.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the remedy is that you put the sick hand on a table, and stretch out the middle fingers, and place the thumb equal, so that it places its palm on the appearance of the jointure, and push until it regains.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	However, it is necessary to check if it is well in place;
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Then put the sick person's hand on a table for extension and reduction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, then the patient puts their back on their hand on the table, and the physician puts their hand on that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it returns now, it is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	But if not, then apply soothing poultices to warm abscesses, and let it be so that it does not start again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back into place after some days, then the twisted joint remains.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and nothing should harm the patient except as long as his hands are softened, and he cannot grasp anything at all.
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	then know that the nerves are cut or the arteries;
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	if there is no other remedy except to draw out by fire cauterization around the case, and by chance it is not worth anything else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when his hands are back in place, then put on the ointment that we have said, then strain and leave it for five days, then release it and let it be so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is any swelling, then soak it in hot water and rub it until it is clean.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Some times the two bones of the hand are separated on each side, some times in the back of the palm or the belly.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	then straighten the two bones and push the dislocation into your pockets until it recedes, then support the head of the bone and pull it towards the part where it is separated.
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	and leave it for two days, and then put it back in its place that day.
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	and bind it with a nut, as we have said, and loosen the tie of yesterday, and make it move, and rebind it to the nut;
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this often, until it is tight, and do the same thing, if it becomes dislocated in the palm of the hand, and do just as you have done before, until it is healed;
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and do the same thing, when it becomes dislocated on the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the sciatic nerve of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the sciatic nerve of the back or neck is dislocated, or if there are multiple dislocations, then there is no remedy, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.
