And the signs are that the evacuations jump beyond natural sense, nor can they be held, and many times some limb is softened, or both hips or two arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And often the shinbone bends into four parts;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	that which bends at the back is called "gilbositez";
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	the cure is that you reward if the gilbositez has come from childhood:
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	if there is no care or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, say the old methods of cures by great words, where there is no true benefit at all.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have abbreviated it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the swelling that comes to the liver before, there is no understanding or health;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also that which comes directly in both sides, and one can only cure fevers by the proper one that comes to the back, as I say;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is that the patient should be stretched on his face in one position and have a strap underneath him, so he does not get hurt;
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then insert a firebrand into the ground firmly, and another at the feet, and bind a band around the joints of the patient, and another at the hips, and knees, and ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	and two ministers know the bonds, one at the head and the others at the feet, among the two fires;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and be well closed, the fire as we have said, and the mirror puts its palms on the spine firmly, until it recovers.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it doesn't recover with this treatment, then take a three-branched stick of length, and hollow out the appearance below, and the patient should be in position, and push the head of the stick into the appearance, then place the middle of the stick on the spine.
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and put the mirror's feet on the other head of the stick, and press well, until it recovers to its place;
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and if you see, then do it to the twisting one who twists with the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And it is that you put two fires on the head of the patient, one arm's length away, and towards the feet, two others, and have between each fire, a palm-breadth apart.
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	and have a small pit in each coal, where the core runs through, and let the coals be firmly on the ground, so they do not move;
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and between each pair of coals let there be one coal turning, on which the core turns, and have in each turning two small coals a palm's length long, so that the core may turn;
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the cord that is among the assemblers to the core towards the head, and the other cord to another core towards the feet, and each of the attendants turns his core to all the cord, and the master sets the spine equal just as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is equal, then place upon it a drying plaster with an abundance of egg white, and then bind it, and then take the knife of three fingerbreadths in length to open up the joint and the part of the spine so that the bone may heal, then tie it with a cord just as we have said, and use gentle massage on the patient until they are healed.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	and if no thing comes to the end of health, it is necessary to administer soothing and calming medicines, with the steel that we have said before.
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	and sometimes when one administers a splint, and sometimes the appearance comes in the lower back of the spine of the back, and it is thought to be dislocation;
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	and that's the bone which opens, so one should not have presumption there;
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	in case it would bring about death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of the dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder only come forth with dislocations alone, nor does it come so with other joints;
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	and the joint of the hip is dislocated into four parts:
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	inside and outside, and in front and behind;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	and even more inside, and a little dislocated in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of his dislocation is that when one joins the sick leg with a healthy one, it is longer, and the sick person's knee protrudes more than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot double their knee at the fire;
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and it is the swelling that is below an abscess, hot, because the inflammation of the crotch comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	The sign of him to whom it comes to an end is that these accidents are contrary to those beforehand.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the signs of him who has it in front, is that his leg is well-shaped according to its fulfillment;
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	nevertheless, do not bend the knee without pain, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot beforehand, and retains his urine, and swells the inguinal area, and when he walks, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of him to whom it happens behind is that he cannot spread his knee, nor double over, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and there is a swelling on the hip at the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	The remedies for this type of dislocation are that you reward if the dislocation is ancient and it stays according to its condition, if there is no care.
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	and it is not necessary that he has presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in the one where the dislocation is fresh, and it's of four kinds of dislocation, if you hurry to move the joint, and stretch it within and without, and move it to the right and left;
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	by chance it will return, and there is no need for another treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this way, then you must make the minister strong, and stretch the leg strongly with two hands, or with one strap that is tied above the knee.
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	and another minister stretches his hand on top in the same way that he puts his hands under his armpits, then tightens a soft strap above the hip.
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another tightens the head of the strap;
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and they stretch upwards and downwards all at once, until the patient is lifted off the ground at one time, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of stretching is common to the three likenesses, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If so, then it is necessary to apply treatment to its likeness.
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When the dislocation is in the shoulder, then you must take care of the patient on their chest side, then place the ligament on the root of the crotch, and the bone that is below the armpit, then stretch the ligament up towards the armpit and towards the flank.
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	then take other attendants by their arms, and encircle the thick bone of the patient's crotch, and stretch it out strongly.
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	so it will return to its place now;
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	and this manner of dislocation is easier than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot tighten it in this way as we have said, then it is necessary that you bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong soft ligament on both heels and both knees, and let the sick leg be stretched out two doits more than the others.
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	Then let it hang on the top of a pole, and let two long arms stretch out over the ground.
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then instruct the minister to wrap the top of the groin, and let another minister stand with the patient, wrapping the groin tightly, because the joints are returning quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is at the end, let the patient lie down as we have said in those with gilboesite, and stretch the bandage over the afflicted leg properly, and also on the back.
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	Then place two torches, one at the head and another at the back, then insert the torch between the patient's thighs in the shape.
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and let wet cloths be placed around them so the patient does not get hurt, then each minister stretches towards him, and the doctor puts an equal weight in his hand to the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put on the bed, and press it as we have said in the gilbositeit, and place the patient on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	And when the dislocation is before, it is necessary to extend the sick leg quickly, and according to what I said;
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	and place the mirrors so that their weight is on the sick angle, then press with the other hand, and stretch downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	And if the dislocation is in back, it is not necessary to extend the sick leg downwards or lift it up to the earth, rather it should be as if the hip were dislocated in back, as we have said about the posture on both hips;
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and be above its face, and the ligament stretched as we have said before, and one must press on the joint at the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	and it will be adjusted when the patient stretches their legs, and they will be equal.
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	then adjust the hips, and apply an ointment, and tie with a bandage, so that the hip does not move;
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	and then rest for three days or four, and afterwards loosen it, and put the plaster on.
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	and if you see that they are even, then strain it, as before, and let it be for three days.
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	then loosen it, and make him walk gently, until the limbs are comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The jaw is dislocated according to three manners:
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	that is to say, inward and outward, and behind.
et ne desalue point devant.	and do not dislocate in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the sign is that you instruct the patient to bend his leg to his hip, and if it does not bend to his hip, know that he is dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit straight, and stretch his leg if he can, and place your back on his face, and put his foot on your feet.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	Then take his knee to your palms, and bring it between your thighs, then bend the two sides of the knee sharply.
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	and another attendant stretches out his foot, so that the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he has eased his leg slightly at the hip.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	and put plaster on top, and make the leg settle at the hip, and keep it together firmly for three or four days, then loosen.
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and do not trouble the patient to get up, until the limbs are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not straight, then extend it strongly, as we have said in the treatment of gout, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes strained, and sometimes completely dislocated, and inward and outward.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and tense ahead of the part where it is dislocated:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	the return is gentle, and one must stretch it gently with his hands when he is merely stretched.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is dislocated entirely, then you must make the patient sit straight, and one attendant hold him forth except by the leg, above the ankle.
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	Then draw the foot to you with your right hand, and then with your left hand two times, then stretch it up, and put the foot beautifully up.
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	and do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and drawing the foot.
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	if it returns, that's good;
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	if not, then start the work again, for it will return;
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return like this, then make the patient sit on the ground on his back, and place one pillow firmly in the ground between his thighs, and tie cloth around, so that the patient is not harmed;
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then take hold of the thigh by the attendants, and another attendant stretches the foot to their hands or to a cord that they tie around the calf of the foot;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then stretch each attendant equally, and the cord should be placed between the thighs of the patient to retain the patient when one stretches;
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then place the mirrors equal to the dislocation in their hands, and other attendants take hold of the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is fixed, then place the plaster and bandages on top, and form straps, and bind the foot to the leg, and watch out for those nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the ligament is not too tight.
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	Then leave it two days or three, and if the ligament loosens, then loosen the straps;
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	Then release it on the third day or the fourth, and prevent the patient from walking for four days;
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if he goes before that term is reached, it's not a guarantee that it won't dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come to this, then it is necessary that you ease them, as we have said elsewhere, until he is healed.
des dois	knees
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the knees are dislocated, then they should be well stretched without labor, and that is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any part of the heel or foot, then it's necessary that you make the patient sit on a flat surface or on a one-piece table straight, and place your foot on what appears to be these joints, then press firmly with your foot until it returns.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	and when it is equal, and nothing appears, then place a two-legged stool under the heel of the foot, then strain together, and leave it for three days, then release.
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and make him rest until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with the dislocation and one tries to restore it, many times it happens that the patient dies:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not humble in the treatment, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not merciful and compassionate and slow, nor hasty;
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and use soothing things on the abscess first, and leave the patient in God's hand, if you do not see hope of recovery;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, then reset the member to its place, so that the abscess may live and not become worse;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the member is at rest, administer soothing things to the abscess hot, and cure the wound as it needs, with anointed dried substances;
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if there is a break with the dislocation, and small bones disconnected, then set them, and do what we have said in simple diseases;
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	and take care not to enter into a path of fear, according to what I have said, for this is worth moving according to your Creator, and by the knowledge of your armor and body.
